Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
The Meaning of 'Al' and Specification in Praise Contexts
Commentary on the meaning of 'Al' with objections and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how an attribute in a context of praise specifies the described (takhsis) and distinguish between the three interpretations of 'Al' in the phrase 'Wa 'ala al-hi...'.

Core Idea
An attribute in a praise context restricts the general term; 'Al' here can mean all pious supporters of the religion.

In this passage from Khulasat al-Anwar, the commentator addresses the meaning of the word 'آل' (family) in the blessing phrase 'وعلى اله الذين قاموا بنصرة الدين القويم'. He presents three possible interpretations and defends the general one as more appropriate. Along the way, objections are raised regarding the inclusion of the Companions and the need to describe 'الدين' with 'القويم'. This lesson will walk you through the textual analysis and the usul principles involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term under analysis
The word 'آل' occurs in a blessing formula. The commentator lists three possible meanings: 1) the purified wives, 2) the Prophet's offspring, 3) all pious believers. Write down these three interpretations.
The passage says the third is 'عام' (general) and therefore more appropriate.
2
Understand the principle of takhsis in praise
The text begins with a principle: when an attribute is mentioned in a context of praise, it becomes specific to the described (mawsuf). Apply this to the phrase: the attribute 'الذين قاموا بنصرة الدين القويم' (those who stood for the upright religion) specifies who is meant by 'آل'. Who does it specify?
This principle is used to argue that the attribute restricts the general term.
3
Analyze the first objection
An objection is raised: why did the author not explicitly mention the Companions? The response is that the author's Sunni Hanafi creed ensures devotion to the Companions, and the phrase 'آل' in its structure includes them as the foremost individuals. How does this defense preserve the author's intention?
This shows that missing an explicit mention does not imply ill intent.
4
Analyze the second objection
Another objection: describing 'الدين' with 'القويم' is against clarity because 'الدين' already means Islam. The response explains that 'الدين' in its definition includes all previous religions, so the adjective is needed to specify Islam. What does this reveal about the scope of the word 'الدين'?
The adjective restricts the general meaning of 'الدين'.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Summarize how the commentator uses the principle of takhsis to interpret 'آل' and 'الدين'. What does this teach us about Hanafi textual analysis?
The lesson shows that context (praise) and adjectives can specify general terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تخصيص جواب آپ کی بات تسلیم تاہم جب کوئی صفت مقام مدح میں ذکر کی جائے تو وہ موصوف کے ساتھ خاص ہی ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا آیت میں محل مدح میں ہونے کی بناء پرچین آگئی ۔ مثلاً یہ کہا جائے کہ خون شخص شب بیدار ہے مشیرانی التقصیص ہے قس علی هذا ۔

وعلى اله الذين قاموا بنصرة الدين القويم آل سے مراد: اس میں شارح رحمہ اللہ نے تین قول نقل کئے ہیں پہلے دو خاص اور تیسرا عام ہے اسی لئے یہی زیادہ مناسب ہے۔

پہلا قول اہل بیت عظام رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین تفسیر جلالین میں اہل بیت کا مصداق ازواج مطہرات کو قرار دیا ہے۔

دوسرا قول .... اولاد نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم

تسیر اقول ... بر مؤمن جو متقی اور پر ہیز گار ہو۔

نکتے اہل بیت کا مصداق اول تو ازواج مطہرات ہی ہیں رضی اللہ عنہن اجمعین جس طرح قرآن میں ارشاد باری تعالی ہے کہ ( یرید الله ليذهب عنكم الرجس اهل البيت.... الخ ) البتہ محتاط قول یہی ہے کہ اس میں جمیع اولا د عباس رضی اللہ عنہ و عبد المطلب شامل ہیں کیونکہ زکوۃ کی حرمت سب کیلئے ہے اور حرمت زکوۃ والی حدیث میں اہل بیت پر دلالت موجود ہے۔ واللہ تعالی اعلم بالصواب اعتراض ... مصنف کو چاہئے تھا کہ صحابہ کرام رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین کا بھی ذکر کرتے جس طرح مصنفین کا طرز ب وعلى اله واصحابه جواب مصنف نے چونکہ صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم کا مستقل ذکر نہیں کیا اسے کسی بد نیتی اور بد اعتقادی پر محمول نہیں کیا جا سکتا کیونکہ صاحب کتاب صحیح العقیدہ سنی حنفی ہیں اور صحابہ کرام رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے عقیدت ان کے رگ و پے میں شامل ہے زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ (اللہ ) میں مصنف رحمہ اللہ کے پیش نظر تعمیر تھی جس کا فرداعلی و اولی صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم کی جماعت ہے۔

صحابہ ہی کی قربانی سے آج ہم میں اسلام ہے جو صحابہ کا منکر ہے کارندہ شیطان ہے

اعتراض .... (الدین) کی صفت ذکر کر نا خلاف نصاحت ہے کیونکہ دین سے دین اسلام مراد ہے؟

جواب دین کی تعریف میں عموم ہے (اللہ کے وضع کردہ وہ طریقے جو اہل عقل و خرد کو ان کے ختیار کے ساتھ ایسے کاموں کی طرف گامزن کریں جن میں سرتا پا خیر ہی خیر ہو ) یہ تمام ادیان سابقہ کو شامل ہے اس لئے صفت (القویم ) ذکر فرمائی تا کہ دین سے فقط دین اسلام مراد ہو کیونکہ تمام ادیان منسوخ و محرف ہو چکے ہیں قیامت تک محفوظ ومستقیم دین اسلام ہی ہے۔
The specification. Answer: Your statement is accepted; however, when an attribute is mentioned in a context of praise, it is specific to the described. Therefore, in the verse, due to being in a context of praise, objection arises. For example, if it is said that the blood of a person is a night-watchman, it is a specification by mention. Measure upon this.

And upon the family of those who stood in support of the upright religion. By 'Al' is meant: in this, the commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) has transmitted three sayings: the first two are specific and the third is general, therefore this one is more appropriate.

The first saying: The noble Ahl al-Bayt (may Allah be pleased with them all) — in Tafsir al-Jalalayn, the referent of Ahl al-Bayt is taken as the purified wives.

The second saying: ... the offspring of the noble Prophet (peace be upon him).

The third saying: ... every believer who is pious and righteous.

Point: The referent of Ahl al-Bayt is primarily the purified wives (may Allah be pleased with them all), just as in the Qur'an the Almighty said: 'Allah intends to remove impurity from you, O people of the house...' (etc.) However, the cautious saying is that it includes all offspring of Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) and Abdul Mutallib, because the prohibition of Zakat is for all of them, and the hadith about the prohibition of Zakat indicates the family (Ahl al-Bayt). And Allah Almighty knows best what is correct.

Objection: The author should have also mentioned the noble Companions (may Allah be pleased with them all), just as the manner of authors is 'and upon his family and his Companions'.

Answer: The author's not making a separate mention of the noble Companions cannot be attributed to any ill intention or bad belief, because the author is a correct-creed Sunni Hanafi, and devotion to the noble Companions is embedded in his blood and veins. At most it can be said that in (Allah) the author (may Allah have mercy on him) had in view the structure whose highest and best individuals are the group of the noble Companions.

It is due to the sacrifice of the Companions that today we have Islam; whoever denies the Companions is an agent of Satan.

Objection: Describing (al-Din) with an adjective is against clarity, because by 'Din' is meant the religion of Islam?

Answer: The definition of 'Din' encompasses generality (the ways laid down by Allah which, with the choice of people of intellect, guide them towards actions that have only good). This includes all previous religions. Therefore, the adjective (al-Qayyim) was mentioned so that by 'Din' is meant only the religion of Islam, because all previous religions have been abrogated and distorted; only the religion of Islam is preserved and upright until the Day of Judgment.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'وعلى اله الذين قاموا بنصرة الدين القويم' from the matn. The commentator begins by discussing the concept of takhsis (specification) when an attribute is mentioned in a context of praise. He then explains that the word 'آل' (family) has been interpreted in three ways by the commentator (al-Sharh): first, specifically the purified wives; second, the offspring of the Prophet; third, all pious believers. He deems the third interpretation more suitable as it is general.

He then provides a detailed note: the primary referent of Ahl al-Bayt is the purified wives, as per the verse from Surah al-Ahzab. However, the cautious opinion is that it includes all descendants of Abbas and Abdul Mutallib because the prohibition of Zakat applies to all of them, as indicated by a hadith.

An objection is raised: why did the author not mention the Companions separately? The responder defends the author's Sunni creed and suggests that the phrase 'آل' in context includes the Companions as the foremost individuals of the structure the author had in mind.

Another objection concerns the description 'القویم' for 'الدین'. The response explains that 'الدین' in its definition includes all past religions, so the adjective is necessary to specify Islam as the only preserved and upright religion.

This passage demonstrates how textual analysis and careful reasoning are used to reconcile different interpretations and defend the author's position.

Key Terms
آل (Al): Family; in this passage, it is interpreted in three ways: specific wives, specific offspring, or general pious believers.
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification; restricting a general term by an attribute or context, here exemplified by an attribute in a praise context making it specific.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which interpretation of 'آل' does the commentator consider most appropriate?
A) That it refers only to the purified wives.
B) That it refers only to the Prophet's offspring.
C) That it includes all pious believers.
D) That it refers only to the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The meaning of 'آل' in praise contexts is broadened to include all pious supporters, demonstrating the Hanafi principle that attributes in praise specify the described.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Qualification of 'al-Din' as 'al-Qawim': Specifying the General
Explaining why 'al-din' is qualified as 'al-qawim' to specify Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a general term (amm) requires a restrictive attribute (qayd) and apply this principle to analyze Quranic and textual expressions.

Core Idea
A general term needs qualification to specify the intended meaning; 'al-qawim' restricts 'al-din' to Islam alone.

In usul al-fiqh, understanding when a word is general (amm) and when it is restricted (muqayyad) is crucial for correct interpretation. This passage addresses a subtle objection: if 'al-din' already means Islam, why add 'al-qawim'? The answer reveals a key principle: the general includes all revealed religions, so the attribute is needed to specify the one that remains valid. Let's unpack this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the objection: why would someone say that adding the attribute is against clarity? Understand the assumption that 'din' alone suffices.
The objector thinks 'din' is already specific.
2
Examine the generality of 'din'
The answer gives a definition of 'din' that shows it encompasses all divine ways. Recognize that 'din' is a general term (amm) that includes Islam and previous religions.
The definition is given to show inclusion.
3
See how 'al-qawim' restricts
The attribute 'al-qawim' (the upright) limits the general to only Islam, because other religions are abrogated and distorted. This is a classic case of takhsis (specification) of an amm by a descriptive attribute.
The attribute functions as a qayd (restriction).
4
Apply the principle elsewhere
Think of other texts where a general term is qualified to avoid ambiguity. For example, 'aqimu al-salah' (establish prayer) – 'salah' is general, but its pillars and conditions restrict it.
This principle reappears in many fiqh derivations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض .... (الدین) کی صفت ذکر کر نا خلاف نصاحت ہے کیونکہ دین سے دین اسلام مراد ہے؟ جواب دین کی تعریف میں عموم ہے (اللہ کے وضع کردہ وہ طریقے جو اہل عقل و خرد کو ان کے ختیار کے ساتھ ایسے کاموں کی طرف گامزن کریں جن میں سرتا پا خیر ہی خیر ہو ) یہ تمام ادیان سابقہ کو شامل ہے اس لئے صفت (القویم ) ذکر فرمائی تا کہ دین سے فقط دین اسلام مراد ہو کیونکہ تمام ادیان منسوخ و محرف ہو چکے ہیں قیامت تک محفوظ ومستقیم دین اسلام ہی ہے۔
Objection: Mentioning the attribute of (al-Din) is against clarity because by 'din' is meant the religion of Islam? Answer: The definition of 'din' has generality (the ways laid down by Allah that direct people of intellect and reason, with their choice, towards actions that are entirely good). This includes all previous religions. Therefore, the attribute (al-Qawim) was mentioned so that only the religion of Islam is meant by 'din', because all other religions have been abrogated and distorted, and until the Day of Judgment, only the religion of Islam is preserved and upright.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
The passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the word 'al-din' in the text. The objector argues that adding the attribute 'al-qawim' (the upright) to 'al-din' is unnecessary because 'din' already refers to Islam. The answer clarifies that the term 'din' linguistically has a general meaning encompassing all divinely revealed ways. To specify that only Islam is intended, the attribute 'al-qawim' is added, as previous religions are abrogated and distorted. This demonstrates a key usul principle: a general term can be qualified to restrict its meaning.

Key Terms
الدین (al-din): The ways laid down by Allah that direct people of intellect and reason, with their choice, towards actions that are entirely good.
القویم (al-qawim): The upright, straight religion; used here to specify Islam as the only preserved and valid religion.
صفت (sifah): Attribute or adjective that qualifies a noun.
عموم (umum): Generality; the property of a term that applies to all individuals of its category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the word 'al-din' qualified with 'al-qawim'?
A) To emphasize that Islam is the best religion.
B) To specify that only Islam is meant, as 'din' includes all previous religions.
C) Because the text requires a rhythmic pattern.
D) To indicate that religion is upright by nature.

Key Takeaway
A general term (amm) can be restricted by an attribute (qayd) to specify the intended meaning; this principle prevents ambiguity and is essential for accurate textual interpretation.

The Quran's Definition: Mutawatir Transmission without Doubt
Analysis of the third attribute in the definition of the Quran and the mutawatir condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of the Hanafi definition of the Quran (transmitted from the Prophet, mutawatir, without doubt) and evaluate the dispute between the majority and Imam al-Khassaf regarding the function of 'bila shubha'.

Core Idea
The Quran is speech transmitted from the Prophet mutawatir without doubt; 'bila shubha' is either emphasis or restriction.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi usul definition of the Quran, focusing on the third attribute: 'al-manqul 'anhu taqlan mutawatiran bi la shubha'. We will see how this attribute resolves a potential circularity in an earlier definition and explore a key dispute among Hanafi scholars about whether 'bila shubha' is a restrictive clause or mere emphasis. This sharpens our understanding of the categories of transmission (mutawatir, mashhur, ahad) and their role in defining revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the circularity objection
The text raises the problem that defining the Quran as 'what is written in mushafs' leads to circularity (dawr) because it defines the Quran by the mushafs and the mushafs by the Quran. Understand why this definition fails to be comprehensive (jami') and exclusive (mani') without the third attribute.
2
Analyze the third attribute
The attribute 'al-manqul 'anhu taqlan mutawatiran bi la shubha' resolves the circularity. Break down each component: 'al-manqul 'anhu' (transmitted from him, i.e., the Prophet), 'taqlan' (by recitation/transmission), 'mutawatiran' (tawatur), and 'bila shubha' (without doubt). Understand how each element restricts the definition.
3
Examine the exclusion function of 'mutawatir'
The term 'mutawatiran' excludes qira'at that are transmitted by khabar wahid (single chain) or khabar mashhur (well-known but not tawatur). Note the examples given: Ubayy ibn Ka'b's qira'a on fasting (khabar wahid) and Ibn Mas'ud's qira'a on the theft verse (khabar mashhur).
4
Evaluate the dispute over 'bila shubha'
Compare the majority (jumhur) view, which treats 'bila shubha' as emphasis (ta'kid) because mutawatir is inherently above doubt, with Imam al-Khassaf's view that it is a restriction to exclude his second category of mutawatir (mutawatir bi shubha = khabar mashhur). Understand the practical difference.
5
Consider the lam condition (jinsi vs. ahdi)
The text notes that if 'al-mushaf' is generic (lam jinsi), the third attribute is a restrictive condition; if it is specific (lam ahdi), the third attribute becomes merely explanatory. Recognize how this affects the interpretation of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں اگر کہا جائے ( ما كتب فيه القرآن ) یہ وہ مصاحف ہیں جن میں قرآن مجید لکھا گیا تو سوال ہوتا ہے کہ ما القرآن ؟ اور جواب میں کہا جاتا ہے (ملكتب في المصاحف ) پھر "ما المصاحف ؟" کا سوال ہوتا ہے اس طرح دور لازم آتا ہے اس لئے سرے سے تعریف ہی نہیں کی۔ پہلا احتمال موجب اشکال ہے کہ تعریف قرآن کیلئے جامع اور خول [؟] غیر سے مانع نہیں کیونکہ مصاحف جمع ہے مصحف کی اور مصحف کا لفظ تو ہر کتاب پر صادق آتا ہے کیونکہ وہ مصاحف میں لکھی گئی ہے۔ جواب ... اس تمیم سے تعریف پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑتا کیونکہ آگے صفت ثالث آرہی ہے جس سے تعریف جامع مانع ہوگئی۔ قوله المنقول عنه تقلا متواتر أبلا شبهة : یہ قرآن کی تیسری صفت ہے اور پہلے احتمال کی تقدیر پر یہ قید احترازی ہے کیونکہ عنہ کی ضمیر الرسول کی طرح راجع ہے اور الرسول سے مراد حضور اکرم صلی اللہ وسلم ہی ہیں لہذا تعریف جامع مانع ہوگئی - قوله متواتراً : یہ قید احترازی ہے اس کے ذریعہ وہ قراءات خارج ہو گئیں جو خبر واحد کے طریق پر منقول ہیں مثلاً قراءة ابی بن کعب رضی اللہ عنہ دربارہ قضائے رمضان نیز وہ قرآت خارج ہو گئیں جو خبر مشہور کے طریق پر منقول ہیں۔ مثلاً حد سرقہ میں حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی ( قرأت فاقطعوا أیمانہما اور فصيام ثلاثة ايام متتابعات قوله بلا شبهة: متواتر کی تعریف سے بلاشبہ کی حیثیت کی تعیین ہو جاتی ہے جان لیجئے کہ متواتر کی تعریف میں جمہور اور امام خصاف کے درمیان اختلاف ہے: (1) جمہور کے ہاں متواتر اسی کو کہتے ہیں جو شک وشبہ سے بالاتر ہو لہذا بلا شبهة تاکید ہے متواتر کے لئے ۔ (۲) امام خصاف کے ہاں متواتر کی دو قسمیں ہیں: اول متواتر بلا شبهة یہ وہی ہے جو جمہور کے ہاں متواتر کہلاتی ہے۔ دوم... متواتر بالشبهة اس سے مراد خبر مشہور ہے۔ چنانچہ امام خصاف کے نزدیک بلا شبهة قید احترازی ہے اور خبر مشہور سے احتراز کے لئے نکتہ یہ تمام تفصیل اس صورت میں تھی جبکہ المکتوب في المصاحف میں .... المصاحف کا الف لام جنسی ہو اگر الف لام عہدی ہو تو چونکہ تعریف قرآن مجید کے ساتھ خاص ہو چکی ہے لہذا پوری صفت ثالثہ قید کی بجائے ماقبل کا بیان ہوگی۔
If it is said: 'What is written in the Quran' — these are the mushafs in which the Noble Quran is written, then the question arises: 'What is the Quran?' And in response it is said: 'That which is written in the mushafs.' Then the question 'What are the mushafs?' arises; thus a circularity (dawr) occurs, so no definition is given at all. The first probability causes an objection: that the definition is not comprehensive (jami') and exclusive (mani') from others because mushaf is plural of mushaf, and the word mushaf applies to every book that is written in mushafs. The answer: This completion (tatmim) does not affect the definition because the third attribute follows, by which the definition becomes comprehensive and exclusive. His saying: 'al-manqul 'anhu taqlan mutawatiran bi la shubha' — this is the third attribute of the Quran, and on the first probability this is a restrictive clause, because the pronoun 'anhu refers back to al-rasul, and al-rasul means the Prophet (peace be upon him), so the definition becomes comprehensive and exclusive. His saying 'mutawatiran': this is a restrictive clause, by which those qira'at transmitted by way of khabar wahid are excluded, e.g., the qira'a of Ubayy ibn Ka'b (رضی اللہ عنہ) regarding the fasting of Ramadan, and also those qira'at transmitted by way of khabar mashhur, e.g., in the verse of cutting hands, the qira'a of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (رضی اللہ عنہ): 'faqta'u aymanahuma' and 'fasiyam thalathati ayyam muttabi'at'. His saying 'bila shubha': the definition of mutawatir determines its status as being without doubt. Know that there is a difference between the majority (jumhur) and Imam al-Khassaf in the definition of mutawatir: (1) According to the majority, mutawatir is that which is above doubt and suspicion, so 'bi la shubha' is a confirmation (ta'kid) for mutawatir. (2) According to Imam al-Khassaf, mutawatir has two types: first, mutawatir bi la shubha, which is the same as what the majority call mutawatir; second, mutawatir bi shubha, which means khabar mashhur. So according to Imam al-Khassaf, 'bi la shubha' is a restrictive clause to exclude khabar mashhur. Note: All this explanation is when the lam in al-mushaf is for genus (jinsi); if it is for a specific known (ahdi), then since the definition is already specific to the Noble Quran, the entire third attribute becomes not a condition but an explanation of what precedes.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a definitional analysis of the Quran from a Hanafi usul text. The author begins by addressing a potential circularity in defining the Quran as 'that which is written in the mushafs'. The objection is that this definition fails to be comprehensive (jami') and exclusive (mani') because the term 'mushaf' can apply to any book. The response is that the third attribute ('al-manqul 'anhu taqlan mutawatiran bi la shubha') resolves the issue by restricting the definition to what is transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) with tawatur without doubt. Then the author explains each element: 'al-manqul 'anhu' ties it to the Prophet, 'mutawatiran' excludes qira'at transmitted singly or through mashhur chains, giving examples: Ubayy ibn Ka'b's qira'a on fasting and Ibn Mas'ud's qira'a on the theft penalty. Then 'bila shubha' is analyzed, revealing a dispute between the majority (jumhur) and Imam al-Khassaf. For the majority, 'bila shubha' is a ta'kid (emphasis) because mutawatir by definition is above doubt. For Imam al-Khassaf, mutawatir includes a lower category (mutawatir bi shubha) meaning khabar mashhur, so 'bila shubha' becomes a restrictive clause to exclude that. Finally, the author notes that this entire discussion applies only if 'al-mushaf' is generic (jinsi); if it refers to the specific mushafs (ahdi), then the third attribute is merely explanatory, not a restriction.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawatir): A narration transmitted by so many chains that it is certain and above doubt.
خبر مشہور (khabar mashhur): A narration transmitted by a lesser number than mutawatir but widely known; below mutawatir in authenticity.
تعریف جامع مانع (ta'rif jami' mani'): A definition that includes all members of the defined class (jami') and excludes all non-members (mani').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority (jumhur) of Hanafi scholars, what is the function of the phrase 'bila shubha' in the definition of the Quran?
A) It is a restrictive clause to exclude khabar mashhur from being mutawatir.
B) It is an emphasis (ta'kid) because mutawatir is inherently above doubt.
C) It indicates that the Quran is transmitted without any doubt, unlike other books.
D) It refers to the condition that the Quran must be recited without doubt in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is defined by its transmission through mutawatir chains without any doubt, and the phrase 'bila shubha' serves as emphasis (majority view) or restriction (al-Khassaf view), affecting how we classify widely-known transmissions.

Imam Khasaf's Two Types of Mutawatir
Defines Imam Khasaf's classification of mutawatir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Khasaf's two types of mutawatir and distinguish khabar mashhur from true mutawatir.

Core Idea
Imam Khasaf divides mutawatir into true mutawatir and mutawatir bil-shuhra, which is actually khabar mashhur.

Imam Khasaf, a prominent Hanafi usuli, offers a nuanced classification of mutawatir hadith. Understanding his two types helps clarify the boundary between certain and widely transmitted reports. This lesson parses his definition and highlights the restrictive role of the phrase 'bila shubha'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Read the passage and extract the two categories Imam Khasaf mentions for mutawatir.
Look for the terms 'mutawatir bila shubha' and 'mutawatir bil-shuhra'.
2
Define each type
State what each type means in your own words. Mutawatir bila shubha is the standard definition; mutawatir bil-shuhra is explicitly equated with khabar mashhur.
Note that the second type is not true mutawatir but a different category.
3
Analyze the restrictive phrase
The author says 'bila shubha' (without doubt) is a restrictive condition. Explain why it is added and what it excludes.
It excludes any report that falls short of certain knowledge, i.e., khabar mashhur.
4
Link to broader Hanafi usul
Relate this classification to the standard Hanafi tripartite division: mutawatir, mashhur, ahad. Where does mutawatir bil-shuhra fit?
It corresponds to khabar mashhur, which is between mutawatir and ahad in strength.

(۲) امام خصاف کے ہاں متواتر کی دو قسمیں ہیں: اول متواتر بلا شصتہ یہ وہی ہے جو جمہور کے ہاں متواتر کہلاتی ہے۔ دوم... متواتر بالشمعتہ اس سے مراد خبر مشہور ہے۔ ہے۔ چنانچہ امام خصاف کے نزدیک بلا شمہ قید احترازی ہے اور خبر مشہور سے احتراز کے لئے
(2) According to Imam Khasaf, mutawatir has two types: First, mutawatir bila shubha – this is what the majority call mutawatir. Second, mutawatir bil-shuhra (by fame) – by this is meant khabar mashhur. Hence, according to Imam Khasaf, the phrase 'bila shubha' is a restrictive condition, and it is for avoidance of khabar mashhur.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage introduces a technical classification of mutawatir by Imam Khasaf, a Hanafi usuli. He divides mutawatir into two: the first is true mutawatir (without any doubt), identical to the common definition. The second is mutawatir bil-shuhra, which actually refers to khabar mashhur (widely transmitted but not reaching mutawatir level). This is a nuanced position within Hanafi usul. The author notes that the phrase 'bila shubha' is used restrictively to exclude khabar mashhur from the definition of mutawatir.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawātir): A hadith reported by a large number of narrators at each level, making falsehood impossible.
خبر مشہور (khabar mashhūr): A hadith transmitted by three or more narrators at some stages but not reaching mutawatir; it is also called mustafid.

Key Takeaway

The Four Categories of Words in Usul al-Fiqh
Explaining the necessity of knowing the divisions of nazm and ma'na and introducing the four categories of words

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the four categories of words (specific, general, common, interpreted) and explain the logical basis for their enumeration in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Words are classified by whether they indicate one meaning or many, and whether that meaning is exclusive or shared.

In Hanafi usul, understanding the divisions of words (nazm) and meaning (ma'na) is essential for deriving Shariah rulings. The commentator on Noor al-Anwar explains that all rulings of the Shariah depend on knowing these divisions. He then introduces a logical four-fold classification of words based on how they indicate meaning. This classification is the foundation for interpreting commands and prohibitions in the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the necessity
The commentator asserts that Shariah rulings are known only by knowing the divisions of words and meaning. Recognize that this lesson is about the classification of words as they indicate meaning.
2
Grasp the logical enumeration
The classification is based on two binary distinctions: whether a word indicates one meaning or multiple, and if one meaning, whether it indicates individually (without sharing) or with sharing among individuals. This yields four categories: specific (khass) for one meaning exclusive, general (amm) for one meaning shared, common (mushtarak) for multiple meanings equally, and interpreted (mu'awwal) for multiple meanings with one preferred.
The commentator provides a detailed reasoning for the enumeration.
3
Identify each category with examples
Work through the definitions: khass (e.g., 'Zaid'), amm (e.g., 'men'), mushtarak (e.g., 'ayn'), and mu'awwal (e.g., a word whose apparent meaning is abandoned for a stronger evidence).
The key_terms section provides definitions.
4
Apply the classification to a text
Choose a Quranic verse or hadith, identify the word type, and consider how the classification affects the ruling. For instance, the word 'mushrikun' in 'اقتلوا المشركين' is amm, including all polytheists.
This connects theory to practice.

وجه حصر:
کتاب اللہ میں یا تو معنی سے بحث ہو گی یا نہیں اگر معنی سے بحث ہو گی تو تقسیم اربع ہے اگر لفظ سے بحث ہو تو حیثیات کا اعتبار ہوگا جو تین ہیں یا تو لفظ سے بحث معنی موضوع الہ میں استعمال کے اعتبار سے ہوگی یا ظہور اور خفاء معنی کے اعتبار سے ، اگر استعمال کے اعتبار سے ہو تو تقسیم ثالث ہے ورنہ اگر بحث ظہور و خفاء کے اعتبار سے ہو تو تقسیم اول ۔ دلالت کے اعتبار سے ہو تو تقسیم جانی بھر ہر تقسیم کی کئی قسمیں ہیں جن کا بیان بالترتیب آگے آرہا ہے۔

قوله الااول فى وجوه النظم صيغة ولغة پہلی تقسیم اعظم کی باعتبار وضع اقسام و انواع کے بیان میں ہے کہ لفظ ایک معنی کے لئے وضع ہوا ہے یا کثیر معانی کیلئے ۔ صیغہ اور لغت کہنا یہ ہیں وضع ہے۔

اشکال ..... لغت مادہ اور ہیئت دونوں پر مشتمل ہے جبکہ صیغہ فقط ہیئت کو کہتے ہیں جبکہ لغت دونوں کو شامل ہے تو صیغہ کو کیوں ذکر کیا؟

جواب ..... یہاں صیغہ کو لغت کے مقابل ذکر کیا ہے اس لئے اب لغت سے فقط مادہ اور صیغہ سے فقط ہیئت مراد ہوگی۔

قوله : وهى اربعة الخاص والعام والمشترك والمؤول تقسیم اول کی چار اقسام ہیں جن میں وجہ حصریہ ہے۔

اقسام اربعہ کا بیان بطریق وجه حصر لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے یا تو وہ معنی واحد پر دلالت کرے گا یا معانی کثیرہ پر، اگر لفظ معنی واحد پر دلالت کرے تو پھر دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو دلالت علی سبیل الانفراد عن الافراد ہوگی یا مع الاشتراک بین الافراد اگر اول ہے تو خاص اثانی ہے تو عام ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر لفظ کی دلالت
His statement: 'And the rulings of the Shariah are only known by knowing their divisions.' The author (may Allah have mercy on him) is explaining the division of nazm (words) and ma'na (meaning). Because all the rulings of the Shariah, whether related to what is permissible or forbidden, can only be known when we know the divisions of the Book of Allah. Saying 'aqsam' (parts) is not correct because under Islam there is nothing; rather here under 'division' there are numerous categories. The dual form 'aqsamihima' indicates that these divisions are of both nazm and ma'na. In the division, consideration of the word is insofar as it indicates meaning.

His statement: 'And that is four.' In the four divisions, for ease of retention, stating that enumeration is more appropriate.

Explanation of enumeration: In the Book of Allah, either meaning is discussed or not. If meaning is discussed, then there are four divisions. If words are discussed, then there are three considerations: either the discussion of words is regarding meaning intended for use, or regarding clarity and obscurity of meaning. If regarding use, then it is the third division. Otherwise, if the discussion is regarding clarity and obscurity, then it is the first division. Regarding indication, it is the second division. Each division has several types, which will be mentioned in order later.

His statement: 'The first is regarding the forms of nazm, sigha and lugha.' The first great division is regarding the consideration of the coinage (wad') of categories and types: whether a word is coined for one meaning or for multiple meanings. Saying 'sigha' and 'lugha' refers to coinage.

Objection: Lugha includes both the root (maddah) and the form (hay'ah), while sigha only refers to form. Since lugha includes both, why is sigha mentioned separately?

Answer: Here, 'sigha' is mentioned in contrast to 'lugha', so now 'lugha' means only the root and 'sigha' means only the form.

Objection: Lugha is the principle and basis for sigha, and the principle should be mentioned first. Why is sigha given precedence?

Answer: Here, the intention is not principle and derivative; rather our discussion is about general and specific. Sigha is more related to general and specific than lugha, so it was given precedence.

His statement: 'And they are four: specific, general, common, and interpreted.' The first division has four categories, and there is a reason for enumeration.

Statement of the four categories by way of enumeration: A word is either indicative of a single meaning or multiple meanings. If it indicates a single meaning, then there are two possibilities: either it indicates individually (without sharing among individuals), then it is specific; or it indicates with sharing among individuals, then it is general. Similarly, if the word indicates...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Noor al-Anwar, explaining the necessity of understanding the divisions of words (nazm) and meaning (ma'na) in order to derive rulings of the Shariah. The commentator first clarifies that the author's use of 'aqsamihima' (their two divisions) refers to both nazm and ma'na, and that the division of words is considered in relation to their indication of meaning. The commentator then introduces the four-fold division of words that will be discussed. He provides a logical justification for the enumeration: the discussion in the Book of Allah either concerns meaning (yielding four categories) or words (yielding three aspects, each with subcategories). The first division is then introduced: the classification of words according to coinage (wad'), i.e., whether a word is coined for one meaning or multiple. This leads to the types of sigha (form) and lugha (root). The commentator addresses two objections: first, why mention sigha separately from lugha when lugha includes both? The answer is that here sigha and lugha are contrasted, so each takes a narrower meaning. Second, why prioritize sigha over lugha? The answer is that the discussion is about generality and specificity, which is more directly tied to sigha. Finally, the four categories of the first division are listed: خاص (specific), عام (general), مشترك (common/shared), and مؤول (interpreted). The commentator provides a logical reasoning for the enumeration: words either indicate one meaning or multiple. If one meaning, it is either exclusive to one individual (specific) or shared among individuals (general). If multiple meanings, it is either used for each meaning equally (common) or one meaning is preferred over others (interpreted). This classification is foundational for understanding how commands and prohibitions in the Quran and Sunnah are to be understood.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A word indicating a single meaning individually, i.e., exclusive to one individual or a limited set without sharing among individuals (e.g., Zaid, this man).
عام (amm): A word indicating a single meaning shared among all individuals of a class (e.g., 'men' includes all men).
مشترك (mushtarak): A word coined for multiple meanings equally and used for each (e.g., 'ayn meaning eye, spring, spy, etc.).
مؤول (mu'awwal): A word that carries a preferred meaning over its apparent meaning due to evidence, i.e., interpreted away from its literal sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) خاص، عام، مشترك، مجمل
D) حقيقة، مجاز، مشترك، مؤول

Key Takeaway
The four-fold division of words—specific, general, common, and interpreted—is based on whether the word indicates one meaning or many, and whether that meaning is exclusive or shared.

The Fourfold Classification of Words in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Explaining the four types of words based on linguistic assignment (وضع)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given word using the Hanafi usul framework into specific, general, common, or interpreted, and explain the underlying reasoning.

Core Idea
A word is either for one meaning or many; if one, it is specific or general; if many, it is common or interpreted.

This passage lays the foundation for understanding how words convey rulings in Hanafi jurisprudence. Before diving into specific textual analysis, we must master this essential classification. The author first clarifies a nuance about the terms 'form' (صيغة) and 'lexicon' (لغة), then presents a logical exhaustive division (وجه حصر) of all words into four categories. This classification directly impacts how we derive legal rulings from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Initial Distinction
Note that the passage begins by distinguishing between 'form' (صيغة) and 'lexicon' (لغة). The author resolves a potential confusion: here 'lexicon' means only the root (مادة), while 'form' means the structure (هيئة). Recognize that the discussion prioritizes form because it is more directly related to generality and specificity.
This is a terminological clarification specific to this passage.
2
Grasp the Exhaustive Division (وجه حصر)
The division is based on whether a word indicates one meaning or multiple meanings. If one meaning, it either indicates an individual on its own (خاص) or a commonality among individuals (عام). If multiple meanings, either one is preponderant through interpretation (مؤول) or none is preponderant (مشترک). This is a binary tree covering all possibilities.
Memorize the tree: word → one meaning (خاص or عام) / many meanings (مؤول or مشترک).
3
Define Each Category Concisely
خاص: a word that indicates a single individual meaning exclusively (e.g., 'Muhammad'). عام: a word that indicates a commonality shared among all individuals of its category (e.g., 'men'). مشترک: a word that indicates multiple meanings with equal weight (e.g., 'عين' can mean eye or spring). مؤول: a word that indicates multiple meanings but one is given preponderance through evidence (e.g., 'القرء' interpreted as menstruation or purity based on context).
These definitions are foundational for applying usul al-fiqh later.
4
Test the Classification on Examples
Take a few common Arabic words and determine their category. For instance: 'رجل' (man) is عام because it applies to all men. 'يد' (hand) is عام (all hands) but can be made specific. 'عين' is مشترک. 'صلاة' (prayer) is خاص in its legal sense (the specific prescribed prayer).
Practice makes this classification intuitive.

تقسیم اول کی چار اقسام ہیں جن میں وجہ حصریہ ہے۔
اقسام اربعہ کا بیان بطریق وجه حصر
لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے یا تو وہ معنی واحد پر دلالت کرے گا یا معانی کثیرہ پر، اگر لفظ معنی واحد پر دلالت کرے تو پھر دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو دلالت علی سبیل الانفراد عن الافراد ہوگی یا مع الاشتراک بین الافراد اگر اول ہے تو خاص اثانی ہے تو عام ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر لفظ کی دلالت معانی کثیرہ پر ہے تو یا معانی متعدہ میں سے ایک کو بطریق تاویل ترجیح [؟] معنی کو تر نیج حاصل نہیں ہے تو مشترک ہے ، ورنہ موکول ہے۔
He said: The first (division) is regarding the forms of wording, (in terms of) form and lexicon. The first major division, according to (linguistic) assignment, is about explaining the types and kinds: that a word is placed for one meaning or for multiple meanings. Saying 'form' and 'lexicon' refers to assignment. Objection: Lexicon includes both root and form, while form is only the structure; lexicon includes both, so why mention form? Answer: Here, form is mentioned in contrast to lexicon; therefore, by 'lexicon' only the root is meant, and by 'form' only the structure. Objection: Lexicon is the basis and foundation for form, and the basis is given precedence; why has form been given precedence? Answer: The intended here is not basis and subsidiary; rather, our discussion is about generality and specificity, and form has more relation to generality and specificity than lexicon, so it was given precedence. He said: And they are four: the specific, the general, the common, and the interpreted. The first division has four types, which are exhaustive. Explanation of the four types in an exhaustive manner: A word is not free from two states: either it indicates a single meaning or multiple meanings. If it indicates a single meaning, then there are two possibilities: either it indicates on the basis of individuality from individuals, or with sharedness among individuals. If the first, it is specific; if the second, it is general. Similarly, if the word indicates multiple meanings, then either one of the multiple meanings is given preponderance through interpretation, or it is not; if it is not given preponderance, it is common; otherwise, it is interpreted.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of words in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins the first major division of words, which is based on linguistic assignment (وضع): whether a word is assigned for a single meaning or multiple meanings. The author first addresses a potential confusion: why mention both 'form' (صیغہ) and 'lexicon' (لغت) when lexicon encompasses both root and form? The answer is that in this context, 'lexicon' is restricted to the root (مادہ) and 'form' to the structure (ہیئت), so they are distinct. Then, an objection is raised that lexicon is the foundation and should be mentioned first, but the author responds that the discussion is about generality and specificity, and form is more directly related to that, so form is given precedence. The four types are then introduced: خاص (specific), عام (general), مشترک (common), and مؤول (interpreted). The reasoning for this exhaustive division (وجه حصر) is explained: A word either indicates one meaning or many. If one meaning, it either indicates an individual on its own (خاص) or a commonality among individuals (عام). If many meanings, either one is given preponderance through interpretation (مؤول) or none is preponderant (مشترک). This classification is foundational for understanding how texts convey rulings in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
خاص (khaass): A word that indicates a single individual meaning exclusively, without sharing among individuals.
عام (aamm): A word that indicates a commonality shared among all individuals of its category.
مشترک (mushtarak): A word that indicates multiple meanings with equal weight, no one being preponderant without context.
مؤول (mu'awwal): A word that indicates multiple meanings but one is given preponderance through interpretation (تأویل) based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the exhaustive division that yields the four categories?
A) Word indicates one meaning or many; if one, it is خاص or عام; if many, it is مشترک or مؤول.
B) Word indicates a person or thing; if person, it is خاص; if thing, it is عام.
C) Word indicates a physical object or an abstract concept; if physical, it is مشترک; if abstract, it is مؤول.
D) Word indicates a necessary meaning or a possible meaning; if necessary, it is خاص; if possible, it is عام.

Key Takeaway
The four-category classification (خاص، عام، مشترک، مؤول) is an exhaustive framework for analyzing any Arabic word's indication in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

The Four Modes of Textual Inference and the Fifth Comprehensive Division
Defines four modes of textual inference and introduces a fifth meta-division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the four modes of textual inference (ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida) and explain the fifth comprehensive division according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The four modes of textual inference are the primary tools of istidlal; the fifth division adds meta-analysis for systematic comprehension.

This passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar elucidates the Hanafi classification of how rulings are derived from textual evidence. You already know that texts can be literal or metaphorical, explicit or implicit. Now we delve into the four recognised modes of inference: from the explicit wording, from implied indication, from lexical denotation, and from necessary implication. The commentator then introduces a fifth overarching division that organizes these modes in terms of their linguistic origins, meanings, priority order, and rulings, leading to a comprehensive taxonomy of 80 subcategories. Understanding this framework is essential for mastering Hanafi istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four modes of inference
From the passage, list the four modes: 'ibarah an-nass (explicit wording), isharah an-nass (implied indication), dalalah an-nass (lexical denotation), and iqtida an-nass (necessary requirement). Understand that these are the tools a mujtahid uses to extract rulings from the divine text.
2
Distinguish between inference from wording and from meaning
The passage explains that inference is either from the wording (nazm) or from the meaning. If from wording, it is either 'ibarah (if the wording was placed for that meaning explicitly) or isharah (if implied). If from meaning, it is either dalalah (if the meaning is lexical) or iqtida (if the meaning is required for coherence).
This binary classification is key to understanding the Hanafi approach.
3
Understand the fifth comprehensive division
After listing the four modes, the author introduces a fifth division that applies to all of them. It consists of four aspects: (1) knowing the linguistic derivations (mawadi'), (2) knowing the terminological meanings (ma'ani), (3) knowing the order of precedence (tartib) when conflicts arise, and (4) knowing the rulings (ahkam) which are definitive, speculative, or requiring suspension.
4
Calculate the resulting subcategories
The passage states that when each of the four aspects of the fifth division is combined with each of the four modes of inference, the total number of subcategories becomes 20x4 = 80. This demonstrates the systematic nature of Hanafi usul.
The 20 comes from the four aspects multiplied by the four modes? Actually 4 modes × 4 aspects = 16, but the text says 20x4. Possibly the 20 refers to subdivisions of modes? The exact calculation is not critical; the point is the combinatorial approach.
5
Analyze the objection and response regarding the fifth division
The commentator addresses why the majority of usul scholars (jumhur) do not mention this fifth division. The response is that it is not a division of the Qur'anic text itself but a division of the 'names' of the divisions (asma' al-aqsam), and therefore the majority ignored it. The author follows Imam al-Bazdawi, who included it for systematic organization.
This highlights a subtle but important difference in Hanafi usul methodology.

They are (1) Haqiqah (literal) and (2) Majaz (metaphorical). Then he made Sarih (explicit) and Kinayah (implicit) as subdivisions of Haqiqah and Majaz, which is better, as is clear from the reason of enumeration. He said: 'And the fourth is about knowing the ways of pausing at the intended meaning.' It is a fourth division explaining the methods by which the mujtahid and the one seeking evidence become aware of the intended meaning of the Legislator. He said: 'And they are also four: inference from the expression of the text (ibarah an-nass), from its indication (isharah), from its denotation (dalalah), and from its requirement (iqtida).' The face: The one seeking evidence has only two forms: he will infer from the word or from the meaning. If his inference is from the wording (nazm), it is examined: if the wording was placed for that meaning explicitly, it is ibarah an-nass; otherwise, isharah an-nass. If the inference is from the meaning, there are two forms: if it is the lexical meaning of that wording, then it is dalalah an-nass; otherwise, iqtida an-nass. He said: 'And after knowing these divisions, there is a fifth division that encompasses all.' The matn author (may Allah have mercy on him) states that fundamentally these are the four divisions of the text, from which, going forward, all divisions are obtained. For easy memorization, see the diagram. According to the usuliyyun, these are the same divisions in this topic, but a fifth division is also mentioned, which relates to each of the aforementioned divisions. He said: 'And it is also four: knowing their places, their meanings, their order, and their rulings.' Below is a brief summary of each: (1) Knowing the places of the text: it means knowing the lexical derivational meanings of the mentioned divisions. (2) Knowing the meanings of the text: it means knowing the terminological concepts of the mentioned divisions. (3) Knowing the order of the text: it means that if there is a conflict among the subdivisions of one division, which is given precedence and which is postponed. (4) Knowing the rulings of the text: the rulings of the text are of three types: definitive (qati), conjectural (zanni), and obligatory suspension (wajib at-tawaqquf). When these four divisions are combined with each subdivision of every division, a total of 80 divisions are obtained (20x4=80). Objection: If this is also a division of the Qur'anic text, why did the majority (jumhur) not mention it? Answer: This is not a division of the Qur'an but a division of the names (asma') of the divisions of the Qur'an, therefore the majority ignored it. Objection: Why did the author (may Allah have mercy on him) not follow the majority? What is the reason for mentioning this division? Answer: The author, in usul, follows the Imam of the Usuliyyin, Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali al-Bazdawi (may Allah have mercy on him), so he mentioned it following his way. Note: It is a fact that the author could not fully follow 'Ali al-Bazdawi (may Allah have mercy on him) because he (Bazdawi) fully adhered to these four divisions in every explanation throughout the book, but the author...
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the fourfold classification of inferring rulings from a text (nass) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The commentator first clarifies that the previous discussion distinguished between haqiqah (literal) and majaz (metaphorical), and further between sarih (explicit) and kinayah (implicit). Then, the fourth major section is introduced: knowing the ways of ascertaining the Legislator's intention. The commentator states that there are four methods of istidlal (inference) from a text: 'ibarah (explicit wording), isharah (implied indication), dalalah (lexical denotation), and iqtida' (necessary implication). He then explains the rationale: the seeker of evidence either infers from the wording itself or from the meaning. If from wording, if the wording is explicitly placed for that meaning, it is 'ibarah; otherwise, it is isharah. If from meaning, if the meaning is the lexical meaning of the wording, it is dalalah; otherwise, it is iqtida'. After this, a fifth comprehensive division is introduced, which applies to all four types. This fifth division consists of four aspects: (1) knowing the linguistic origins (mawadi) of the terms, (2) knowing their terminological meanings (ma'ani), (3) knowing the order of priority (tartib) when conflicts arise, and (4) knowing the rulings (ahkam) which are qati (definitive), zanni (conjectural), or wajib at-tawaqquf (obligatory suspension). When each of these four aspects is applied to each of the four types of textual inference, a total of 80 subcategories result. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: why does the author include this fifth division when the majority of usul scholars (jumhur) do not? The answer is that this division is not about the Qur'an itself but about the names of the divisions, so the majority ignored it. Another objection asks why the author did not follow the majority; the response is that the author follows the method of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, who included it. The note acknowledges that the author could not fully replicate Bazdawi's thorough application of the four aspects to every division throughout the book.

Key Terms
عبارة النص (ibarah an-nass): Inference from the explicit wording of the text, where the wording was placed specifically for that meaning.
إشارة النص (isharah an-nass): Inference from an implied indication of the text, where the wording is not primarily intended for that meaning but it is understood from context.
دلالة النص (dalalah an-nass): Inference from the lexical meaning of the wording, i.e., the meaning that the words naturally convey according to language.
اقتضاء النص (iqtida an-nass): Inference from what the text necessarily requires or implies, even if not explicitly stated, to make sense of the text.
معرفة مواضعها (ma'rifat mawadi'iha): Knowing the linguistic-lexical origins (ishtiqaq) of the terms used in the four types of textual inference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many total subcategories result when the four aspects of the fifth division are applied to each of the four types of textual inference?
A) 80
B) 20
C) 16
D) 4

Key Takeaway
The four modes of textual inference (ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida) are the core tools of Hanafi istidlal; the fifth division provides a meta-framework for systematic analysis, resulting in an 80-fold taxonomy that distinguishes Hanafi usul from the simpler jumhur approach.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Definition and Types of Khaas in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Defining Khaas and dividing it into three categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Khaas, identify each part of the definition, and classify words into the three types of Khaas.

Core Idea
Khaas is a word placed for a single known meaning; it excludes ambiguous and general words.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of Khaas, a fundamental concept in usul al-fiqh. Understanding Khaas is essential for correctly applying legal texts, as it determines the scope of a ruling. We will dissect the definition and explore its three categories with examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the definition of Khaas in the passage: 'كل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد'. Commit it to memory.
2
Analyze each term
Break down the definition: 'لفظ' (word) as genus, 'وضع' (placed) excludes meaningless words, 'لمعنى معلوم' (for a known meaning) excludes ambiguous words if interpreted as 'known intent', and 'على الانفراد' (individually) excludes both ambiguous and general words.
The phrase 'على الانفراد' is key; it restricts the word to a single meaning, not multiple or general.
3
Understand the exclusions
Note what each part excludes: 'وضع' excludes muhmal (meaningless); 'معلوم' excludes mushtarak (ambiguous) if intent is unknown; 'على الانفراد' excludes mushtarak and 'aam (general). The passage explains the dual role of 'على الانفراد'.
There is a nuance: if 'معلوم' means 'known expression', then only 'على الانفراد' excludes ambiguity.
4
Learn the three categories
The passage lists three types of Khaas: Khusoos al-Jins (specificity of genus, e.g., 'insan'), Khusoos al-Naw' (specificity of species, e.g., 'rajul'), and Khusoos al-Ayn (specificity of individual, e.g., 'Zaid'). Each applies to a different level of specificity.
5
Apply to examples
Practice classifying words: 'insan' is Khusoos al-Jins, 'rajul' is Khusoos al-Naw', 'Zaid' is Khusoos al-Ayn. Explain why each is Khaas and which part of the definition applies.
Ensure you can distinguish between 'aam and khaas: 'aam covers all individuals under a common meaning (e.g., 'mu'minun'), while khaas is restricted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حمداللہ نے معنی اور احکام ذکر کئے ہیں ترتیب بھی کہیں کہیں ہےاور کہیں نہیں مر مواضع و پوری کتاب میں کہیں بھی ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔

كل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد
ترجمہ: خاص ہر وہ لفظ ہے جس کو معنی معلوم کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہو علی الانفراد فوائد قیود لفظ... بمنزلہ جنس کے ہے۔ دو وضع یہ قید احترازی ہے اس سے لفظ مہمل نکل گیا۔ معلوم سے مراد اگر ( معلوم المراد ) ہے تو اس سے مشترک نکل جائیگا ۔ اس لئے کہ اس کی مراد معلوم نہیں ہوتی اور اگر اس سے مراد ( معلوم البیان ہے ) تو پھر یہ قید احترازی نہیں ہوئی بلکہ علی الانفراد کی قید سے مشترک نکل جائیگا۔
نشته ..... علی الانفراد کی قید مشترک اور عام سب سے احتراز کیلئے ہے بایں طور کہ مشترک میں دوسرے معانی پائے جاتے ہیں جبکہ عام میں تو افراد بھی ہوتے ہیں۔
وهو اما أن يكون خصوص الجنس أو خصوص النوع او
خصوص العين كانسان ورجل وزيد
خاص کی تقسیم
خاص کی تعین نہیں ہیں۔
(1) خصوص الجنس (۲) خصوص النوع (۳) خصوص العین
Praise be to Allah, He mentioned meanings and rulings. The arrangement is sometimes present and sometimes not. He did not mention the subject matters anywhere in the entire book.
Discussion of Khaas:
His statement: 'As for Khaas, it is every word placed for a known meaning, individually.'
Technical definition of Khaas: Every word placed for a known meaning, individually.
Translation: Khaas is every word that has been placed for a known meaning, individually. Benefits: 'word' is like a genus. 'Placed' is a restrictive clause to exclude meaningless words. If 'known' means 'known intent', then it excludes ambiguous words (mushtarak) because their intent is not known. If it means 'known expression', then this clause is not restrictive, and the clause 'individually' alone excludes ambiguous words.
Note: The clause 'individually' is to avoid ambiguous and general words, in that ambiguous words contain other meanings, while general words contain individuals.
And it is either: specificity of genus, or specificity of species, or specificity of individual, like 'insan', 'rajul', 'Zaid'.
Division of Khaas: The types of Khaas are three: (1) Specificity of genus, (2) Specificity of species, (3) Specificity of individual.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage begins with a brief remark about the author's style, then transitions to the discussion of Khaas. The definition of Khaas is taken from the matn: 'كل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد' meaning a word placed for a single known meaning. The sharh explains each term: 'لفظ' (word) is the genus, 'وضع' (placed) excludes meaningless words, 'لمعنى معلوم' (for a known meaning) ensures the meaning is known; if interpreted as 'known intent' it excludes mushtarak (ambiguous) because its intent is ambiguous. The key phrase 'على الانفراد' (individually) excludes both mushtarak (which carries multiple meanings) and 'aam' (general, which applies to many individuals). The three types of Khaas are: خصوص الجنس (specificity of genus) e.g. 'insan' (human), خصوص النوع (specificity of species) e.g. 'rajul' (man), and خصوص العين (specificity of individual) e.g. 'Zaid' (a proper name). This classification helps in understanding the scope of legal texts.

Key Terms
خاص (khaas): A word placed for a specific meaning, covering one individual or class.
علي الانفراد (ala al-infiraad): The word denotes its meaning individually, not including other meanings or individuals.
خصوص الجنس (khusoos al-jins): Specificity of genus: a word covering a general category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition presented, which of the following is excluded by the phrase 'علي الانفراد' (individually)?
A) Lafz muhmal (meaningless word)
B) Lafz mushtarak (ambiguous word)
C) Lafz mufassar (explicit word)
D) Lafz mubayyan (clarified word)

Key Takeaway
Khaas is a word with a single, known meaning; it is definitive in its indication and covers three levels of specificity: genus, species, and individual.

خاص: Definition, Types, and the Logician-Jurist Dispute on جنس/نوع
Defining خاص, its three categories, and the logician-jurist disagreement on جنس/نوع

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'خاص' as a word placed for a known meaning individually, classify it into three types (خصوص الجنس, خصوص النوع, خصوص العين) with examples, and explain the methodological difference between logicians and jurists in defining جنس and نوع.

Core Idea
خاص is a single-meaning word; it may be genus-specific, species-specific, or individual-specific, and jurists define جنس by purpose, not essence.

This passage from Khulasat al-Anwar Urdu Sharh Noor al-Anwar introduces the usul concept of 'خاص' (the specific). Understanding خاص is foundational because it governs how legal texts narrow down general commands. The text also highlights a key methodological divergence: logicians define genus by essences, while jurists define it by purposes. This distinction directly impacts how legal rulings are derived from shared purposes in qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the definition of خاص
Identify the matn definition 'كل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد'. Break down each qualifier: 'لفظ' excludes meaningless sounds; 'وضع' indicates conventional placement; 'معنى معلوم' excludes ambiguous words; 'على الانفراد' excludes general words. Understand why each exclusion is necessary.
The commentary explains that 'معلوم' can be interpreted either as 'known in intent' or 'known in clarification', affecting which words are excluded.
2
Classify the three types of خاص
Using the examples 'إنسان' (human), 'رجل' (man), and 'زيد' (Zayd), differentiate: خصوص الجنس is specific to a genus but applies to multiple individuals (e.g., human includes men and women); خصوص النوع is specific to a species with a shared purpose (e.g., man refers to males); خصوص العين refers to a single specific entity (e.g., Zayd). Note that each type has a different level of specificity.
The division is not exhaustive; these are common categories.
3
Contrast the logician and jurist definitions of جنس and نوع
Read the passage's explanation: logicians define genus based on essence (e.g., 'حيوان ناطق'), while jurists define it based on purposes. This difference arises because logicians seek the reality of things, whereas jurists focus on legal purposes (maqasid).
The logician's definition given is 'كلى مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالحقائق دون الاغراض' – a universal predicable of many differing in realities without regard to purposes.

قوله : أما الخاص فكل لفظ وضع المعنى معلوم على الانفراد
خاص کی اصطلاحی تعریف
كل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد
ترجمہ: خاص ہر وہ لفظ ہے جس کو معنی معلوم کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہو علی الانفراد فوائد قیود لفظ... بمنزلہ جنس کے ہے۔ دو وضع یہ قید احترازی ہے اس سے لفظ مہمل نکل گیا۔ معلوم سے مراد اگر ( معلوم المراد ) ہے تو اس سے مشترک نکل جائیگا ۔ اس لئے کہ اس کی مراد معلوم نہیں ہوتی اور اگر اس سے مراد ( معلوم البیان ہے ) تو پھر یہ قید احترازی نہیں ہوئی بلکہ علی الانفراد کی قید سے مشترک نکل جائیگا۔

وهو اما أن يكون خصوص الجنس أو خصوص النوع او خصوص العين كانسان ورجل وزيد
خاص کی تقسیم

(1) خصوص الجنس (۲) خصوص النوع (۳) خصوص العین

خصوص الجنس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ منی کے اعتبار سے اس کی جنس خاص ہو اگر چہ جن افراد پر صادق آتی ہے وہ متعدد ہوں جیسے انسان اس کے تحت رجل اور امراة دونوں داخل ہیں اور دونوں کے اغراض بھی مختلف ہیں۔

لہذاوہ تعریف میں اس کو مد نظر رکھتے ہیں۔ جبکہ علمائے فقہ شئی کی اغراض کو زیر بحث لاتے ہیں

كلى مقول على كثير ين مختلفين بالحقائق دون الاغراض
Discussion of خاص (The Specific). His statement: As for the specific, it is every word placed for a known meaning individually. Technical definition of خاص: Every word placed for a known meaning individually. Translation: خاص is every word that has been placed for a known meaning individually. Benefits of the qualifiers 'word'... it is like a genus. The two 'وضع' (placing) is a restrictive qualifier; through it the meaningless word is excluded. If by 'known' is meant 'known in intent', then the ambiguous word is excluded because its intent is not known. And if by it is meant 'known in clarification', then this restrictive qualifier does not apply; rather, through the qualifier 'individually' the ambiguous word is excluded. A point: The qualifier 'individually' serves to exclude both the ambiguous and the general, in that the ambiguous has other meanings while the general has individuals. And it is either specificity of genus or specificity of species or specificity of individual, like 'human', 'man', and 'Zayd'. Division of خاص: Its divisions are not limited. (1) Specificity of genus (2) Specificity of species (3) Specificity of individual. The meaning of specificity of genus is that its genus is specific in terms of meaning, even though the individuals to which it applies are numerous, like 'human' includes both man and woman, and their purposes are different. Specificity of species: Its meaning is that its species is specific in terms of meaning, even though the individuals to which it applies are numerous, like 'man' applies to individuals all of whom share one purpose. Specificity of individual: Its meaning is that it is for a specific person and indicates a specific entity in terms of meaning, like 'Zayd' is the name of a known particular individual. The disagreement between logicians and jurists in the definition of species and genus. It is appropriate to write the reason and basis of this disagreement before mentioning the definitions. It is that the logicians' discussion is about the essence and reality of a thing, so they consider that in the definition. Whereas the jurists discuss the purposes of things, thus they consider purposes in the definition. The logicians' definition of genus: A universal predicable of many things differing in their realities without regard to purposes.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a lesson in Hanafi usul al-fiqh defining the term 'خاص' (specific) and its categories. It begins by citing the matn definition: 'أما الخاص فكل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد' – the specific is every word placed for a single known meaning. The commentator then breaks down the qualifiers: 'لفظ' excludes meaningless utterances; 'وضع' indicates convention; 'معنى معلوم' excludes ambiguous words if taken as 'known in intent', but if taken as 'known in clarification' then it is not restrictive; 'على الانفراد' excludes both ambiguous and general words. The passage then divides خاص into three types: خصوص الجنس (genus-specific), e.g., 'إنسان' (human) which includes both men and women but is specific to the human genus; خصوص النوع (species-specific), e.g., 'رجل' (man) which is specific to the male gender; and خصوص العين (individual-specific), e.g., 'زيد' (Zayd) which refers to a particular person. Finally, the author introduces a methodological dispute: logicians define جنس (genus) based on essence (e.g., 'حيوان ناطق'), while jurists define it based on purposes (maqasid). The logicians' definition given is 'كلى مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالحقائق دون الاغراض' – a universal predicable of many things differing in realities without regard to purposes. This sets up the distinction between usul al-fiqh and logic.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A word placed for a known meaning individually (كل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد)
خصوص الجنس (khusus al-jins): Specificity of genus: a word that is specific to a genus but applies to multiple individuals within that genus, e.g., 'insan' (human) includes men and women
خصوص النوع (khusus al-naw'): Specificity of species: a word that is specific to a species, applying to individuals sharing a common purpose, e.g., 'rajul' (man) refers to males only
جنس (jins): Genus: a universal predicable of many differing in realities (logician) or a category defined by shared purposes (jurist).
نوع (naw'): Species: a subcategory under genus where individuals share a specific purpose, e.g., 'رجل' (man).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT a type of خاص?
A) خصوص الجنس
B) خصوص النوع
C) خصوص العين
D) خصوص الصفة

Key Takeaway
خاص is a word indicating a single known meaning, and its three categories—جنس, نوع, عين—show how specificity operates from broad class to unique individual.

Three Types of Khusoos and the Dispute on Jins and Naw'
Defines three types of specificity and contrasts definitions of genus and species between logicians and usuliyun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of specificity (khusoos) in Hanafi usul and explain the difference between logicians' and jurists' definitions of genus and species.

Core Idea
Specificity in Hanafi usul is about scope based on purpose and essence; jurists prioritize purposes, logicians prioritize realities.

In this passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar, we explore how Hanafi usuliyun categorize specificity into three types: khusoos al-jins, al-naw', and al-'ayn. This classification is essential for understanding how general terms are qualified. The passage then highlights a fundamental methodological divergence between logicians and jurists in defining universal terms like jins and naw', revealing how each discipline's focus—essences versus purposes—shapes its definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of specificity
From the passage, list khusoos al-jins, al-naw', and al-'ayn, noting the key feature that distinguishes each.
Focus on the condition of differing or agreeing purposes (aghrad).
2
Contrast the logicians' and jurists' definitions of jins and naw'
Write down both definitions side by side. Observe that logicians use 'realities' (haqa'iq) while jurists use 'purposes' (aghrad) as the differentia.
This reflects their different objects of study: essence vs. legal objectives.
3
Understand the methodological reason
The passage states that logicians investigate the essence (kahna) of a thing, while jurists investigate its purposes (aghrad). Reflect on why this leads to swapping jins and naw' for many universals.
A universal like 'human' is a species for logicians but a genus for jurists.
4
Apply the classification to a new example
Consider the word 'prayer' (salah). According to jurists, different prayers have different purposes, so it is jins. For logicians, prayer is a species because its reality is the same.
This illustrates the practical impact of the definitions.

Specificity of genus: It means that its genus is specific in terms of [؟], even if the individuals to which it applies are multiple, like 'human' — under it both man and woman are included, and their purposes are different. Specificity of species: It means that its species is specific in terms of meaning, even if the individuals to which it applies are multiple, like 'man' — its application is to individuals whose purpose is one. Specificity of individual: It means that it is for a specific person and indicates a particular essence in terms of meaning, like 'Zaid' is knowledge of a known specified [person]. The disagreement between logicians and jurists in the definition of species and genus: It is appropriate that before mentioning the definitions, the reason and basis of this disagreement be written, which is that the logicians' discussion is about the essence and reality of a thing, so they keep that in view in the definition. While the jurists bring the purposes of a thing under discussion; therefore they also consider purposes in the definition. Logicians' definition of genus: A universal predicated of many differing in realities but not in purposes. Usuliyun's definition of genus: A universal predicated of many differing in purposes but not in realities. Logicians' definition of species: A universal predicated of many agreeing in realities but not in purposes. Usuliyun's definition of species: A universal predicated of many agreeing in purposes but not in realities. Based on this difference in definitions, you will see that many universals that are species for logicians will be genera for usuliyun, and similarly many universals that are of the type of species for usuliyun are included in the category of genera for logicians. Points... The author of the book has returned the pronoun to the divider of the division. Its referent, at first glance, seems to be 'specific'. Based on this, it is commonly said that this is a division of specific. However, in reality the referent of the pronoun is not specific but rather that concept which was mentioned implicitly under the definition of specific. In short, this is a division of specificities, as is also apparent from the names of the divisions.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This is a definition passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar, clarifying the three types of Khusoos (specificity) in Usul al-Fiqh. The author first explains each type: خصوص الجنس (specificity of genus) where the term applies to multiple individuals sharing the same genus but different purposes, like 'human' covering both men and women whose aims differ; خصوص النوع (specificity of species) where the term applies to multiple individuals sharing the same purpose, like 'man' where all men share the aim of masculinity; and خصوص العین (specificity of the individual) which refers to a specific person, like 'Zaid'. The passage then discusses a key methodological difference between logicians (مناطقہ) and jurists (اصولیین) in defining universal terms (کلیات): logicians focus on essence (حقائق) while jurists focus on purposes (اغراض). This leads to different definitions of جنس and نوع. For example, what logicians call a species may be a genus for jurists if their purposes differ. Finally, a note clarifies that the division of 'specific' into three types actually refers to the division of 'specificities' (خصوص) not the term 'خاص' itself, because the pronoun refers back to the concept of specificity mentioned earlier.

Key Terms
خصوص الجنس (khusoos al-jins): Specificity in terms of genus: the word applies to multiple individuals of the same genus but with different purposes.
خصوص النوع (khusoos al-naw'): Specificity in terms of species: the word applies to multiple individuals of the same species sharing the same purpose.
خصوص العین (khusoos al-'ayn): Specificity of the individual: the word applies to a specific person or entity, exclusive to that individual.
جنس (jins): According to usuliyun: a universal predicated of many differing in purposes but not in realities. According to logicians: differing in realities but not purposes.
نوع (naw'): According to usuliyun: a universal predicated of many agreeing in purposes but not in realities. According to logicians: agreeing in realities but not purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi jurists (Usuliyun), which of the following is the correct definition of 'جنس' (genus)?
A) A universal predicated of many differing in realities but not in purposes.
B) A universal predicated of many differing in purposes but not in realities.
C) A universal predicated of many agreeing in realities but not in purposes.
D) A universal predicated of many agreeing in purposes but not in realities.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, specificity is categorized by genus, species, or individual based on purpose; and usuliyun define universal terms by purposes, not essences.
