The Definitive Ruling of the Specific Term (Khas)
Defines the ruling (hukm) of the specific term (khas).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hukm of a specific term (khas) in Hanafi usul and apply it to distinguish khas from general terms.

Core Idea
A specific term (khas) definitively includes its designated meaning and excludes all other possibilities; it is inherently clear.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines a foundational category in Hanafi usul: the specific term (khas). Understanding its definitive nature is crucial for correctly deriving rulings from the primary sources. Unlike general terms which may require specification (takhsis), a specific term is immediately binding and clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its ruling
Locate the Arabic term 'khas' in the passage and note that its hukm (ruling) is that it includes the specific entity (makhsus) definitively (qat'an).
The ruling is stated at the beginning: 'And its ruling is that it includes the specific definitively.'
2
Understand definitive inclusion
The term 'definitively' (qat'an) means there is no room for alternative meanings. The specific term points to its referent with certainty.
This contrasts with general terms (amm) which are probabilistic (zanni) until specified.
3
Recognize the exclusion of other meanings
The passage states clearly: 'and does not admit of explanation because it is clear'—meaning it needs no further elaboration and cannot be interpreted otherwise.
This is a key feature: khas is bayyin (clear) by itself.
4
Examine the example
The example 'Amr and poet' is given. 'Amr' (a proper name) and 'poet' (a descriptive noun) are both specific: they refer only to their respective meanings. No other meaning like 'Zaid' or 'knowledge' can be intended.
The example illustrates that even if the word could theoretically have other uses, in the given context it is specific.
5
Contrast with general terms
Consider how this differs from a general term (amm) like 'men' (rijal) which includes all men but can be specified. The khas term is narrower and immediately certain.
This contrast is essential for usul analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وحكمه ان يتناول المخصوص قطعاً ولا يحتمل البيان لكونه بيناً
خاص کا حکم :۔ : خاص کا حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ مخصوص کو قطعی طور پر شامل ہوتا ہے۔ اور غیر کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا مثلا عمر و شاعر جب سے صرف عمر اور شاعر ہی مفہوم ہو نگے کیونکہ دونوں خاص ہیں دوسرا کوئی معنی مثلا زید که با علم ، خطابت وغیر ہ اس کا اس میں کوئی شائبہ نہیں ہے۔
His saying: And its ruling is that it includes the specific definitively and does not admit of explanation because it is clear. The ruling of khas: The ruling of khas is that it includes the specific definitively, and it does not have any possibility of other (meanings). For example, 'Amr and poet' — only 'Amr' and 'poet' will be understood because both are specific. No other meaning like 'Zaid, knowledge, eloquence, etc.' has any shade (of meaning) in it.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage explains the legal ruling (hukm) of a specific term (خاص) in Hanafi usul. The commentator is expanding on the matn of Noor al-Anwar. The ruling is that a specific term indicates its designated meaning (مخصوص) with certainty (قطعاً) and does not admit of any other possible meaning. It is inherently clear (بين) and requires no further explanation (بيان). For instance, the proper noun 'Amr' specifically refers to that individual, and the word 'poet' specifically refers to someone who composes poetry; they cannot mean anything else like 'Zaid' or 'knowledge'. This definitiveness is a key feature of خاص as opposed to عام (general), which is probabilistic. In Hanafi usul, خاص is considered qat'i (definitive) in its meaning, unlike general terms which require specification.

Key Terms
خاص (khas): A word that indicates a specific individual, group, or meaning with no possibility of other interpretations.
مخصوص (makhsus): The specific entity or meaning that a khas term refers to.
حكم (hukm): The legal characteristic or effect of a term: in this case, definitive inclusion and exclusion of other meanings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) of a specific term (خاص) according to Hanafi usul al-fiqh?
A) It is ambiguous and requires explanation.
B) It definitively includes its specific meaning and excludes all others.
C) It always carries multiple possible meanings.
D) It is only used in metaphors.

Key Takeaway
Every specific term (khas) yields a definitive ruling (qat'i al-dalalah) and requires no further explanation because its meaning is clear and exclusive.

Definitions of Jins and Naw in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Defining universal terms (kulli) as jins and naw according to logicians and usul scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usuli definitions of jins and naw, distinguish them from the logicians' definitions, and identify the referent of the pronoun in the matn's division of khas.

Core Idea
Jins and naw are defined differently by logicians and usuliyun: usuliyun prioritize purposes, logicians prioritize essence.

In this lesson, we examine the definitions of two key universal terms—jins (genus) and naw (species)—as used in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The source passage from Khulasat al-Anwar contrasts these definitions with those of the logicians (mantiqiyun) and clarifies a subtle point about the division of 'khas'. Understanding these distinctions is essential for precise textual analysis and classification of legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate the definitions of jins and naw as given by usuliyun. Note that each definition specifies agreement/difference in either purposes (aghrad) or realities (haqa'iq).
The Arabic terms: 'كلى مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالأغراض دون الحقائق' for jins; 'كلى مقول على كثيرين متفقين بالأغراض دون الحقائق' for naw.
2
Contrast with logicians' definitions
Compare the usuli definitions with the logicians' definitions provided in the text. Observe that the criteria are swapped: logicians use realities, usuliyun use purposes.
Logicians' naw: 'متفقين بالحقائق دون الأغراض'.
3
Analyze the pronoun reference
Recognize that the author's note clarifies that the pronoun in 'division of khas' actually refers to the meaning (mafhum) of khas, not the term itself, making it a division of 'khusus' (specifics).
The text says: 'ضمیر کا مرجع خاص نہیں بلکہ وہ مفہوم ہے...'
4
Apply the concept
Consider how this distinction affects the classification of universals in usul al-fiqh, such as in the analysis of 'amm and khass.
For example, a term like 'salah' may be classified differently as jins or naw depending on the definition used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصولیین کی تعریف جنس
كلى مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالا غراض دون الحقائق
مناطقہ کی تعریف نوع
كلى مقول على كثيرين متفقين بالحقائق دون الاغراض
اصولیین کی تعریف نوع
كلى مقول على كثير ين متفقين بالا غراض دون الحقائق

مرہ تعریفوں کے اسی اختلاف کی بناء پر آپ دیکھیں گے کہ بہت ہی کلیاں جو مناطقہ کے ہاں نوع ہیں وہ اصولیین کے ہاں جنس ہوں گی اور اسی طرح بہت سی کلیاں جو اصولیین کے ہاں من قبیل النوع میں دو مناطقہ کے نزدیک اجناس کے زمرے میں شامل ہیں۔ نکتے... صاحب کتاب نے تقسیم کے مقسم کی طرف ضمیر لوٹائی ہے جس کا مرجع سرسری نظر میں ) خاص) ہی محسوس ہوتا ہے اس بناء پر صرف عرف میں یہی کہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ یہ خاص کی تقسیم ہے جبکہ در حقیقت ضمیر کا مرجع خاص نہیں بلکہ وہ مفہوم ہے جس کا ذکر خاص کی تعریف کے تحت ضمناً ہو چکا الغرض یہ خصوص کی تقسیم ہے۔ اس طرح کہ اقسام کے ناموں سے بھی ظاہر ہے۔
Definition of jins according to usuliyun: a universal predicated of many differing in purposes but not in realities. Definition of naw according to logicians: a universal predicated of many agreeing in realities but not in purposes. Definition of naw according to usuliyun: a universal predicated of many agreeing in purposes but not in realities. Due to this difference in definitions, you will see that many universals that are naw according to logicians are jins according to usuliyun, and many universals that are from the category of naw according to usuliyun are included in the category of ajnas according to logicians. Note: The author of the book returned the pronoun to the divided thing (maqsam), whose reference at first glance appears to be 'khas', therefore it is said in custom that this is a division of khas, while in reality the pronoun does not refer to khas but to the meaning that was implicitly mentioned under the definition of khas. In short, this is a division of khusus (specifics), as is also apparent from the names of the divisions.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage defines the terms 'jins' (genus) and 'naw' (species) as used by the logicians (mantiqiyun) and the usul scholars (usuliyun). The difference lies in the criteria: logicians classify based on sharing in the essence (haqiqah) regardless of accidental purposes, while usuliyun classify based on sharing in the purposes (aghrad). The author then notes a subtle point: when the matn author said 'division of khas', the pronoun actually refers to the meaning under the definition of khas, not the term khas itself. Thus it is a division of 'khusus' (specifics). This clarification prevents misunderstanding that the division applies to 'khas' as a technical term.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): A universal predicated of many differing in purposes but not in realities (according to usuliyun).
نوع (naw): A universal predicated of many agreeing in purposes but not in realities (according to usuliyun).
كلى (kulli): A universal term that applies to many individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The meaning (mafhum) of khas.
C) The logicians' definition of jins.
D) The usuli definition of naw.

Key Takeaway
The usuli definitions of jins and naw prioritize purposes, distinguishing them from logicians' definitions, and careful attention to pronoun reference prevents misinterpretation of the division of khas.

The Rulings of Khas and Their Application to Ta'dil al-Arkan
Explaining two rulings of khas and a furu' on ta'dil al-arkan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a text as khas, apply the Hanafi rule that khas does not accept bayan tafsir, and derive the ruling on ta'dil al-arkan accordingly.

Core Idea
A specific Quranic text is definitive and cannot be expanded by a single-narrator hadith, making ta'dil al-arkan wajib, not fard.

In this passage we meet a foundational Hanafi usul principle: the rulings of khas (specific term). The author states that khas includes its referent definitively and does not accept clarificatory bayan (bayan tafsir). He then applies this principle to the well-known dispute over ta'dil al-arkan in prayer. Understanding this will sharpen your ability to handle conflicts between Quranic texts and ahad reports.

Guided Path
1
State the two rulings of khas
Identify the two legal characteristics of a khas (specific) word: (1) it definitively covers only its designated meaning, and (2) it does not accept bayan tafsir because it is already clear.
The second ruling is the focus of the furu' (branches).
2
Distinguish bayan tafsir from other types
Note that khas does accept other forms of bayan (taqrir, tabdil, taghyir). Only bayan tafsir is excluded, because khas is inherently clear and does not need elaboration.
Bayan tafsir clarifies something ambiguous; khas is not ambiguous.
3
Identify the key Quranic text as khas
The Quranic command 'Irka'u wa-sjudu' (Bow and prostrate) contains the words 'ruku' and 'sujud', both of which are specific terms. They refer exclusively to the acts of bowing and prostrating, not to any postural adjustments like ta'dil.
Ruku' means bending from standing; sujud means placing the forehead on the ground.
4
Apply the principle to the hadith of the Bedouin
The hadith (khabar wahid) that implies ta'dil is part of the prayer cannot serve as bayan tafsir for the Quranic khas, because khas does not accept bayan tafsir. To make ta'dil fard would be adding a new obligation via khabar wahid, which is impermissible.
Khabar wahid is zanni; Quranic khas is qat'i; qat'i cannot be overridden by zanni.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Hanafi school, omitting ta'dil makes the prayer valid but makruh tahriman (wajib omitted); in the Shafi'i school, the prayer would be invalid (fard omitted).
This is the real-world consequence of the usul dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وحكمه ان يتناول المخصوص قطعاً ولا يحتمل البيان لكونه بيناً
خاص کا حکم :۔
:
خاص کا حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ مخصوص کو قطعی طور پر شامل ہوتا ہے۔ اور غیر کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا مثلا عمر و شاعر جب سے صرف عمر اور شاعر ہی مفہوم ہو نگے کیونکہ دونوں خاص ہیں دوسرا کوئی معنی مثلا زید که با علم ، خطابت وغیر ہ اس کا اس میں کوئی شائبہ نہیں ہے۔

خاص کا دوسرا حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ بیان کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا، کیونکہ یہ خود واضح ہوتا ہے۔ بیان سے مراد بیان تفسیر ہے باقی رہا بیان تقریر و بیان تبدیل و تغییر تو یہ ان کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ تفریعات ( خاص کے حکم ثانی پر )
مصنف نے اس پر چار تفریعات اٹھائی ہیں کہ خاص بیان کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔
قوله : فلا يجوز الحاق التعديل بأمر الركوع والسجود على سبيل الفرض.
(1) پہلی تفریح
امام شافعی اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ تعدیل ارکان فرض ہے اور وہ حدیث اعرابی سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔ ہمارے نزدیک تعدیل ارکان واجب ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں حکم ہے (ارکعو واسجدو ..... الخ) رکوع اور سجدہ دونوں لفظ خاص ہیں ایک معنی معلوم کے لئے وضع کئے گئے ہیں۔ رکوع کا معنی ہے (انحناء عن القيام) اور سجدے کا معنی ہے (وضع الجبهة على الارض) - خاص چونکہ بیان کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا اس لئے یہ حدیث خاص کے لئے بیان نہیں بن سکتی۔ اگر ہم اس حدیث کے ذریعے تعدیل کو رکوع اور سجود کے حکم کے ساتھ بطور فرض کے لا حق کرینگے تو خبر واحد کے ذریعہ کتاب اللہ کے حکم خاص میں زیادتی کا ارتکاب لازم آئے گا اور یہ ایک مسلمہ امر ہے کہ خبر واحد کے ذریعہ خاص یعنی کتاب اللہ میں زیادتی جائز نہیں ۔ لہذا جو کتاب اللہ سے ثابت ہے یعنی نفس تجدہ اور رکوع اسے ہم کہیں گے کہ وہ فرض ہے اور جو سنت سے ثابت ہے ( یعنی تعدیل ارکان وغیرہ ) اسے ہم کہیں گے کہ وہ واجب ہے۔
His saying: And its ruling is that it includes the specific (makhsus) definitively and does not accept bayan because it is clear. The ruling of khas: It includes the specific definitively and does not accept the possibility of other meanings. For example, 'Amr' and 'poet' when they are specific only indicate 'Amr' and 'poet' because both are specific; no other meaning like Zayd, knowledge, oratory, etc., has any trace. Second ruling of khas: It does not accept bayan (clarification) because it is itself clear. By bayan is meant bayan tafsir; as for bayan taqrir and bayan tabdil wa taghyir, it does accept them. Branches on the second ruling of khas: The author adduces four branches that khas does not accept bayan. His saying: So it is not permissible to attach ta'dil to the command of ruku' and sujud as obligatory (fard). First branch: Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf say that ta'dil al-arkan is fard, and they argue from the hadith of the Bedouin. In our view, ta'dil al-arkan is wajib. Our evidence is that in the Holy Qur'an the command is 'Bow and prostrate...' etc. Ruku' and sujud both are specific words placed for known meanings. Ruku' means 'bowing from standing' and sujud means 'placing the forehead on the ground'. Since khas does not accept bayan, this hadith cannot serve as a bayan for khas. If we attach ta'dil to the ruling of ruku' and sujud as fard through this hadith, then it would necessarily entail adding to the specific ruling of the Book of Allah through khabar wahid, and it is an established matter that addition through khabar wahid to the specific ruling of the Book of Allah is not permissible. Therefore, what is established from the Book of Allah, i.e., the act of sujud and ruku' itself, we call it fard, and what is established from the Sunnah (i.e., ta'dil al-arkan, etc.) we call it wajib.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage states the two rulings of 'khas' (specific term) in Hanafi usul: First, it definitively covers only its specific referent and no other; second, it does not accept bayan tafsir (clarificatory explanation) because it is already clear. However, it can accept other types of bayan (like taqrir, tabdil, taghyir). The author then applies this principle to the dispute over ta'dil al-arkan (straightening the posture during prayer). The Hanafi position, relying on the Quranic commands for ruku' and sujud which are specific, holds that these commands are definitive and cannot be expanded by a khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith) to make ta'dil fard. Therefore, ta'dil is wajib, not fard. The Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf view that ta'dil is fard from the hadith is rejected because it would be adding to the Quranic text via a speculative source. This illustrates the usul principle that a specific text (khas) from the Quran is qat'i and cannot be overridden by a zanni source.

Key Terms
خاص (khas): A word that is specific in meaning, indicating a particular individual or set of individuals exclusively.
بيان (bayan): Clarification or explanation; specifically bayan tafsir (elaborative explanation) is not applicable to khas because it is already clear.
تعديل اركان (ta'dil al-arkan): Straightening the posture in prayer, including standing upright after ruku' and sitting upright between prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is ta'dil al-arkan not considered fard?
A) Because the hadith of the Bedouin is weak.
B) Because making it fard would be adding to a specific Quranic text via khabar wahid, which is impermissible.
C) Because ta'dil al-arkan is not mentioned in the Quran at all.
D) Because the Quran commands only ruku' and sujud, so ta'dil is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule that khas is qat'i and does not accept bayan tafsir means that no khabar wahid can elevate a sunnah act to the level of fard when the Quranic text is already specific.

The Khas Principle and Its Application to Wudu Conditions
Applies khas principle to wudu conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that khas is not subject to bayan to evaluate whether a prophetic hadith can establish a condition (shart) in wudu.

Core Idea
Adding conditions to a khas Quranic command via khabar wahid would be naskh, so wala, tartib, tasmiyah, niyyah are sunnah, not fard.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle through a concrete fiqh dispute. The Quranic verse on wudu is khas, commanding only washing and wiping. Can prophetic hadith add additional conditions like continuity, order, naming, or intention? The Hanafi answer: no, because khas does not accept bayan from khabar wahid; doing so would abrogate the Quran, which is impermissible. Understanding this argument clarifies why Hanafis treat these acts as sunnah while other schools treat them as conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Khas Text
Extract the Quranic verse (5:6) and identify the words 'ghusl' (washing) and 'mash' (wiping) as khas (specific) for those actions.
Khas is a term that denotes a specific, unambiguous meaning.
2
Identify the Disputed Additions
List wala, tartib, tasmiyah, and niyyah; note that each is supported by prophetic hadith (khabar wahid).
These are not mentioned in the Quranic verse.
3
Apply the Hanafi Rule
Khas is qat'i (definitive) and cannot be expanded by zanni (speculative) evidence like khabar wahid. Adding conditions would be ziyadah 'ala al-nass, which amounts to naskh (abrogation), and naskh of the Quran by khabar wahid is impermissible.
This is the core argument: the hadith cannot create new obligations beyond the khas text.
4
Evaluate Opposing Views
Malikis treat wala as a condition based on prophetic practice (considered bayan). Shafi'is treat tartib and niyyah as conditions, arguing the verse is amm (general) and the hadith specify (takhsis). Zahiris treat tasmiyah as a condition from a direct hadith.
Each school's usul framework determines how they interpret the same sources.
5
Conclude the Hanafi Position
Thus, the Hanafi ruling: washing and wiping are fard; wala, tartib, tasmiyah, niyyah are sunnah.
This shows the practical consequence of the khas principle.

قوله وبطل شرط الولاء والترتيب والتسمية والنية في آية الوضوء (۲) دوسری تفریح ہمارے نزدیک وضو میں ولا و ترتیب ، تسمیہ اور نیت کی شرط لگانا باطل ہے بلکہ یہ چیزیں سنت ہیں۔ جب کہ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ ولا یعنی اعضاء کو اس طرح دھونا کہ ایک عضو خشک نہ ہونے پائے کہ دوسرا عضو دھو ڈالے یہ شرط ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس پر دوام کیا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ نیت اور ترتیب شرط ہے ترتیب کیلئے ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ب لا يقبل الله صلوة امرا ..... الخ یعنی اللہ تعالٰی اس شخص کی نماز قبول نہیں کرتا جو اعضاء کے دھونے میں ترتیب کا لحاظ نہ کرے او کما قال علیہ السلام ۔ اور نیت کیلئے یہ حدیث ہے انما الاعمال بالنیات یعنی تمام اعمال کی صحت کا دارو مدار نیتوں پر ہے۔ اہل ظواہر کہتے ہیں کہ وضو کیلئے تسمیہ شرط ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ الا وضو لمن لم يسم ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ہمیں وضو میں غسل اور مسح کا حکم دیا ہے کما قال الله تعالى تبارك وتعالى اذا قمتم الى الصلوة فاغسلوا وجوهكم وأيد يكم الى المرافق وامسحوا برؤوسكم وارجلكم الى الكعبين اور سید دونوں لفظ یعنی (غسل) اور (مسیح) خاص میں معنی معلوم کیلئے وضع کئے گئے ہیں۔ اگر ہم اس کے ساتھ ساتھ ان چاروں چیزوں کی شرط لگا ئیں تو یہ ان کے لئے بیان تو بن نہیں سکتے اس لئے کہ دو تو خود بین نفسہ ہے۔ اس سے کتاب اللہ کا نسخ لازم آئیگا اور کتاب اللہ کا شخ کر ناخبر واحدت جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ہم نے کہا جو کتاب اللہ سے ثابت ہے۔ یعنی فسل اعضاء اور سح وہ فرض ہے اور جو کچھ حدیث سے ثابت ہے یعنی ولاء ترتیب اور تسمیہ وغیرہ وہ سنت ہے الجماع -
His saying: 'And the condition of continuity, order, naming (Bismillah), and intention in the verse of wudu is invalid.' (2) Second branch: According to us, making wala (continuity), tartib (order), tasmiyah (saying Bismillah), and niyyah (intention) conditions in wudu is invalid; rather, these things are sunnah. While Imam Malik says that wala – i.e., washing the limbs in such a way that one limb does not become dry before washing the next – is a condition. His proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) persisted in it. Imam al-Shafi'i says that niyyah and tartib are conditions. For tartib, his proof is the hadith: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a person who does not observe order in washing the limbs' – as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said. And for niyyah, the hadith: 'Actions are but by intentions' – i.e., the correctness of all deeds depends on intentions. The Zahiris say that tasmiyah is a condition for wudu; their proof is the hadith: 'No wudu for the one who does not mention Allah's name.' Our proof is that Allah Almighty commanded us in wudu to wash and wipe, as Allah, Blessed and Exalted, said: 'When you rise for prayer, wash your faces and your hands to the elbows, and wipe over your heads and your feet to the ankles.' And both words, i.e., 'ghusl' (washing) and 'mash' (wiping), are khas placed for a known meaning. If we make these four things conditions along with them, then they cannot become an explanation for them, because they are [the conditions] themselves clear. This would necessitate naskh (abrogation) of the Book of Allah, and abrogating the Book of Allah with a khabar wahid is not permissible. Therefore, we say: What is established from the Book of Allah, i.e., washing the limbs and wiping, is fard; and what is established from hadith, i.e., continuity, order, and naming, etc., is sunnah. [And the matter ends with] 'al-jama'' [consensus?].
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents the second branch (furu') illustrating the usul principle that khas does not accept bayan. The issue is whether certain conditions are necessary (fard/condition) in wudu: wala (continuity without drying), tartib (order), tasmiyah (saying Bismillah), and niyyah (intention). The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa and his school) is that these are not conditions; they are sunnah. Other schools differ: Imam Malik holds wala as a condition; Imam al-Shafi'i holds tartib and niyyah as conditions; the Zahiris hold tasmiyah as a condition. The Hanafi proof: The Quranic verse of wudu (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) commands washing (ghusl) and wiping (mash). These words are khas – they have clear, specific meanings (washing and wiping). If we add conditions like continuity, order, intention, or tasmiyah as obligatory, that would amount to adding a condition (shart) that is not part of the original khas command. Since khas does not accept bayan (explanatory addition) from a khabar wahid, such addition would actually be an abrogation (naskh) of the Quranic ruling, which is impermissible via khabar wahid in Hanafi usul. Hence, the acts commanded in the Quran (washing and wiping) remain fard, while the additional details from hadith (wala, tartib, tasmiyah, niyyah) are sunnah – recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala): Continuity in washing the limbs so that no limb becomes dry before the next is washed.
ترتیب (tartib): Order in washing the limbs as mentioned in the Quran (face, hands, wipe head, feet).
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' at the start of wudu.
نیت (niyyah): Intention (to perform wudu for prayer or worship).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul argument in this passage, why are wala, tartib, tasmiyah, and niyyah not considered conditions in wudu?
A) Because all authentic hadith regarding them are weak.
B) Because the Quranic command to wash and wipe is khas, and adding conditions via khabar wahid would be naskh, which is impermissible.
C) Because the Quran explicitly says these are not required.
D) Because there is a consensus (ijma) that they are not conditions.

Key Takeaway
The khas principle protects Quranic commands from being overwritten by khabar wahid; therefore, additional conditions from hadith are sunnah, not fard.

Hanafi Usul: Why Additional Conditions Cannot Be Obligatory in Wudu
Hanafi refutation using usul principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that khabar wahid cannot abrogate the Quran to evaluate whether an extra condition derived from a hadith can be obligatory.

Core Idea
The Quranic command is clear; adding conditions would abrogate it, but a solitary hadith cannot abrogate the Quran.

This passage presents a foundational Hanafi usul argument: the Quranic verse on wudu uses specific terms (ghusl and mash) that are already clear. Any attempt to make additional conditions obligatory from hadith would require changing the Quranic ruling, which is naskh. Since khabar wahid cannot abrogate the Quran, such conditions can only be sunnah. This lesson unpacks that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and its nature
Locate the Quranic verse (5:6) that commands washing and wiping. Recognize that it is a clear, specific command (khass) with no ambiguity.
2
Classify the key terms as khass and mubayan
The words 'ghusl' and 'mash' are placed for known meanings – they are specific and self-evident. No additional explanation (bayan) is needed.
In Hanafi usul, a text that is mubayan cannot be subject to further bayan; any extra requirement would be a change (naskh).
3
Understand why adding a condition would be naskh, not bayan
If we add a condition like niyyah or tartib, we are altering the original ruling. Since the original is clear, this is abrogation (naskh), not mere explanation (bayan).
4
Recall the Hanafi principle on naskh by khabar wahid
Hanafi usal holds that khabar wahid (solitary hadith) cannot abrogate the Quran. Only Quran or mutawatir sunnah can abrogate.
This is a key difference from Shafi'i usul, which allows khabar wahid to specify the Quran.
5
Conclude that the hadiths can only establish sunnah
Since the hadiths (e.g., about niyyah, tartib) cannot abrogate, they cannot make these actions obligatory. They remain sunnah, based on prophetic practice but not at the level of fard.
Wisdom: This preserves the primacy of the Quranic text while honouring the Sunnah.

His statement: And the condition of wala', tartib, tasmiyah, and niyyah in the verse of wudu is invalid.
(2) Second branch: According to us, making wala', tartib, tasmiyah, and niyyah conditions in wudu is invalid; rather these things are sunnah. Our proof is that Allah has commanded us to wash and wipe in wudu, as Allah the Exalted said: 'O you who believe, when you rise to prayer, wash your faces and your hands up to the elbows, and wipe over your heads and your feet up to the ankles.' The end.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the conditions of wudu. The author presents the Hanafi position that wala' (continuous washing), tartib (order), tasmiyah (mentioning Allah's name), and niyyah (intention) are sunnah, not fard or shart. The opposing views: Imam Malik makes wala' a condition based on the Prophet's continuous practice. Imam al-Shafi'i makes niyyah and tartib conditions, citing hadiths. The Zahiris make tasmiyah a condition from a hadith. The Hanafi response is grounded in usul: the Quranic verse (5:6) uses the specific terms ghusl and mash, which are clear and self-sufficient. Adding extra conditions would either be a bayan (which is impossible as the terms are mubayan) or would abrogate the Quran. Since khabar wahid cannot abrogate the Quran (a Hanafi usul principle), the additional conditions cannot be obligatory. Hence they are sunnah, based on hadith but not at the level of fard. This exemplifies the Hanafi rule that amm in the Quran is qat'i, and hadith ahad cannot restrict or abrogate it.

Key Terms
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith reported by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation
بيان (bayan): Explanation of a mujmal or specific ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul argument in this lesson, why can the additional conditions (wala', tartib, etc.) not be obligatory?
A) Because they contradict the Quran
B) Because the hadiths are weak
C) Because the Quranic terms are khass and making them conditions would abrogate the Quran, which khabar wahid cannot do
D) Because the Prophet never performed them

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the clarity of the Quranic text (bayān) prevents addition by khabar wahid; such addition would be naskh, which is impermissible.

Wudu Conditions: Comparing Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, and Zahiri Views
Multi-madhhab dispute on wudu conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast the Hanafi position on wala', tartib, tasmiyah, and niyyah with the positions of other madhahib, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds wala', tartib, tasmiyah, and niyyah as sunnah; other schools make some of them conditions, changing the validity of wudu.

In this lesson, we examine the specific conditions disputed in wudu: continuous washing (wala'), order (tartib), basmalah (tasmiyah), and intention (niyyah). The Hanafi school argues they are sunnah, while Malik, Shafi'i, and the Zahiris consider some or all as obligatory. The usul basis is the same as in the previous lesson, but here we focus on the practical fiqh application and the evidence from hadith.

Guided Path
1
List the four disputed conditions and their proponents
Identify each condition and which school makes it a shart (condition) versus sunnah.
Wala' is shart for Malik; tartib and niyyah are shart for Shafi'i; tasmiyah is shart for Zahiris.
2
State each school's ruling on each condition
For each school, state clearly whether the condition is obligatory (fard/shart) or recommended (sunnah).
Hanafi: all four are sunnah. Maliki: wala' is wajib. Shafi'i: niyyah and tartib are wajib. Zahiri: tasmiyah is wajib.
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
For each disputed condition, state what happens if a person omits it according to each school.
E.g., Hanafi: wudu is valid but makruh tanzihan; Shafi'i: wudu is invalid if niyyah or tartib is omitted.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the opposing proofs
Understand why the Hanafis do not accept these conditions as obligatory. The key is that the Quranic verse is sufficient and clear, and hadith cannot abrogate it.
Refer to the usul principle from Lesson 1.
5
Apply the thamarah to a practical scenario
Given a specific scenario of omission, determine the validity of wudu according to each school.
For example, a person performs wudu without saying bismillah.

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the conditions of wudu. The author presents the Hanafi position that wala' (continuous washing), tartib (order), tasmiyah (mentioning Allah's name), and niyyah (intention) are sunnah, not fard or shart. Adding extra conditions would either be a bayan (which is impossible as the terms are mubayan) or would abrogate the Quran. Since khabar wahid cannot abrogate the Quran (a Hanafi usul principle), the additional conditions cannot be obligatory. Hence they are sunnah, based on hadith but not at the level of fard. This exemplifies the Hanafi rule that amm in the Quran is qat'i, and hadith ahad cannot restrict or abrogate it.

Key Terms
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith reported by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation
بيان (bayan): Explanation of a mujmal or specific ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a direct consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the Hanafi position that niyyah is sunnah for wudu?
A) Wudu without niyyah is invalid
B) Wudu without niyyah is valid but makruh tanzihan
C) Wudu without niyyah is valid but must be repeated
D) Niyyah is irrelevant and makes no difference

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard (from Quran) and sunnah (from hadith) in wudu, affecting validity and compensation.

The Hanafi Usul Argument Against Making Wudu a Condition for Tawaf
Hanafi usul argument against making wudu a condition for tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a khass text is self-evident and cannot be subject to bayan, and evaluate the Shafi'i argument from the hadith 'Tawaf is prayer'.

Core Idea
A khass (specific) Quranic text is self-evident; adding a condition via a khabar wahid would be naskh, not bayan.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the obligation of wudu in tawaf. The Hanafis rely on the Quranic word 'tawaf' being khass (specific) and self-evident, while the Shafi'is cite a hadith analogizing tawaf to prayer. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi usul principles protect the clarity of nusus from being qualified by zanni evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and conflicting positions
State the dispute: does wudu become a condition (shart) for tawaf? The Shafi'i position says yes; the Hanafi says no, it is only wajib.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith 'Tawaf around the House is prayer' (al-tawaf bil-bayti salat). Analyze how this hadith creates an analogy between tawaf and prayer, implying wudu is required.
The hadith is a khabar wahid (zanni al-thubut).
3
Apply the Hanafi textual analysis
Classify the word 'tawaf' in the Quran as khass (specific, self-evident). In Hanafi usul, khass is bayyin bi nafsihi and cannot be subject to bayan (clarification) because it is already clear.
Adding a condition would not be bayan but naskh (abrogation), which is impermissible from a zanni source.
4
Explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis argue that making wudu a condition for tawaf would require abrogating the clear Quranic text, which cannot be done by a khabar wahid. The hadith is interpreted to indicate wujub (obligation) of taharah, not shartiyyah.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shafi'i hold tawaf invalid without wudu; Hanafi hold tawaf valid but requiring dam (sacrificial penalty) for leaving a wajib.
This exemplifies the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والطهارة في اية الطواف
تیسری تفریح
امام شافعی کے نزدیک بیت اللہ شریف کے طواف میں وضو شرط ہے۔ دلیل یہ حدیث ہے کہ حضور اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بیت اللہ شریف کا طواف کرنا نماز ہے، اور جس طرح نماز بغیر وضو کے صحیح نہیں اسی طرح طواف بھی بغیر وضو کے صحیح نہیں ہوگا۔ الفاظ حدیث یہ ب الطواف بالبيت صلوة
احناف کی دلیل ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کلام پاک میں دلیل فو ا کے الفاظ میں کا مادہ احتفاق طواف لفظ خاص ہے جس کا معنی گھومنا ہے اور حرم کعبہ کے ارد گرد چکر لگانا ۔ اگر ہم اس خاص میں طہارت کی شرط لگا ئیں تو یہ اس کے لئے بیان تو ہین نہیں سکتا کیونکہ وہ بین بنفسہ ہے بلکہ اس کا منسوخ ہونا لازم آئیگا اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ہم نے کہا کہ نفس طواف تو فرض ہے لیکن طواف کے موقع پر طہارت واجب ہے۔ وجوب کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ اس کے چھوڑنے سے طواف کرنے والے پر دم واجب ہوتا ہے۔
His statement: And taharah in the verse of tawaf.
Third branch: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, wudu is a condition for tawaf of the Holy House. His proof is the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer.' Just as prayer is not valid without wudu, tawaf also will not be valid without wudu. The wording of the hadith: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer.' The Hanafi proof: we say that in the clear speech [Quran], the word 'tawaf' is a specific (khass) word meaning 'to go around' and 'to circumambulate the Kaaba'. If we make taharah a condition for this specific word, it cannot be a bayan because it is already self-evident; rather it would necessitate abrogation, and that is not permissible. Therefore we say: the tawaf itself is fard, but taharah at the time of tawaf is wajib. The consequence of wajib is that leaving it renders a dam (sacrificial penalty) obligatory upon the one performing tawaf.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the obligation of wudu in tawaf. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that tawaf is like prayer, based on a hadith, and thus requires wudu as a condition. The Hanafi response uses a textual analysis: the word 'tawaf' in the Quran (e.g., Surah Al-Hajj 22:29) is khass, meaning 'to circumambulate'. Since it is specific and self-evident (mubayan), adding taharah as a condition would either be a bayan (which is unnecessary since the word is clear) or an abrogation (naskh) — the latter is impermissible especially by a khabar wahid. Therefore, the Hanafis conclude that tawaf itself is fard (obligatory) but wudu for it is only wajib. The practical difference: if one performs tawaf without wudu, the tawaf is valid but a dam (penalty of sacrificing an animal) becomes required. This ruling exemplifies the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial penalty (usually a sheep) for leaving a wajib in Hajj/Umrah.
بين بنفسه (bayyin bi nafsihi): Self-evident, clear without need for explanation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Tawaf is valid but a dam is required.
C) Tawaf is valid without any penalty.
D) Tawaf is valid but prayer is not accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes fard from wajib: tawaf is fard, wudu is wajib; omission of wajib incurs dam, not invalidity.

The Meaning of 'Quru': Hayd or Tuhur?
Hanafi interpretation of 'quru' as hayd in iddah verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the meaning of 'quru' in the iddah verse and explain the usul basis for interpreting it as khass.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school interprets 'quru' as hayd because it is khass (specific) and cannot be reinterpreted without naskh.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul dispute: what does 'quru' mean in Surah Al-Baqarah 228? Imam Abu Hanifa and the Hanafis maintain it means 'hayd' (menstruation), while Imam al-Shafi'i interprets it as 'tuhur' (purity). The divergence is not merely lexical; it reflects different usul methodologies regarding the categorization of words (khass vs. mushtarak) and the weight given to textual specification over contextual inference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that 'quru' in the verse refers to menstruation (hayd). This leads to the iddah being three menstrual cycles.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that 'quru' means purity periods (tuhur). He bases this on the phrase 'li'iddatihinna' which he interprets as indicating time – divorce occurs during tuhur, so iddah should be counted in tuhur.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafis point to the word 'thalathata quru'' – the number 'three' is a specific (khass) word. According to Hanafi usul, khass is qat'i (definitive) and cannot be reinterpreted without naskh (abrogation).
The Hanafis consider 'quru' itself as khass for hayd, as it is derived from 'qar'a' (to gather) referring to the gathering of blood.
4
Understand the usul principle
The Hanafi principle is that if a word is khass, it is binding in its specific meaning. Reinterpreting it would be a form of tampering (naskh), which is impermissible without clear evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi iddah is three menstrual cycles, which is typically shorter than three purity periods, as purity periods include the menstruation days. This affects the waiting period for remarriage.
Shafi'i iddah is longer because three purity periods require waiting for the end of menstruation each time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والتاويل بالاطهار في آية التربص چوتھی تفریح :
قرآن کریم میں مطلقہ کی عدت کے بیان میں ثلاثہ قروء کے الفاظ آئے ہیں امام شافعی کے نزدیک قروه سے مراد طہر ہے ان کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فطلقو من لعدتهن کہ اس میں الام وقت کیلئے ہے طلاق کا وقت تو بالاتفاق طہر ہے تو عدت کا وقت بھی طہر ہونا چاہئے ۔ امام صاحب رحمہ اللہ اور جمیع احناف فرماتے ہیں کہ قروہ سے مراد حیض ہے۔ ہماری دلیل آیت قرآنی (والمطلقات يتربصن بأنفسهن ثلاثة قروء ) من مذکور لفظ ثالثہ ہے کہ یہ خاص لفظ ہے اور معنی معلوم کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور وہ ہے ، افوق الاثنين اور مادون الابعہ اس لفظ خاص میں زیادتی اور نقصان کا احتمال نہیں ہے جب کہ اگر ہم
His statement: And interpretation of taharah in the verse of waiting period.
Fourth branch:

His proof is the verse: 'Divorce them for their iddah' — here 'li' indicates time; the time of divorce is agreed upon to be tuhur, so the time of iddah should also be tuhur. Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) and all Hanafis say that 'quru' means hayd (menstruation). Our proof is the Quranic verse: 'And divorced women shall wait for themselves three quru'' — the mentioned word is 'thalathah', which is a specific (khass) word placed for a known meaning, and that is 'above two' and 'below ten'. This specific word does not admit increase or decrease. Meanwhile, if we...
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the meaning of 'quru' in Surah Al-Baqarah 228. Imam al-Shafi'i interprets it as 'tuhur' (period of purity) based on the phrase 'li'iddatihinna' in the same verse, arguing that divorce is given during tuhur, so iddah should be counted in tuhur. The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, holds that 'quru' means hayd (menstruation). The Hanafi proof is textual: the word 'thalathah' (three) is a number qualifying 'quru'. The word 'quru' in Arabic is a plurale tantum; the Hanafis argue that it is khass, meaning specifically 'menstrual periods', because the word is derived from qar'a (to gather) referring to the blood. The number 'three' also indicates that it is a known, specific count. They argue that if 'quru' meant tuhur, then the iddah would be counted in tuhur intervals, which would make the iddah much longer and inconsistent. The passage is cut off, but the Hanafi reasoning is that the word is khass and cannot be reinterpreted without naskh.

Key Terms
قروء (quru): Plural of qar'; Hanafi: menstrual periods; Shafi'i: purity periods between menses.
خاص (khass): A word with a specific, non-probabilistic meaning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of 'quru' as hayd is based on the usul principle that the word is khass, making its meaning definitive and not subject to reinterpretation.

Hanafi Usul: The Dispute over Quru' in the Idda Verse
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over interpreting quru' in idda verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument that the specific term 'thalatha' (three) requires quru' to mean menstruation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument regarding the lam in 'li'iddatihinna'.

Core Idea
The specific term 'three' (khass) cannot be violated; thus quru' must mean menstruation.

This lesson delves into a classic usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the interpretation of 'quru'' in the Qur'anic verse on idda. The Hanafi school uses a principle of specific terms (khass) to argue that 'quru'' must mean menstruation, while the Shafi'i school relies on a contextual reading of the preposition 'lam'. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi usul prioritizes precise textual wording over contextual inference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the two positions: Hanafi says quru' means hayd (menstruation); Shafi'i says quru' means tahr (purity). Note the practical difference: Hanafi idda is three menstruations; Shafi'i idda is three purifications (two menstruations in between).
2
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof is the lam in 'li'iddatihinna' (so divorce them for their idda). They interpret lam as indicating time (li al-waqt), meaning the time of divorce (which is a state of purity) should be the starting point for counting idda. Understand this temporal interpretation.
The lam is a preposition; its meaning is crucial.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof using khass
The Hanafi proof is the word 'thalatha' (three) in the verse. They classify it as a specific term (khass) that cannot accept increase or decrease. If quru' meant purity, then counting three purities would either require counting the purity of divorce (exceeding three) or not counting it (falling short of three), both violating the specific number three.
Khass is qat'i in Hanafi usul; it cannot be overridden without a clear specifier.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the lam argument
The Hanafi response reinterprets the lam as for reason (li al-ta'lil), not time. The verse means: 'Divorce them in a way that facilitates their idda' – i.e., in a purity without intercourse, so pregnancy is not ambiguous. This interpretation avoids the contradiction with the specific term 'three'.
This is a classic example of prioritizing a specific term over a contextual inference.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and the objection about plural minimum
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is the number of periods counted. The text also addresses an objection: could the plural minimum (three) be used to argue the same? The response shows that plural can sometimes apply to less than three, as in the Hajj verse, so the stronger argument is the specificity of 'three' itself.
This nuance shows the depth of Hanafi usul reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اس میں الام وقت کیلئے ہے طلاق کا وقت تو بالاتفاق طہر ہے تو عدت کا وقت بھی طہر ہونا چاہئے ۔ امام صاحب رحمہ اللہ اور جمیع احناف فرماتے ہیں کہ قروہ سے مراد حیض ہے۔ ہماری دلیل آیت قرآنی (والمطلقات يتربصن بأنفسهن ثلاثة قروء ) من مذکور لفظ ثالثہ ہے کہ یہ خاص لفظ ہے اور معنی معلوم کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور وہ ہے ، افوق الاثنین اور مادون الابعہ اس لفظ خاص میں زیادتی اور نقصان کا احتمال نہیں ہے جب کہ اگر ہم طہر مراد لیس تو یا زیادتی ہوئی یا کمی ہوگی اس لئے کہ جس طہر میں طلاق دی ہے اگر ہم اس کو شمار نہ کر میں تو زیادتی ہوگی کہ مین طبر مستقل اور طہر کا کچھ حصہ وہ ہے جس میں طلاق دی گئی اگر ہم اس طہر کو شمار کرنے میں تو ثلاثہ کے لفظ خاص پر عمل نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ ظاہر ہے کہ جس طہر میں طلاق دی ہے اس کا کچھ نہ کچھ حصہ گذر ہی گیا ہے دونوں صورتیں خرابیوں کو مستلزم ہیں اول کی صورت میں عورت پر عدت کو طویل کرنا لازم آتا ہے جبکہ دوسری صورت میں کتاب اللہ کے خاص ثلاثہ کے مقتضی' پر عدم عمل لازم آتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ قروء سے طہر مراد لینا درست نہیں ہے، اس لئے حیض مراد لیا جائے گا کیونکہ اگر قروء سے حیض مراد لیں تو ثلاثہ سے کم ہوگا نہ زیادہ۔ بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی پر اعتراض کرنے کے لئے لفظ ثلاثہ کی ضرورت نہیں بلکہ یہ اعتراض تو لفظ قردہ سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ ثلاثہ جمع کا لفظ ہے اور اقل جمع تین ہوتا ہے لیکن یہ بات صحیح نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ بعض اوقات جمع کا اطلاق تین سے کم پر بھی کیا جاتا ہے۔ جیسے الحج اشهر معلومات یہاں اشہر صیغہ جمع ہے حالانکہ حج کے مہینے تین نہیں بلکہ دو مہینے اور دس دن ہیں ۔ امام شافعی کو جواب امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ( لعد تھن ) میں لام وقت کیلئے نہیں بلکہ لام تعلیل کیلئے ہے۔ یعنی ان کو طلاق دو اس طریقے سے کہ ان کے لئے عدت کا گزارنا بآسانی ممکن ہو۔ اور یہ اس طرح ہوگا کہ ایسے طہر میں طلاق دی جائے کہ جس میں ولی نہ کی ہو کیونکہ اگر ایسے طہر میں طلاق دے کہ جس میں ولی کی ہے تو پتہ نہیں چلے گا کہ یہ حاملہ ہے یا نہیں اور اس کی عدت وضع حمل ہے یا تین قروء اور عدت کا شمار مشکل ہو جائے گا، اسی طرح حیض میں بھی۔ طلاق نہ دی جائے۔
He said: And interpretation by purity in the verse of waiting. Fourth issue: In the Qur'an, regarding the idda of divorced women, the words 'three quru'' appear. According to Imam Shafi'i, 'quru'' means purity. His proof is the verse: 'So divorce them for their idda' – the 'lam' indicates time; the time of divorce is unanimously purity, so the time of idda should also be purity. Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) and all Hanafis say that 'quru'' means menstruation. Our proof is the Qur'anic verse: 'And divorced women shall wait three quru'' – the word 'three' is a specific term (khass) placed for a known meaning, which is above two and below four. In this specific term, there is no possibility of increase or decrease. If we take purity as meaning, then either increase or decrease occurs: because if we do not count the purity in which divorce was given, there is increase (since that purity would be separate); if we count that purity, then the specific term 'three' is not observed because part of that purity has already passed. Both scenarios entail problems: in the first, the woman's idda would be prolonged; in the second, the specific 'three' of the Book of Allah is not acted upon. So it is known that taking 'quru'' as purity is not correct; therefore, it must be taken as menstruation, because if 'quru'' means menstruation, there is no increase or decrease from three. Some say that for objecting to Imam Shafi'i, the word 'three' is not necessary; rather, the objection could be from the word 'quru'' itself because 'three' is a plural word and the minimum of plural is three. But this is not correct because sometimes the plural is applied to less than three, as in 'Hajj is in well-known months' (al-Hajj ash-hurun ma'lumat) – 'ashhur' is plural, yet the months of Hajj are not three but two months and ten days. Response to Imam Shafi'i: The proof of Imam Shafi'i is answered by saying that the 'lam' in 'li'iddatihinna' is not for time but for reason (lil-ta'lil), meaning 'divorce them in a manner that they can easily complete their idda.' This is achieved by divorcing in a purity in which no intercourse occurred, because if divorced in a purity with intercourse, it would be unclear whether she is pregnant; her idda might be delivery or three quru', making counting difficult. Similarly, do not divorce during menstruation.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute over the interpretation of 'quru'' in the Qur'anic verse on idda (Surah al-Baqarah 2:228). The Shafi'i position takes 'quru'' as purity (tahr), using the lam in 'li'iddatihinna' as temporal, implying that the idda period should be counted from a state of purity. The Hanafi position takes 'quru'' as menstruation (hayd). The Hanafi argument uses a usul al-fiqh principle: the word 'three' (thalatha) is a specific term (khass); interpreting it as purity would lead to either expanding or contracting the number of periods, violating the specificity. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof reinterprets the lam as causal rather than temporal, focusing on the ease of determining the idda. Additionally, the text addresses a potential objection regarding the minimum of plural, citing the example of 'ashhur' (months) in the Hajj verse. This is a classic example of Hanafi textual analysis prioritizing the precise meaning of a specific term (khass) over contextual interpretation.

Key Terms
قروء (quru'): Plural of qur'; disputed meaning: Hanafi: menstruation; Shafi'i: purity.
خاص (khass): A specific term with a precise, unchangeable meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because purity cannot be counted accurately.
B) Because the word 'three' is a specific term and applying it to purities would either exceed or fall short.
C) Because the hadith explicitly says quru' means menstruation.
D) Because the verse uses the word 'quru'' in the plural.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the definitive nature of the specific term 'three' over contextual inferences, establishing that 'quru'' must mean menstruation in the idda verse.

The Hanafi Proof for Transfer of Ownership in Theft
Responding to Shafi'i objection about Quranic proof for transfer of ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the absolute is intended for the complete individual to the word 'jaza' in the theft verse and derive the ruling that amputation alone suffices without compensation.

Core Idea
The word 'jaza' in the theft verse proves amputation is complete recompense, eliminating the need for compensation.

In this lesson, we examine a classic usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the implications of the theft verse (Quran 5:38). The Hanafi school argues that the word 'jaza' (recompense) indicates that amputation alone is sufficient punishment, transferring the sanctity of the stolen property to Allah. The Shafi'i school objects, leading to a detailed linguistic and juristic analysis. By understanding this dispute, you will see how absolute language in the Quran is interpreted in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on transfer of ownership
The Hanafis hold that the sanctity (ismah) of the stolen property is voided from the owner and transferred to Allah, but ownership remains. Therefore, the property is returned if still existent, but no monetary compensation (daman) is due from the thief.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: practical consequence of the dispute.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i objects that the verse only commands amputation ('faqta'u') and does not imply transfer of sanctity. Requiring compensation remains valid.
The Shafi'i rely on the specific command of cutting, not on the word 'jaza'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: reliance on 'jaza'
The Hanafis respond that they do not use 'faqta'u' but the word 'jaza' (recompense) from the same verse. In Hanafi usul, when 'jaza' is used absolutely in punishments, it refers to the complete recompense due to Allah's right.
The word 'jaza' is a maf'ul mutlaq, from the root meaning 'to suffice'.
4
Apply the principle of al-mutlaq yuhmalu 'ala al-fard al-kamil
The absolute word 'jaza' is interpreted to mean the perfect individual (al-fard al-kamil), i.e., the complete punishment. Thus, amputation alone fulfills the recompense, and no additional compensation is needed.
This principle is a qa'ida in Hanafi usul: the absolute, when absolutely mentioned, is intended for the complete individual.
5
Derive the practical consequence
The ruling: amputation is sufficient; the thief is not liable for monetary compensation (daman) even if the stolen property is consumed. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The Shafi'i position, in contrast, holds that amputation does not preclude compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالی کی طرف ۔ گویا کہ چور نے جرم اللہ تعالی کی عصمت میں کیا ہے اور اللہ تعالیٰ کو ضمان اور جرمانے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اب آئیے اصل اعتراض کی طرف۔ اعتراض پھر آپ یہ کیوں کہتے ہیں کہ اگر مال موجود ہو تو اس مال مسروق کو مالک کی طرف واپس کیا جائے گا ؟ اعتراض مذکور کا احناف کی طرف سے جواب اسکا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ مال کی عصمت باطل ہوگئی ہے لیکن مالک کی ملکیت تو باقی ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ مام شافعی کا اعتراض ۔ امام شافیتی اعتراض کرتے ہیں کہ چوری کے باب میں آیت سرقہ سے استدلال کیا جاتا ہے یعنی ( السارق والسارق فاقطعوا اید معھما ) سے اور فاقطعوا کا مادہ اعتقاق قطع لفظ خاص ہے جو معنی معلوم کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے یعنی ہاتھ کو گھٹے سے جدا کرنا لیکن یہ لفظ اس بات پر دلالت نہیں کرتا کہ مال کی عصمت مالک سے باطل ہو کر اللہ تعالی کی طرف منتقل ہو گئی ۔ اگر تم ایسا کہتے ہو تو یہ کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی ہے جواب:۔ اسکا جواب یہ ہے ہم عصمت کے باطل ہونے کیلئے استدلال ( فاقطعوا ) سے نہیں کرتے بلکہ (جزاء ( سے کرتے ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ جزاء کا لفظ جب مطلقا عقوبات کے بیان میں آتا ہے تو اس سے مراد وہ جزاء ہوتی ہے جو اللہ تعالٰی کے حق کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اور اللہ تعالی کے حق کی وجہ سے یہ جزا وتب ہوگی جب یہ جرم اللہ تعالٰی کی عصمت میں ہوا ہو ۔ اس جواب کی ضمن میں چند اور نکات بھی بیان کئے گئے ہیں جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ آیت میں لفظ ( جزاء کو مطلق ذکر کیا گیا ہے تو جزاء سے مراد جزائے کامل ہوگی اور وہ صرف قطع ہے ضمان کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور جزاء سے جزائے کامل مراد لینے کیلئے قاعدہ مسلمہ ہے المطلق از اطلق مراد به الفرد الکامل، اور مزید یہ کہ ( جزاء مفعول مطلق ہے جزی یجزی سے ہے اسکا معنی ہے ( کافی ہو جاتا ) تو گویا کہ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ نہیں سزا کافی ہے ضمان کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اگر قطع ید کے ساتھ ساتھ منعمان [؟ضمان] بھی واجب کر دی جائے تو ( جزاء ) بمعنی کلی کاج مقتضی باطل ہو جائے گا
Towards Allah. It is as if the thief committed the crime in the sanctity of Allah the Exalted, and Allah the Exalted has no need for compensation or fine. Now come to the original objection. Objection: Why do you say that if the stolen property still exists, it should be returned to the owner? Answer from the Hanafis: The answer is that although the sanctity of the property has been voided, the ownership of the owner remains, therefore it is necessary to return it. Objection of Imam Shafi'i: Imam Shafi'i objects that in the chapter of theft, the verse of theft is used as evidence, i.e., 'The thief, male and female, cut off their hands.' The root of 'faqta'u' is 'qata'a', a specific word placed for a known meaning, i.e., severing the hand from the wrist. But this word does not indicate that the sanctity of the property is voided from the owner and transferred to Allah. If you say so, it is an addition to the Book of Allah. Answer: The answer is that we do not use 'faqta'u' to prove the voiding of sanctity, but rather 'jaza' (recompense). Because the word 'jaza' when used absolutely in the context of punishments refers to that recompense which is obligatory due to the right of Allah. And this recompense and punishment will occur when the crime is against Allah's sanctity. Within this answer, a few other points are also explained, the summary of which is that the word 'jaza' in the verse is mentioned absolutely, so the complete recompense is meant, and that is only amputation, no need for compensation. To take the complete recompense from 'jaza', the established principle is 'the absolute, when mentioned absolutely, is intended for the complete individual'. Moreover, 'jaza' is an absolute object from 'jaza yajzi', meaning 'sufficient', so it indicates that the punishment is sufficient, no need for compensation. If along with amputation, compensation is also made obligatory, then the meaning of 'jaza' as complete sufficiency would be invalidated.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi response to a Shafi'i objection regarding the proof for transfer of ownership in theft. The Shafi'i argument is that the Quranic verse 'cut off their hands' only specifies amputation and does not imply that the stolen property's sanctity (ismah) transfers from the owner to Allah, thus the requirement of returning the property remains. The Hanafi response clarifies that they do not rely on the word 'faqta'u' for the transfer of sanctity but on the word 'jaza' (recompense) in the same verse. In Hanafi usul, the word 'jaza' when used absolutely in punishments refers to the complete recompense due to Allah's right, and that complete recompense is amputation alone without compensation. They support this with the principle that the absolute (mutlaq) is intended for the perfect individual (al-fard al-kamil). Additionally, they parse 'jaza' as an absolute object (maf'ul mutlaq) from the root meaning 'to suffice', indicating that the punishment is sufficient and no compensation is needed. The passage thus defends the Hanafi position that in theft, the property's sanctity is voided and transferred to Allah, but ownership remains, so the property is returned to the owner without the thief being liable for compensation. This is a classic Hanafi usul argument using Quranic text and linguistic principles.

Key Terms
جزاء (Jazā’): Recompense, specifically in the context of punishment; when absolute, it implies the complete recompense due to Allah's right.
عصمت (‘Iṣmah): Sanctity or inviolability; here it refers to the legal protection of property from being taken without compensation.
ضمان (Ḍamān): Financial compensation or liability for loss.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi proof for transfer of ownership in theft relies on the absolute word 'jaza' in the verse, which, by usul principle, indicates complete recompense, making amputation sufficient without compensation.

Minimum Mahr and the Dispute on 'Farad' in Quran 33:50
Presents Hanafi ruling and Shafi'i dispute on minimum mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi istinbat chain to derive the minimum mahr from Quran 33:50, hadith, and qiyas, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on textual categories.

Core Idea
The word 'farad' in Quran 33:50 is specific for estimation, not obligation, and the minimum mahr is 10 dirhams.

In this lesson, we examine a classical usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is over the minimum mahr. The core of the dispute turns on the interpretation of the word 'farad' in Quran 33:50 and its legal implications. You will learn how the Hanafis use linguistic precision, hadith, and qiyas to establish a fixed minimum, while the Shafi'is argue for no minimum based on context and transitivity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Determine what exactly is being disputed: the existence and amount of a minimum mahr. The Hanafis say mahr has a minimum of 10 dirhams; the Shafi'is say there is no minimum.
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence
Study the Hanafi proof from Quran 33:50, where 'faradna' is interpreted as 'We have estimated', along with the hadith 'No mahr less than ten dirhams' and the qiyas on cutting the hand for theft.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection
Understand the Shafi'i claim: 'farad' in the verse means obligation (ijab) because it is transitive with 'ala', and the context refers to maintenance, not mahr.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafis respond: the transitivity is due to inclusive meaning, and a second 'faradna' is implied for maintenance. The first 'faradna' means estimation.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi law, a nikah with mahr less than 10 dirhams is valid but the wife is entitled to the minimum; under Shafi'i, any amount is valid without minimum.

Source Text

ہمارے نزدیک مہر کا نفس وجوب صرف نکاح کرنے سے آجائیگا اور وجوب دو چیزوں سے آئیگا یا تو دلی سے یا موت ہے۔
ہماری دلیل اللہ تعالی کا یہ فرمان ہے (واحل لكم ما وراء الكم.... الخ ) یہاں پر (یا) لفظ خاص ہے جو معنی معلوم کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے یعنی (الصاق) جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تمہارا بیویوں کو تلاش کرنا تمہارے مالوں سے ملصق ہونا چاہئے ۔ بعض نے کہا کہ اگلا لفظ تبتغوا ہے جس کا مادہ احتفاق ابتغاء لفظ خاص ہے اس کا معنی ہے طلب دونوں صورتوں میں معنی یہ بنتا ہے کہ عورتوں کو تلاش کرنا مہر سے ملصق ہونا چاہئے ۔ اول تو مہر کو لفظوں میں ذکر کرے اگر ایسا نہیں کرتا تو کم از کم ذمے میں تو واجب ہونا چاہئے ۔ لیکن یہ ساری تفصیل اس وقت ہے جب کہ نکاح صحیح ہو اگر نکاح فاسد ہوتو بالاتفاق ولی سے مہر واجب ہو گا اسی طرح اگر عورت کو اجارہ یا متعہ کے ساتھ حاصل کرتا ہے تو بھی مہر واجب نہیں ہوگا ۔
قوله : وكان المهر مقدرا شرعاً غير مضاف الى العبد ساتویں تفریح :
امام شافع کے نزدیک مہر کی کوئی مقدار مقرر نہیں بلکہ جو چیز ثمن بنے کی صلاحیت رکھے وہ مہر بنے کی بھی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک اکثر کی کوئی مقدار نہیں لیکن اقل کی تعداد مقرر ہے جو دس درہم ہے ہم اللہ تعالی کے اس قول سے استدلال کرتے ہیں قد علمنا ما فرضنا.... الخ (فرض ) لفظ خاص ہے جو معنی معلوم کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور وہ ہے تقدیر اسی طرح فرضنا میں (ن) ضمیر متکلم بھی خاص ہے اور فرض کی اسناد متکلم کی طرف کرنا بھی خاص ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ اللہ تعالی کے علم میں مہر کی مقدار مقرر ہے البتہ اس مقدار متعینہ میں اجمال تھا جس کو حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے لا مهر اقل من عشرة دراهم میں بیان فرمایا ۔
مزید دلائل احناف یہ ہیں کہ احناف اس کو قیاس کرتے ہیں قطع ید پر جب ہاتھ کاٹنے کیلئے مال مسروقہ کی کم ازکم دس درہم مالیت کی مقدار ضروری ہے تو بضع کے مالک بنے کیلئے بھی دس درہم ضروری ہونے چاہیں۔
آگے صاحب کتاب نے وضاحت فرمائی ہے کہ (فرض) کے معنی کے ضمن میں جو کچھ ہم نے بیان کیا ہے وہ فقہا کی اصطلاح میں ہے جبکہ لغت میں فرض کا معنی ہے ایجاب اور قطع ۔ اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہاں ایجاب والا معنی مراد ہے اور اس پر دو قرینے ہیں ایک تو یہ کہ فرض کو متعدی کیا علی کے ذریعے سے کما قال تعالى قد علمنا ما فرضنا علیہم اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ فرض جب متعدی ہو علی کے ساتھ تو اس سے ایجاب والا معنی مراد ہوتا ہے۔ دوسرا قرینہ یہ ہے کہ ملکت ايمانهم کا عطف ( ازواجهم) پر ہے اور لونڈیوں کیلئے تو مہر ہے ہی نہیں بلکہ نفقہ ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں مراد یہ ہے کہ نفقہ واجب ہے بیویوں کے لئے بھی اور لونڈیوں کے لئے بھی ۔ جو کہ قد علمنا ما فرضنا کا تعلق وجوب مهر سے نہیں بلکہ وجوب نفقہ سے ہے۔
احناف کا جواب: ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ علی کے ذریعے سے اس وجہ سے متعدی ہے کہ فرض یہاں پر ایجاب کے معنی کو ضمن ہے اور ملکت ايمانهم سے پہلے دوسرا فرضنا مقدر ہے تو پہلے فرضنا کا معنی ہے قدرنا اور دوسرے فرضنا کا معنی ہے أوجنا۔
According to us, the obligation of mahr arises merely from performing nikah, and the obligation comes from two things: either from consummation or from death. Our proof is Allah's statement: '...and lawful to you are what is beyond that...' (Quran 4:24). Here the letter 'ya' is a specific letter placed for a known meaning, i.e., attachment, the summary of which is that your seeking of wives should be attached to your wealth. Some said that the next word is 'tabtaghu' whose root is 'ibtigha', which is a specific word meaning 'seeking'. In both cases, the meaning is that seeking women should be attached to mahr. First, he should mention mahr in words; if he does not do so, then at least it should be obligatory in his liability. But all this detail is when the nikah is valid; if the nikah is invalid, then by consensus mahr becomes obligatory from him. Similarly, if he obtains a woman through hire or mut'ah, then mahr is not obligatory. His statement: 'And mahr is legally determined, not added to the slave' - seventh branch. According to Imam Shafi'i, mahr has no fixed amount; rather, whatever is capable of being a price, it is capable of being mahr. According to us, there is no fixed maximum, but the minimum is fixed at ten dirhams. We derive proof from Allah's statement: 'We have known what We have prescribed...' (Quran 33:50). The word 'farad' is a specific word placed for a known meaning, which is estimation. Similarly, the 'nun' in 'faradna' is the pronoun of the speaker, which is specific, and attributing the 'farad' to the speaker is also specific. So it is known that in Allah's knowledge, the amount of mahr is fixed; however, there was ambiguity in that specific amount, which the Prophet (peace be upon him) clarified in 'No mahr less than ten dirhams.' Further proofs of the Hanafis: they analogize it to cutting of the hand. When for cutting the hand, the minimum value of stolen goods is ten dirhams, then for owning the private part also ten dirhams should be necessary. Next, the author of the book has clarified that what we have said regarding the meaning of 'farad' is in the terminology of jurists, whereas in language 'farad' means obligation and cutting. Imam Shafi'i says that here the meaning of obligation is intended, and there are two indications: one is that 'farad' is made transitive with 'ala', as Allah said: 'We have known what We have prescribed upon them' (Quran 33:50), and the rule is that when 'farad' is transitive with 'ala', it means obligation. The second indication is that 'what your right hands possess' is conjoined to 'your wives', and for slave women there is no mahr but rather maintenance, so it is known that what is meant here is that maintenance is obligatory for both wives and slave women. Thus the verse 'We have known what We have prescribed' does not relate to the obligation of mahr, but to the obligation of maintenance. The Hanafis' response: We answer that it is made transitive with 'ala' because here 'farad' includes the meaning of obligation, and before 'what your right hands possess' a second 'faradna' is implied. So the first 'faradna' means 'We have estimated' and the second 'faradna' means 'We have obligated.'
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of mahr (dower) in marriage and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the minimum amount. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: mahr becomes wajib upon the valid contract of nikah, and the obligation is confirmed either by consummation (dul) or by death. The proof is derived from the Quranic verse (4:24) where the letter 'ya' or the word 'ibtigha' indicates that seeking women must be attached to mahr, implying that mahr is a necessary condition for marriage. If the nikah is invalid, mahr is still wajib by consensus, but if the woman is obtained through hire (ijarah) or temporary marriage (mut'ah), mahr is not obligatory. The author then moves to the seventh branch: the minimum amount of mahr. The Hanafis hold that while there is no fixed maximum, the minimum is ten dirhams. This is proved by the Quranic verse (33:50) 'We have known what We have prescribed for them' – the word 'farad' here means 'estimation' (taqdir), and the Prophet's hadith 'No mahr less than ten dirhams' clarifies the ambiguous amount. Additionally, the Hanafis use qiyas (analogy) with the cutting of the hand for theft: since the minimum value of stolen goods for amputation is ten dirhams, similarly, the minimum for owning the private part (i.e., mahr) should be ten dirhams. The author then presents the Shafi'i objection: in the Quranic verse, 'farad' means 'obligation' (ijab), not estimation, because it is transitively used with 'ala' (upon), and the context indicates the obligation of maintenance (nafaqa), not mahr. The Hanafi response is that the transitivity with 'ala' is due to the inclusive meaning of obligation, but in the first instance, 'faradna' means 'We have estimated', and a second 'faradna' is implied for the obligation of maintenance. Thus, the verse supports both: estimation of mahr for free women and obligation of maintenance for slave women. The passage is a clear example of inter-madhhab usul dispute, focusing on the interpretation of a Quranic word ('farad') and the application of qiyas.

Key Terms
فرض (fard/farad): In fiqh terminology, estimation (taqdir) of a specific amount; in language, it means obligation (ijab) and cutting.
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife in marriage, obligatory upon valid nikah.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction used to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whether the word 'farad' is ambiguous or specific.
B) Whether 'farad' means estimation or obligation.
C) Whether the verse refers to free women or slave women.
D) Whether the minimum mahr is 10 dirhams or 5 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi minimum mahr of 10 dirhams is derived from a multi-step istinbat: Quran 33:50 (mujmal), hadith (bayan), and qiyas (support), with a careful rebuttal of the Shafi'i linguistic objection.

The Imperative Form and the Negation of Synonymy and Homonymy
Clarifying that the imperative form is exclusively for obligation, addressing synonymy and homonymy issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the imperative form exclusively indicates obligation and identify how the concept of 'lazim musawi' resolves the simultaneous negation of both homonymy and synonymy.

Core Idea
The imperative form is specific to obligation; other meanings are contextual, not inherent.

This passage is a commentary on a matn statement about the imperative form. The author explains that the imperative form is exclusively associated with obligation (wujub). The discussion addresses two linguistic issues: homonymy (ishtirak) where a word has multiple meanings, and synonymy (taraduf) where multiple words share the same meaning. The author argues that the imperative form is specific to obligation, and obligation is understood only through the imperative form, thereby rejecting both homonymy and synonymy. The text also notes that other possible meanings of the imperative (like threat or inability) are not genuine cases but arise from context.

Guided Path
1
State the claim and the two negations
Identify the author's primary claim: the imperative form (صيغة الأمر) is exclusively for obligation (wajib). Recognize that this claim simultaneously negates two concepts: ishtirak (homonymy: the imperative having multiple meanings) and taraduf (synonymy: obligation being expressed by other words).
Note that 'ha' in 'mukhtass' specifies that the imperative is specific to obligation, not vice versa.
2
Analyze the role of 'lazim'
Understand that 'lazim' (necessary concomitant) is used to describe the relationship: obligation is necessary for the imperative. The author discusses two interpretations: lazim aam (broader necessary) and lazim musawi (co-extensive necessary). The preferred interpretation is lazim musawi, which makes the relationship mutual: if obligation is lazim musawi of the imperative, then wherever the imperative appears, obligation is necessarily present, and wherever obligation is intended, only the imperative form can express it. This consistently negates both homonymy and synonymy.
If lazim aam were taken, synonymy would be negated but homonymy would still be possible because the imperative could have other meanings.
3
Address the objections from Quranic examples
Consider the objection that Quranic verses like 'اعملوا ما شئتم' (Do what you will) and 'فأتوا بسورة' (Then bring a surah) use the imperative for threat (tahdid) and challenge (ta'jiz), not obligation. The author responds that these are not genuine 'amr' in the usul sense; they lack the element of isti'la (high status) with binding intent. Genuine amr must include the intention to make the action binding on the addressee, which is absent in threat and challenge.
This preserves the rule that the imperative's literal meaning (haqiqah) is obligation; any other use is metaphorical (majaz) due to contextual overrides.

جواب ..... ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ اس سے اہل اصول والا امر ہی مراد ہے لیکن اس میں مقصد صرف استعا نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مراد ایسی استعلاء ہے جس میں مخاطب پر فعل کو لازم کرنا بھی ہوتا ہے اور یہ بات تہدید اور تنجز میں نہیں پائی جاتی ہے۔
