First Type of Time-Bound Command: Time as Container and Intention of Specification
Ruling on first type of time-bound command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a time-bound command as having time as a container (zarf), apply the condition of niyyat al-ta'yin, and derive that performance specifies the act.

Core Idea
When time is merely a container, intention of specification is required and not dropped; only performance assigns the act to that time.

This lesson examines the first category of time-bound commands in Hanafi usul: where time serves as a container (zarf) for the commanded act. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it affects when intention of specification is required and how the act becomes ascribed to a particular time. The source passage clarifies that even narrow time does not excuse the need for specification, and that specification is only effective through performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category: time as container
Recognize that the first type of al-amr al-muwaqqat is when time does not cause obligation but merely accommodates the act. For example, the five daily prayers have times that are containers; the time itself does not make the prayer obligatory.
2
Extract the ruling: condition of niyyat al-ta'yin
The text states that intention of specification is a condition (shart). Why? Because the time can fit multiple types of prayers (ada, qada, fard, nafl), so intention is needed to specify which act is intended.
The Arabic term is 'niyyat al-ta'yin'.
3
Analyze the exception: narrow time does not drop the condition
Even if time becomes very tight (e.g., only enough time for one prayer before the next), the condition of intention of specification remains. Students often assume it drops, but the text explicitly says 'لا يسقط لضيق الوقت'.
4
Determine how specification is achieved: by performance
The text says 'ولا يتعين بالتعيين إلا بالأداء' — it is not specified by specification (verbal/mental) except by performance. If one intends Dhuhr but prays Asr, it counts as ada of Asr, not qada of Dhuhr.
Performance is the decisive factor.
5
Apply the analogy: oath expiation
The hanith fi al-yamin (one who breaks an oath) may specify one expiation but give another; it is valid. Similarly, the act is defined by actual performance, not prior intention.
This analogy reinforces the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وحكمه اشتراط نية التعيين ولا يسقط لضيق الوقت ولا يتعين بالتعيين الا بالأداء كا لحانث في اليمين . قسم اول کا حکم : امر موقت کی اس پہلی قسم کا حکم یہ ہوا کہ اس میں تعین کی نیت شرط ہے کیونکہ وقت ظرف ہے اور وہ اداء اور قضاء فرض اور نفل سب کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے لہذا نیت کے ساتھ معین کرنا ضروری ہے اور اگر کسی عذر کی وجہ سے وقت تنگ ہو گیا تو بھی نیت تعین ساقط نہیں ہوگی اور کوئی بھی وقت تب ہی معین ہو گا جب اس میں نماز ادا کرے لہذا کسی شخص نے زبان سے یا دل سے ایک وقت کو معین کر لیا لیکن نماز دوسرے وقت میں ادا کی تو وہ نماز ادا ہی شمار ہوگی قضاء نہیں ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ حانث فی الیمین شخص کسی کفارے کو معین کرے لیکن پھر کوئی دوسرا کفارہ دے تو جائز ہے۔
His saying: And its ruling is that intention of specification is a condition, and it is not dropped due to narrowness of time, and it is not specified by specification except by performance, like the one who breaks an oath. The ruling of the first category: The ruling of this first category of time-bound command is that intention of specification is a condition, because the time is a container, and it can accommodate performance, making up, obligatory, and supererogatory. Therefore, specification through intention is necessary. Even if time becomes tight due to some excuse, the intention of specification is not dropped. And no time is specified except when he performs the prayer in it. Thus, if a person specified a time verbally or mentally but performed the prayer in another time, that prayer will count as performance, not make-up. Just as a person who breaks an oath specifies a particular expiation but then gives another expiation, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage discusses the first category of time-bound commands (al-amr al-muwaqqat), where time is merely a container (zarf) for the commanded act. The author explains that in this category, the intention of specification (niyyat al-ta'yin) is a necessary condition. The reason is that the time can accommodate multiple obligations (performance, make-up, obligatory, supererogatory), so intention is needed to specify which act is intended. This intention does not fall away even if the time becomes restrictive, such as when someone delays prayer until the last moment. Furthermore, specification is only effective when the act is actually performed within that time; if one verbally intends a particular time but prays later, the prayer counts as performance (ada'), not make-up (qada'). An analogy is given: a person who breaks an oath may specify one type of expiation but then give another; it is valid because the specification is not binding. This principle is used to explain that the mere intention of a time does not make the prayer a make-up if performed out of that time.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): Intention that specifies which particular act is being performed (e.g., which prayer or which fast).
ظرف (zarf): A container; time that does not cause obligation but merely accommodates the act.
حانث في اليمين (hanith fi al-yamin): One who breaks an oath and must offer expiation (kaffara).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first type of time-bound command, when does the act become specified?
A) When the person verbally specifies the time.
B) When the person intends in his heart.
C) When the person actually performs the act in that time.
D) When the time becomes tight.

Key Takeaway
In the first type of time-bound command (time as container), intention of specification is a condition that is never dropped, and only performance actually specifies the act to that time.

Time as a Standard (Mi'yar) for Obligations: The Case of Ramadan Fasting
Explaining time as a standard and its effect on Ramadan fasts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle that time can serve as a standard (mi'yar) rather than merely a cause (sabab), and apply it to the ruling on intention for Ramadan fasts.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, time as a standard (mi'yar) expands the commanded action with the time, and overrides the need for specific intention.

This passage introduces the concept of time as a standard (mi'yar) for obligations, using Ramadan fasting as the central case. The key distinction is between a cause (sabab), which merely triggers the obligation, and a standard, which defines its scope. The passage then explores the practical consequence: when time is a standard, any intention to fast during Ramadan fulfills the obligation, even if one mistakenly intends a different fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept
What does it mean for time to be a standard (mi'yar)? Contrast with sabab.
Mi'yar defines the extent of the obligation; sabab merely triggers it.
2
Apply to Ramadan
How does the standard nature of Ramadan affect the commanded action (fasting)? Note that fasting occupies the entire day.
The obligation expands with daylight hours.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on sabab
What are the different views on the cause of each day's fast? (whole month, day only, first part, each day).
Hanafis hold each day is the cause for that day's fast.
4
Derive the thamara
What is the practical ruling regarding intention? Why does the Hanafi school hold that no specific intention is required?
Because time as a standard itself specifies the obligation.
5
Evaluate the opposing views
What do Imam al-Shafi'i (specification required) and Imam Zufar (no intention needed) say? How does the Hanafi response rely on the mi'yar concept?
Shafi'i analogizes to prayer; Zufar goes further than Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کیلئے سبب ہو مگر اداء کیلئے شرط نہ ہو چونکہ وقت معیار ہے لہذا وقت طویل ہو گا تو مامور بہ بھی طویل ہوگا اور اگر وقت مختصر ہوگا تو مامور بہ بھی مختصر ہو گا مثلاً روزہ کہ یہ ایسا مامور بہ ہے جس کی ادائیگی میں تمام وقت صبح صادق تا غروب آفتاب مشغول ہوتا ہے ایسا نہیں ہے کہ روزہ ختم کر لینے کے بعد بھی کچھ وقت بچتا ہو اس امر میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے کہ رمضان کے روزوں کے لئے کون سا وقت سبب ہے چنانچہ بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ پورا رمضان سبب ہے اور بعض کہتے ہیں کہ صرف دن سبب ہے اور راتیں سبب نہیں بعض کہتے ہیں رمضان کا پہلا جزء سبب ہے جبکہ بعض کہتے ہیں کہ ہر دن کا شروع کا حصہ سبب ہے۔ بالفاظ دیگر ایک ایک دن ایک ایک روزے کے لئے سبب ہے۔ معیار ہونے کا ثمرہ: چونکہ رمضان کا مہینہ روزوں کیلئے معیار ہے لہذا اس میں فرض روزے کے علاوہ اور کچھ بھی جائز نہیں اس لئے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا اذا انسلخ الشعبان فلا صوم الاعن رمضان اور اس میں تعین شروط نہیں ہے بلکہ مطلقا روزے کا نام لینے سے بھی رمضان ہی کا روزہ ادا ہو گا بلکہ اگر وصف میں خطاء ہو جائے مثلاً واجب کی یا نفلی روزے کی نیت کرے تو بھی رمضان ہی کا روزہ ادا ہو گا۔ امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ نیت کا تعین شرط ہے جیسا کہ نماز میں تعیین شرط ہوتی ہے۔ امام زفر کہتے ہیں کہ نیت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں۔
For something to be a cause but not a condition for performance. Since time is the standard, if time is long, the commanded action is also long; if time is short, the commanded action is also short. For example, fasting, which is a commanded action that occupies all the time from true dawn to sunset; it is not that after finishing the fast some time remains. The imams differ on which time is the cause for the fasts of Ramadan. Some say the whole of Ramadan is the cause, some say only the day is the cause and not the nights, some say the first part of Ramadan is the cause, while some say the beginning portion of each day is the cause. In other words, each day is the cause for one fast. The fruit of being a standard: Since the month of Ramadan is the standard for fasts, therefore in it nothing other than the obligatory fast is permissible, because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'When Sha'ban ends, there is no fasting except for Ramadan.' And in it, specification of intention is not a condition; rather, by absolutely naming the fast, the Ramadan fast is fulfilled. Even if there is an error in description, for example, intending an obligatory or voluntary fast, still the Ramadan fast is fulfilled. Imam al-Shafi'i says that specification of intention is a condition, just as specification is a condition in prayer. Imam Zufar says that intention is not required at all.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the usul principle that time can serve as a standard (mi'yar) for obligations rather than merely a cause (sabab). The discussion focuses on Ramadan fasting. The author first establishes that when time is the standard, the scope of the commanded action expands or contracts with the time. For fasting, the entire daylight period is occupied. The imams differ on what exactly constitutes the cause (sabab) for the obligation of each day's fast: the whole month, each day, the first part, etc. The key consequence (thamara) of time being a standard is that no other fast is valid in Ramadan, as per the hadith. Moreover, no specific intention is required; any intention to fast suffices for the Ramadan fast, even if one mistakenly intends a voluntary or other obligatory fast. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar differ on the necessity of intention specification, but the Hanafi position relies on the standard nature of the time.

Key Terms
معیار (mi'yar): A standard or measure that defines the extent of an obligation; contrasts with 'sabab' which merely triggers the obligation without defining its scope.
سبب (sabab): The cause that brings about the obligation; different views on whether the entire month, each day, or first part is the cause for Ramadan fasts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Specific intention for Ramadan is required
B) One must intend only voluntary fasts
C) Any intention to fast suffices for the Ramadan fast, even if mistakenly for another fast
D) No intention is required at all

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when time is a standard (mi'yar), it defines the obligation's scope and removes the need for specific intention; the obligation is fulfilled by any act within that time.

The Third Division of Time-Bound Commands: Time as Measure Only
Defining the third division and its ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third division of time-bound commands (amr muwaqqat) in Hanafi usul, state its two examples, and explain the required conditions (ta'yin and tabyit) and consequence (no fawt).

Core Idea
When time is only a measure, not a cause, the act requires specification and pre-dawn intention, and can never be missed.

In Hanafi usul, commands tied to time are classified into three categories based on the role of time: cause, measure, or both. The third category is unique: time is merely a measure (miyar) for performance, not the cause (sabab) of obligation. This lesson unpacks that category, its examples, and the practical rulings that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the Arabic phrase 'معياراً لا سبباً' and understand that the third division is where time is a measure but not a cause for obligation.
2
State the examples
Recognize the two examples given: qada' of Ramadan (make-up fasts) and absolute nadhr (unvowed fast without time specification). Explain why each fits: the cause is not the time but the original obligation or the vow itself.
For qada', the cause is the missed Ramadan; for mutlaq nadhr, the cause is the vow, not the particular day.
3
Contrast with first two divisions
Mentally compare: first division (Ramadan) – time is both cause and measure; second division (prayer) – time is measure but cause is the event (e.g., noon). The third division lacks time as cause entirely.
4
Extract the ruling
From the text, identify the two conditions: niyat al-ta'yin (specifying which fast) and tabyit (making intention the night before). Also note that no fawt (irretrievable loss) occurs; every fast is ada'.
Unlike prayer or Ramadan, if delayed, it is still ada' (performance in time), not qada'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله أو يكون معياراً لا سبباً لقضاء رمضان والنذر المطلق

امر مقید بالوقت کی قسم ثالث

امر موقت کی تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ وقت مامور بہ کیلئے معیار ہو لیکن سبب نہ ہو جیسے قضاء رمضان المبارک کیونکہ قضاء کا سبب وہی ہے جو اداء کا سبب ہے لیکن یہ دن قضاء کے روزوں کیلئے معیار ہے اور جیسا کہ نذر مطلق اس کا وقت بھی اس کیلئے معیار ہے لیکن وجوب کیلئے سبب نہیں ہے۔ باقی رہی نذر معین تو بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ بعض احکام میں قضاء رمضان کے ساتھ شریک ہے جیسا کہ وقت کا معیار ہونا اور بعض احکام میں نذر مطلق کے ساتھ شریک ہے جیسا کہ وقت کا وجوب کیلئے سبب نہ ہونا۔ بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ نذر معین رمضان کے ساتھ شریک ہے معیار ہونے اور وجوب کا سبب ہونے میں بھی۔
نکته...... صاحب حسامی رحمہ اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ نذر معین صوم رمضان کی جنس میں سے ہے اسی طرح انہوں نے قضا رمضان اور نذر مطلق کو امر مطلق کی قسم میں سے ذکر کیا ہے نہ امر موقت کی اور انہوں نے اسے زکوۃ اور صدقہ فطر کی قبیل سے شمار کیا ہے اور یہی بات زیادہ درست معلوم ہوتی ہے۔
قوله : وتشترط فيه نية التعيين ولا يحتمل الفوات بخلاف الأولين وكذا يشترط فيه التبييت بخلاف الأولين - قسم ثالث کا حکم :
اس تیسری قسم میں نیت کا تعین بھی شرط ہے اور رات سے نیت کرنا بھی شرط ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے علاوہ باقی تمام دن نفلی روزوں کا احتمال رکھتے ہیں لہذا قضاء اور نذر مطلق کیلئے رات سے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اور اس میں فوت ہونے کا بھی احتمال نہیں ہے بلکہ جب بھی روزہ رکھے گا ادا ہوگا بخلاف پہلی دو قسموں کے یعنی صلوۃ اور صوم کے ان میں فوت ہونے کا احتمال ہے۔ کیونکہ بعد میں قضا ہوگی۔
His statement: 'Or it is a measure (miyar) not a cause (sabab) for qada' of Ramadan and absolute nadhr.'

Third division of time-bound command.

The third division of time-bound command is that the time is a measure for the commanded act but not a cause. For example, qada' of Ramadan, because the cause of qada' is the same as the cause of performance (ada'), but these days are a measure for the fasts of qada'. And like absolute nadhr (nadhr mutlaq): its time is also a measure for it but not a cause for obligation. As for specified nadhr (nadhr mu'ayyan), some say that it shares with qada' of Ramadan in some rulings, such as the time being a measure, and shares with absolute nadhr in some rulings, such as the time not being a cause for obligation. Some say that specified nadhr shares with Ramadan in both being a measure and a cause for obligation.

Note: Sahib Husami (may Allah have mercy on him) said that specified nadhr is of the genus of the fast of Ramadan. Similarly, he mentioned qada' of Ramadan and absolute nadhr as being of the category of absolute command (amr mutlaq) and not time-bound command, and he counted them as being of the type of zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. And this seems more correct.

His statement: 'And intention of specification is required in it, and it does not admit of being missed (fawt), unlike the first two. And likewise pre-dawn intention (tabyit) is required in it, unlike the first two.' - Ruling of the third division:

In this third division, both specification of intention and pre-dawn intention are required because all days other than Ramadan are capable of nafl fasts. Therefore for qada' and absolute nadhr, pre-dawn intention is necessary. And there is no possibility of being missed (fawt) in it; rather whenever he fasts, it will be performed (ada'), unlike the first two divisions, i.e., salat and sawm (Ramadan), in which there is the possibility of being missed. Because later qada' would be required.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of time-bound commands (amr muwaqqat) in Hanafi usul. The first two categories are: (1) time is both a cause and a measure (e.g., Ramadan fast), (2) time is a measure but not a cause (e.g., the five daily prayers: their time is a measure but the cause is not the time itself but the occurrence of the obligation). The third category is that time is a measure but not a cause for the obligation itself. Examples are qada' of Ramadan and absolute nadhr. For qada', the cause is the original obligation (the missed Ramadan), not the day chosen for make-up. For absolute nadhr (a vow without specifying a time), the day on which one fasts is merely the time of performance, not the cause of obligation. The passage discusses controversy over specified nadhr (nadhr mu'ayyan, e.g., 'I will fast on Friday'). Some say it shares attributes with both qada' and mutlaq. Sahib Husami opines it belongs to the genus of Ramadan itself, implying time is both measure and cause. However, the text considers the view that qada' and mutlaq are from absolute command (like zakat) rather than time-bound more correct. The ruling then states that for this third category, both 'niyat al-ta'yin' (specifying which fast) and 'tabyit' (intending the night before) are required, unlike the first two categories (obligatory prayer and Ramadan fast) where intention does not require pre-dawn specification? Actually, for prayer, tabyit is not required because the time is short; for Ramadan, the entire month is a single obligation, so specification is not needed. Additionally, this category does not suffer from 'fawt' (the missed obligation being irretrievable) because even if delayed, it can be performed later as ada' (performance in time), unlike prayer which if missed becomes qada'.

Key Terms
معیار (miyar): The time appointed for the act to be performed, serving as a measure but not the cause of obligation.
سبب (sabab): The cause that makes the act obligatory.
نذر مطلق (nadhr mutlaq): A vow without specifying a time, e.g., 'I vow to fast' without saying when.
نية التعيين (niyat al-ta'yin): Intention that specifies which obligation is being fulfilled, e.g., 'I intend to fast for qada' of Ramadan'.
تبييت (tabyit): Making the intention for a fast during the night (from Maghrib to dawn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two conditions required for fasting in the third division according to the passage?
A) Intention of specification (ta'yin) and pre-dawn intention (tabyit)
B) Only pre-dawn intention
C) Intention of specification and daytime intention
D) No conditions; same as Ramadan

Key Takeaway
In the third division of time-bound commands, time is only a measure, so the act requires two conditions (ta'yin and tabyit) and never admits fawt.

The Intra-Madhhab Dispute: Classification of Specified Nadhr (Nadhr Mu'ayyan)
Intra-madhhab dispute over specified nadhr classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute over the classification of specified nadhr (nadhr mu'ayyan) in Hanafi usul, identify the two competing views, and state the preferred view (Sahib Husami) with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Specified nadhr: is it like Ramadan (time as both measure and cause) or like qada' (time as measure only)? Sahib Husami says the first.

The third division's examples are clear for qada' and absolute nadhr, but there is a disagreement about specified nadhr (e.g., 'I vow to fast on Friday'). This lesson unpacks that intra-madhhab ikhtilaf and explains why the preferred view affects whether tabyit and ta'yin are required for such a fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of dispute
Recognize that the dispute is about specified nadhr (nadhr mu'ayyan): does it belong to the third division (time as measure only) or to the first (time as both measure and cause)?
2
State the first opinion
Some hold that nadhr mu'ayyan shares attributes with both qada' (time is measure) and mutlaq nadhr (time is not cause), placing it ambiguously.
3
State the second opinion (Sahib Husami's)
Sahib Husami argues that specified nadhr is of the genus of Ramadan itself—time is both measure and cause. Thus it belongs to the first division, not the third.
He also reclassifies qada' and mutlaq nadhr as absolute commands (amr mutlaq), like zakat.
4
Identify the preferred view
The text states that Sahib Husami's view is 'more correct' (asahh). Therefore the operative ruling: specified nadhr is like Ramadan.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if specified nadhr is like Ramadan, then tabyit and ta'yin are not required; if it is like the third division, they are required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله أو يكون معياراً لا سبباً لقضاء رمضان والنذر المطلق

امر مقید بالوقت کی قسم ثالث

امر موقت کی تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ وقت مامور بہ کیلئے معیار ہو لیکن سبب نہ ہو جیسے قضاء رمضان المبارک کیونکہ قضاء کا سبب وہی ہے جو اداء کا سبب ہے لیکن یہ دن قضاء کے روزوں کیلئے معیار ہے اور جیسا کہ نذر مطلق اس کا وقت بھی اس کیلئے معیار ہے لیکن وجوب کیلئے سبب نہیں ہے۔ باقی رہی نذر معین تو بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ بعض احکام میں قضاء رمضان کے ساتھ شریک ہے جیسا کہ وقت کا معیار ہونا اور بعض احکام میں نذر مطلق کے ساتھ شریک ہے جیسا کہ وقت کا وجوب کیلئے سبب نہ ہونا۔ بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ نذر معین رمضان کے ساتھ شریک ہے معیار ہونے اور وجوب کا سبب ہونے میں بھی۔
نکته...... صاحب حسامی رحمہ اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ نذر معین صوم رمضان کی جنس میں سے ہے اسی طرح انہوں نے قضا رمضان اور نذر مطلق کو امر مطلق کی قسم میں سے ذکر کیا ہے نہ امر موقت کی اور انہوں نے اسے زکوۃ اور صدقہ فطر کی قبیل سے شمار کیا ہے اور یہی بات زیادہ درست معلوم ہوتی ہے۔
قوله : وتشترط فيه نية التعيين ولا يحتمل الفوات بخلاف الأولين وكذا يشترط فيه التبييت بخلاف الأولين - قسم ثالث کا حکم :
اس تیسری قسم میں نیت کا تعین بھی شرط ہے اور رات سے نیت کرنا بھی شرط ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے علاوہ باقی تمام دن نفلی روزوں کا احتمال رکھتے ہیں لہذا قضاء اور نذر مطلق کیلئے رات سے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اور اس میں فوت ہونے کا بھی احتمال نہیں ہے بلکہ جب بھی روزہ رکھے گا ادا ہوگا بخلاف پہلی دو قسموں کے یعنی صلوۃ اور صوم کے ان میں فوت ہونے کا احتمال ہے۔ کیونکہ بعد میں قضا ہوگی۔
His statement: 'Or it is a measure (miyar) not a cause (sabab) for qada' of Ramadan and absolute nadhr.'

Third division of time-bound command.

The third division of time-bound command is that the time is a measure for the commanded act but not a cause. For example, qada' of Ramadan, because the cause of qada' is the same as the cause of performance (ada'), but these days are a measure for the fasts of qada'. And like absolute nadhr (nadhr mutlaq): its time is also a measure for it but not a cause for obligation. As for specified nadhr (nadhr mu'ayyan), some say that it shares with qada' of Ramadan in some rulings, such as the time being a measure, and shares with absolute nadhr in some rulings, such as the time not being a cause for obligation. Some say that specified nadhr shares with Ramadan in both being a measure and a cause for obligation.

Note: Sahib Husami (may Allah have mercy on him) said that specified nadhr is of the genus of the fast of Ramadan. Similarly, he mentioned qada' of Ramadan and absolute nadhr as being of the category of absolute command (amr mutlaq) and not time-bound command, and he counted them as being of the type of zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. And this seems more correct.

His statement: 'And intention of specification is required in it, and it does not admit of being missed (fawt), unlike the first two. And likewise pre-dawn intention (tabyit) is required in it, unlike the first two.' - Ruling of the third division:

In this third division, both specification of intention and pre-dawn intention are required because all days other than Ramadan are capable of nafl fasts. Therefore for qada' and absolute nadhr, pre-dawn intention is necessary. And there is no possibility of being missed (fawt) in it; rather whenever he fasts, it will be performed (ada'), unlike the first two divisions, i.e., salat and sawm (Ramadan), in which there is the possibility of being missed. Because later qada' would be required.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of time-bound commands (amr muwaqqat) in Hanafi usul. The first two categories are: (1) time is both a cause and a measure (e.g., Ramadan fast), (2) time is a measure but not a cause (e.g., the five daily prayers: their time is a measure but the cause is not the time itself but the occurrence of the obligation). The third category is that time is a measure but not a cause for the obligation itself. Examples are qada' of Ramadan and absolute nadhr. For qada', the cause is the original obligation (the missed Ramadan), not the day chosen for make-up. For absolute nadhr (a vow without specifying a time), the day on which one fasts is merely the time of performance, not the cause of obligation. The passage discusses controversy over specified nadhr (nadhr mu'ayyan, e.g., 'I will fast on Friday'). Some say it shares attributes with both qada' and mutlaq. Sahib Husami opines it belongs to the genus of Ramadan itself, implying time is both measure and cause. However, the text considers the view that qada' and mutlaq are from absolute command (like zakat) rather than time-bound more correct. The ruling then states that for this third category, both 'niyat al-ta'yin' (specifying which fast) and 'tabyit' (intending the night before) are required, unlike the first two categories (obligatory prayer and Ramadan fast) where intention does not require pre-dawn specification? Actually, for prayer, tabyit is not required because the time is short; for Ramadan, the entire month is a single obligation, so specification is not needed. Additionally, this category does not suffer from 'fawt' (the missed obligation being irretrievable) because even if delayed, it can be performed later as ada' (performance in time), unlike prayer which if missed becomes qada'.

Key Terms
نذر معین (nadhr mu'ayyan): A vow specifying a particular time, e.g., 'I vow to fast on Friday'.
نذر مطلق (nadhr mutlaq): A vow without specifying a time, e.g., 'I vow to fast' without saying when.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the preferred view regarding specified nadhr?
A) Tabyit and ta'yin are required for specified nadhr
B) Tabyit and ta'yin are not required for specified nadhr
C) Specified nadhr is invalid
D) Specified nadhr becomes a nafl fast

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view (Sahib Husami) places specified nadhr in the first division (like Ramadan), so tabyit and ta'yin are not required.

The Third Type of Time-Bound Command: Time as Criterion, Not Cause
Defining the third type of time-bound command with examples and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between time as a criterion (miyar) and time as a cause (sabab) in time-bound commands, and identify which acts fall under the third type along with their required conditions.

Core Idea
In the third type of time-bound command, the time validates the act but does not obligate it—so the act is never 'missed' in the sense of requiring qada.

We have previously encountered time-bound commands where the time is either a cause or both cause and criterion. This lesson introduces a third category where the time is merely a criterion, neither causing nor fixing the obligation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings of qada, vows, and the conditions of intention. The passage also presents a scholarly disagreement on whether specified vows belong to this category or to the first type.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sabab and miyar
Identify the core distinction: when the time is a cause (sabab), it triggers the obligation; when it is a criterion (miyar), it only measures the act's validity without causing the obligation.
In usul al-fiqh, this distinction affects whether an act can be 'missed' (fawat) and require qada.
2
Locate the examples
Find the two clear examples given: qada of Ramadan fasts and absolute vows (nadhr mutlaq). Note that for these, the time is only a criterion.
The passage contrasts these with the first two types: prayer (salat) and Ramadan fast, where time is both cause and criterion.
3
Analyze the dispute on specified vow
Identify the difference of opinion: some say specified vow (nadhr mu'ayyan) shares characteristics with qada (time as criterion), others say it is like Ramadan (time as both). Note the author's preference for Sahib Hisami's view that it belongs with Ramadan.
This dispute affects whether specified vows require the same conditions as the third type.
4
Extract the conditions
From the ruling section, extract that the third type requires specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) and night intention (tabayyut). Understand why: because days other than Ramadan can host voluntary fasts, so without specific intention the fast might be intended as voluntary.
These conditions are not required for the first two types (prayer and Ramadan fast).
5
Contrast fawat possibility
Note that the third type has no possibility of being missed (fawat); whenever performed, it is considered ada'. In contrast, missing a prayer or Ramadan fast creates a qada obligation.
The phrase 'la yahtamil al-fawat' is key: the act is always on time when done.

امر مقید بالوقت کی قسم ثالث

امر موقت کی تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ وقت مامور بہ کیلئے معیار ہولیکن سبب نہ ہو جیسے قضاء رمضان المبارک کیونکہ قضاء کا سبب وہی ہے جو اداء کا سبب ہے لیکن یہ دن قضاء کے روزوں کیلئے معیار میں اور جیسا کہ نذر مطلق اس کا وقت بھی اس کیلئے معیار ہے لیکن وجوب کیلئے سبب نہیں ہے باقی رہی نذر معین تو بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ بعض احکام میں قضاء رمضان کیساتھ شریک ہے جیسا کہ وقت کا معیار ہونا اور بعض احکام میں نذر مطلق کے ساتھ شریک ہے جیسا کہ وقت کا وجوب کیلئے سبب نہ ہونا بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ نذر معین رمضان کے ساتھ شریک ہے معیار ہونے اور وجوب کا سبب ہونے میں بھی۔

نکته...... صاحب حسامی رحمہ اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ نذر معین صوم رمضان کی جنس میں سے ہے اسی طرح انہوں نے قضا رمضان اور نذر مطلق کو امر مطلق کی قسم میں سے ذکر کیا ہے نہ امر موقت کی اور انہوں نے اسے زکوۃ اور صدقہ فطر کی قبیل سے شمار کیا ہے اور یہی بات زیادہ درست معلوم ہوتی ہے۔

قوله : وتشترط فيه نية التعيين ولا يحتمل الفوات بخلاف الاولين وكذا يشترط فيه التبييت بخلاف الاولين - قسم ثالث کا حکم :

اس تیسری قسم میں نیت کا تعین بھی شرط ہے اور رات سے نیت کرنا بھی شرط ہے کیونکہ رمضان کے علاوہ باقی تمام دن نفلی روزوں کا احتمال رکھتے ہیں لہذا قضاء اور نذر مطلق کیلئے رات سے نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اور اس میں فوت ہونے کا بھی احتمال نہیں ہے بلکہ جب بھی روزہ رکھے گا ادا ہوگا بخلاف پہلی دو قسموں کے یعنی سلوۃ اور صوم کے ان میں فوت ہونے کا احتمال ہے۔ کیونکہ بعد میں قضا شمار ہوگی
Third type of time-bound command: The third type of time-bound command is that the time is a criterion for the commanded act but not a cause, such as the qada of the blessed Ramadan, because the cause of qada is the same as the cause of performance, but these days are a criterion for the fasting of qada. And similarly, for an absolute vow, its time is also a criterion for it but not a cause for obligation. As for the specified vow, some say that it shares with qada Ramadan in some rulings, such as the time being a criterion, and with absolute vow in others, such as the time not being a cause for obligation. Some say that the specified vow shares with Ramadan in being both a criterion and a cause for obligation. Note: Sahib Hisami (may Allah have mercy on him) said that the specified vow is of the genus of the fast of Ramadan. Similarly, he mentioned qada Ramadan and absolute vow in the category of absolute command, not time-bound. And he counted them in the category of zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. And this appears more correct. His statement: 'And it requires specific intention and cannot be missed, unlike the first two, and similarly it requires night intention, unlike the first two.' Ruling of the third type: In this third type, specific intention is required and night intention is also required because all days other than Ramadan are capable of voluntary fasts. Therefore, for qada and absolute vow, night intention is necessary. And there is no possibility of being missed; rather, whenever he fasts, it will be performed, unlike the first two types, i.e., prayer and Ramadan fast, in which there is a possibility of being missed because later it will be counted as qada.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage explains the third type of time-bound command (amr muwaqqat). The author defines it as a command where the time serves as a criterion (miyar) for the act but not as a cause (sabab) for the obligation itself. Examples given: qada (make-up) of Ramadan fasts, and absolute vows (nadhr mutlaq). The key distinction is that the time is necessary for the act to be valid but does not independently obligate it. The passage then discusses a difference of opinion regarding specified vows (nadhr mu'ayyan): some consider them similar to qada in that time is a criterion, while others include them with absolute vows in that time is not a cause. A note from Sahib Hisami reclassifies specified vows as akin to Ramadan fasts (i.e., time-bound and cause), and places qada and absolute vows in the category of absolute commands (like zakat). The author prefers this view. The ruling section then clarifies the conditions for this third type: specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) and night intention (tabayyut) are required, unlike the first two types (prayer and Ramadan fast). The third type cannot be missed (la yahtamil al-fawat) – meaning if delayed, it does not become qada but is still performed when done. This contrasts with obligatory prayers and Ramadan fasts, which if missed become qada. The rationale: any day other than Ramadan can accommodate voluntary fasts, so without specific intention one might intend voluntary; hence intention must specify qada or vow. Night intention ensures the fast is tied to the specific day.

Key Terms
معیار (miyar): A criterion or standard; in this context, the time is a measure for the act but not the cause of obligation.
نذر مطلق (nadhr mutlaq): An absolute vow, not specified to a particular time; its performance is required but not tied to a specific time as a cause.
نذر معین (nadhr mu'ayyan): A specified vow, tied to a particular time (e.g., a specific day); there is a dispute whether the time is a cause or only a criterion.
فوات (fawat): The concept of an act being 'missed' such that it becomes qada; the third type has no possibility of fawat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true about the third type of time-bound command (qada of Ramadan and absolute vow)?
A) It can be missed and become qada.
B) It requires specific intention and night intention.
C) The time is both cause and criterion.
D) It does not require intention.

Key Takeaway
In the third type of time-bound command, the time is a criterion only, so the act never goes into 'missed' status; it is always performed as ada' when done, but requires specific and night intention to distinguish it from voluntary acts.

Definition and Division of Nahy (Prohibition)
Defines nahy and divides it into qabih li-aynihi and qabih li-ghayrihi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nahy (prohibition), distinguish between qabih li-aynihi and qabih li-ghayrihi, and classify examples of prohibited acts according to the Hanafi usul framework.

Core Idea
Nahy always implies the act is evil, but that evil may be inherent or due to external factors.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, nahy (prohibition) is a key type of khass (specific) textual address. Just as a command (amr) implies goodness, a prohibition necessarily implies evilness (qabah) in the prohibited act. However, not all prohibited acts are inherently evil; some become evil only because of external circumstances. This lesson unpacks the definition of nahy and its classification, supported by a Quranic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of nahy
In the source text, locate the linguistic definition of nahy: a demand to abstain issued in a superior manner ('Do not do'). Note that the demand must be from a superior to an inferior.
2
Analyze the necessitation of evilness
The text states that nahy necessarily implies the attribute of evilness (qabah) for the prohibited act, due to the wisdom of the Prohibitor (Allah). Find the Quranic proof cited: 'He prohibits immorality and evil' (Surah al-Nahl: 90). Understand how this verse supports the claim.
The proof is qat'i in transmission (Quran) but zanni in indication (dalala), as the verse does not explicitly state that every prohibition involves evilness; it only shows that Allah prohibits evil.
3
Distinguish between qabih li-aynihi and qabih li-ghayrihi
The passage divides nahy into two main types based on the source of evilness. Qabih li-aynihi: the act is evil in itself, either rationally (wad'an) or legally (shar'an). Qabih li-ghayrihi: the act becomes evil due to an external attribute (wasfan) or adjacency (mujawiran). Study the examples provided.
For qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan, the attribute that causes evilness is connected to the act but not part of its essence (e.g., time, place). For mujawiran, the act is permissible in itself but leads to something haram.
4
Apply the classification to examples
Given a specific prohibited act, determine whether it falls under qabih li-aynihi (and its subtype) or qabih li-ghayrihi. Use the criteria: Is the act inherently evil (reason or sharia says so)? Or does it become evil because of an external factor?
Example: lying is qabih li-aynihi wad'an (reason deems it evil). Prayer at prohibited times is qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan (the act itself is good, but the time makes it evil).
5
Recognize the Hanafi position on the implications of nahy
Understand that in Hanafi usul, nahy necessitates immediate and repeated abstention, and the prohibited act is considered haram. However, if there is evidence that the prohibition is not absolute (e.g., for guidance rather than obligation), the ruling may be different.
This is a foundational point: not every 'do not' in the Quran is a prohibition of obligation; it could be a prohibition of dislike (karaha) or guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نہی کی بحث
قوله : ومنه النهى وهو قوله على سبيل الاستعلاء لا تفعل
نہی کی تعریف:
خاص کی ایک اور قسم نہی ہے
قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء لا تفعل یعنی کہنے والے کا دوسرے کو اپنے آپ کو بڑا سمجھتے ہوئے کہنا کہ یہ نہ کر ۔
قوله وانه يقتضى صفة القبح للمنهى عنه ضرورة حكمة الناهي
:
پھر جیسے مامور یہ کیلئے حسن کا تقاضا ضروری ہوا کرتا ہے اس طرح نہی بھی منہی عنہ کیلئے قبیح کا تقاضا کرتی ہے کیونکہ ناہی حکیم ہے اور حکیم ذات اس چیز سے منع کرتی ہے جو قبیح اور شنیع ہو کما قال تعالى وينهى عن الفحشاء والمنكر
قوله : اما أن يكون قبيحاً لعينه وذلك نوعان وضعاً وشرعاً أو لغيره وذلك نوعان وصفاً ومجاوراً
نہی کی تقسیم
پھر قبح کے اعتبار سے نہی کی دو قسمیں ہیں: (۱) قبیح لعینہ (۲) قبیح لغیرہ پھر قبیح لعینہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) قبیح وضعا اور (۲) قبیح شرعاً کیونکہ اس میں قبح یا تو وضعا ہو گا یعنی عقل اس میں قبح کا تقاضا کرتی ہوگی ۔ یا قبح شرعا یعنی عقل تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کام کو جائز قرار دیدے لیکن شریعت اس سے روکتی ہے۔
Discussion of Nahy
His statement: 'And from them is nahy, and it is one's statement in a superior manner: 'Do not do.''
Definition of Nahy:
Another type of khass is nahy. It is the speaker's statement to someone else in a superior manner: 'Do not do this,' i.e., the speaker says to the other while considering himself superior: 'Do not do this.'
His statement: 'And it necessitates the attribute of evilness for the prohibited act, due to the necessity of the wisdom of the prohibitor.'
Then, just as a command necessitates goodness for the commanded act, similarly nahy necessitates evilness for the prohibited act, because the prohibitor is wise, and a wise being prohibits only what is evil and abominable, as Allah Almighty said: 'And He prohibits immorality and evil.'
His statement: 'It is either evil in itself, and that is of two types: by agreement and by divine law, or evil due to something else, and that is of two types: by attribute and by adjacency.'
Division of Nahy:
Then, according to evilness, nahy is of two types: (1) evil in itself, and (2) evil due to something else. Then, evil in itself is of two types: (1) evil by agreement (rational) and (2) evil by divine law (shar'), because in it, evilness is either by agreement, i.e., reason requires its evilness, or evilness by divine law, i.e., reason may deem the act permissible, but the sharia prohibits it.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage commences the topic of nahy (prohibition) in usul al-fiqh. It first defines nahy: it is a demand to abstain issued from a superior to an inferior, using the phrase 'Do not do.' The author then states that nahy necessarily implies that the prohibited act is evil (qabih), just as amr (command) implies goodness (husn). This is because the Lawgiver (al-Nahi) is wise and only prohibits what is evil. A Quranic proof is given: 'He prohibits immorality and evil' (Surat al-Nahl: 90).
The passage then divides nahy into two main categories:
1. Qabih li-aynihi (evil in itself): The act is inherently evil, regardless of external factors. This is further subdivided into:
   a. Qabih wad'an (by rational agreement): Reason independently judges the act as evil, e.g., lying, injustice.
   b. Qabih shar'an (by divine law): Reason does not necessarily see the act as evil, but the sharia prohibits it, e.g., drinking grape juice after it becomes wine; reason may allow it, but sharia forbids it.
2. Qabih li-ghayrihi (evil due to something else): The act becomes evil because of an external circumstance or attribute. This is subdivided into:
   a. Qabih wasfan (by attribute): The act is evil due to an attribute that departs from the norm, e.g., prayer at prohibited times.
   b. Qabih mujawiran (by adjacency): The act becomes evil due to its connection with something else, e.g., selling grapes to a wine-maker.
This classification is foundational for understanding how prohibitions are analyzed in legal theory.

Key Terms
نہی (nahy): A demand to abstain from an act, issued from a superior to an inferior
قبیح لعینہ (qabih li-aynihi): An act that is evil in itself, regardless of external factors
قبیح لغیرہ (qabih li-ghayrihi): An act that becomes evil due to an external attribute or adjacency

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification of nahy, how is 'prayer during the prohibited times' categorized?
A) Qabih li-aynihi wad'an
B) Qabih li-aynihi shar'an
C) Qabih li-ghayrihi wasfan
D) Qabih li-ghayrihi mujawiran

Key Takeaway
Nahy (prohibition) in Hanafi usul always implies the evilness of the prohibited act, which may be inherent (qabih li-aynihi) or due to external factors (qabih li-ghayrihi).

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Sensory vs Legal Acts and the Effect of Prohibition
Defines two types of acts and how nahy applies to each

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sensory (fi'l hissi) and legal (fi'l shar'i) acts, and apply the Hanafi rule that prohibition on legal acts invalidates an attribute (fath li-ghayrih) unless evidence indicates otherwise.

Core Idea
Prohibition on a legal act invalidates its attribute, not its essence—otherwise prohibition becomes negation.

In Hanafi usul, the categories of sensory and legal acts are foundational for understanding how prohibitions affect validity. This lesson unpacks those definitions and then walks through the rational proof that distinguishes the two, culminating in a key dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of acts
Read the definitions of fi'l hissi and fi'l shar'i. Note that sensory acts (like murder, adultery) have meanings unchanged by revelation, while legal acts (like prayer, sale) have meanings defined or altered by Shari'ah.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi usul.
2
State the default rule for nahy on each category
Prohibition on a sensory act invalidates the act itself (fath li-'aynih). Prohibition on a legal act invalidates an attribute (fath li-ghayrih) unless a specific evidence says otherwise.
Examples for legal acts: sale of mudamin, prayer with hadath.
3
Understand the Hanafi rational proof
Nahy requires the person to have ability/choice (ikhtiyar). If prohibition on a legal act invalidated the essence, it would negate that ability, turning nahy into nafy (negation), which is impossible. So the invalidity must be on an attribute that preserves the essence's permissibility.
This is a qiyas khafi argument.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both types invalidate the substance. He argues that ugliness (qubh) is established by implication (iqtida') and does not nullify the implicator.
The Hanafi response: rejecting the implication because it would negate the required ability.
5
Apply the rule to examples
In the sale of mudamin, the Hanafis rule it invalid due to an attribute (uncertainty) unless evidence shows it is invalid per se. The Shafi'is rule it invalid per se. Know the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
This example appears in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
افعال حسیہ کی تعریف: اس سے مراد وہ افعال ہیں جن کے معانی شریعت سے پہلے بھی معلوم ہوں اور اب بھی وہ اپنے اسی معنی پر قائم ہوں جیسے قتل، زنا، شرب خمر۔ افعال شرعیہ کی تعریف: افعال شرعیہ وہ ہیں جن کی اصلی معانی شریعت کے آنے کے بعد بدل گئے ہوں جیسے صوم، صلوۃ اور بیع وغیرہ۔ جب نہی افعال حسیہ سے آئی ہو تو وہ صحیح تعینہ پر محمول ہوگی اور اگر نہی افعال شرعیہ سے آئی ہو تو وہ فتح لغیرہ وصف پر محمول ہوگی لیکن اگر کوئی دلیل اس کی فتح لعینہ ہونے پر دلالت کرے تو اس کو صبح عید پر محمول کریں گے جیسے مضامین جمع مضمویہ اور ملاقیح (جمع ملقوعہ) کی بیع اور محدث کی نماز۔ قوله: وقال الشافعى رحمه الله فى البابين ينصرف الى القسم الاول. امام شافعی کا مذہب... لیکن امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں بھی افعال شرعیہ اور افعال حسیہ دونوں سے فتح لعینہ پر تمول ہوگی. قوله: لأن القبح يثبت اقتضاء فلا يتحقق على وجه يبطل به المقتضى. احناف کی دلیل ہم کہتے ہیں کہ نھی کا معنی یہ ہے کہ بندے کو اختیار کے باوجود کسی فعل سے روکا جائے لیکن اگر اسے اختیار ہی نہ ہوں تو نہی نفی بن جائیگی جیسے اندھے سے کہا جائے (مت دیکھے)۔ برتن میں پانی نہ ہو اور کہا جائے کہ (مت پی) وغیرہ ذالک من الامثلہ۔ اور ہر چیز میں اسی طرح کا اختیار ہوتا ہے جو اس کے مناسب ہو۔ افعال حسیہ میں اختیار یہ ہے ن مثلاً کسی کام کے کرنے پر قادر ہو اور اسے اس کے کرنے سے رہ جائے اور افعال شرعیہ میں اختیار یہ ہے کہ اس کو شارع کی جانب سے اختیار ہو گویا اس کام کی اجازت بھی ہوگی اور اسی سے بھی بھی ہوگی اور یہ دونوں باتیں اس وقت جمع ہو سکتی ہیں جب ہم یہ کہیں کہ یہ فعل اپنی اصل کے اعتبار سے مشروع ہے اور اپنے وصف کے اعتبار منہی عنہ ہے لیکن اگر ہم یہ کہیں کہ افعال شرعیہ میں نہی ت فتح العد یہ ثابت ہوتا ہے تو اس طرح بندے کے اختیار کو باطل کرنا لازم آئے گا اور نہی نفی بن جائیگی جس کا بطلان محتاج دلیل نہیں۔
Definition of sensory acts: By it is meant those acts whose meanings were known before the Shari'ah and still remain upon that same meaning, such as murder, adultery, drinking wine. Definition of legal acts: Legal acts are those whose original meanings changed after the coming of the Shari'ah, such as fasting, prayer, and sale, etc. When prohibition comes from sensory acts, it will be interpreted upon the substance [being invalid] correctly; and if prohibition comes from legal acts, it will be interpreted upon invalidity due to another attribute. But if there is evidence indicating that it is invalid due to itself, then we will interpret it as invalid due to substance, such as the sale of mudamin, jama' mudmawi, and malaqih (plural of maluqah), and the prayer of a hadath (impure person). His statement: And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, in both categories turns to the first division. Imam Shafi'i's madhhab... But Imam Shafi'i says that for both legal and sensory acts, it will be interpreted as invalidity due to substance. His statement: Because ugliness is established by implication, so it does not occur in a manner that would nullify the implicator. The proof of the Hanafis: We say that the meaning of prohibition is that the servant is restrained from an act despite having ability/choice, but if he has no choice, then prohibition becomes negation, like saying to a blind man 'Do not see'. When there is no water in the vessel and it is said 'Do not drink', etc. from such examples. And every thing has a similar ability that is appropriate for it. In sensory acts, ability is that, for example, he is able to do a task and refrains from doing it; and in legal acts, ability is that he has choice from the side of the Lawgiver, as if there is permission for that act and also [prohibition], and these two matters can be combined when we say that this act is legislated in terms of its essence and prohibited in terms of its attribute. But if we say that in legal acts, prohibition is established upon the substance, then nullifying the servant's choice becomes necessary, and prohibition becomes negation, whose nullity does not need evidence.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary defines two fundamental categories of actions: sensory (hissiyya) and legal (shar'iyya). Sensory actions are those whose meaning is known by natural reason and remain unchanged by revelation, e.g., killing, adultery, drinking wine. Legal actions are those whose meaning is defined or altered by the Shari'ah, such as fasting (sawm), prayer (salat), and sale (bay'). The central rule discussed is how prohibitions (nahy) apply to each type. According to the Hanafis, if a prohibition is on a sensory act, it renders the act itself invalid (fath li-'aynih). If on a legal act, the prohibition renders the act invalid due to an extrinsic attribute (fath li-ghayrih) unless there is evidence to the contrary. Examples where evidence makes a legal act invalid in itself include the sale of mudamin (a type of uncertain sale) and prayer in a state of impurity (hadath). Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that both types of acts, when prohibited, become invalid in themselves (fath li-'aynih). The Hanafis argue that prohibition necessarily implies that the person being prohibited has the ability (ikhtiyar) to perform the act; otherwise the prohibition would become a negation (nafy) — e.g., telling a blind man 'do not see' or telling someone with no water 'do not drink'. For sensory acts, ability means having physical capacity; for legal acts, ability means having legal capacity (i.e., the act is permissible in essence but may be prohibited by an attribute). If prohibition on a legal act were taken as invalidating the essence, it would negate the very ability needed for the prohibition to make sense, thus turning prohibition into negation, which is invalid. Hence, Hanafis maintain the distinction.

Key Terms
فعل حسی (fi'l hissi): An act whose meaning is known by the senses and reason and remains unchanged by revelation.
فعل شرعی (fi'l shar'i): An act whose legal meaning is defined or altered by the Shari'ah.
نہی (nahy): A demand of abstention (kaff) from a person who has the ability to act, otherwise it becomes negation (nafy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, if a prohibition is placed on a legal act (fi'l shar'i), what is the default interpretation?
A) It invalidates the act itself (fath li-'aynih).
B) It invalidates an attribute of the act (fath li-ghayrih).
C) It does not affect the validity of the act.
D) It becomes a negation (nafy).

Key Takeaway
Prohibition on a legal act destroys an attribute, not the essence, because otherwise the necessary ability (ikhtiyar) for prohibition is negated.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Defining 'Aam: The General Term in Hanafi Usul
Defines 'Aam and discusses its exclusions and a Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'Aam as per Hanafi usul, identify exclusions from its definition, and explain the disagreement over istighraq.

Core Idea
Aam inclusively covers all individuals with identical limits — but Hanafis differ on whether comprehensiveness is required.

In Hanafi legal theory, the term 'Aam (general) is a foundational concept for deriving rulings from texts. This passage presents its precise definition and clarifies what is excluded. You will also encounter a subtle disagreement among Hanafi scholars about whether absolute comprehensiveness (istighraq) is a necessary condition. Understanding this definition equips you to correctly identify general terms in the Quran and Hadith and apply the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core components of the definition
The definition states that 'Aam is 'what encompasses individuals that are identical in limits in an inclusive manner.' Break this down: the subject is a word (laft), it encompasses individuals, those individuals share identical limits, and the coverage is inclusive.
The word 'individuals' excludes terms that refer to species or types.
2
Analyze each qualifier and its exclusions
The qualifier 'encompasses individuals' excludes specific terms like 'particular genus' or 'specific individual'. 'Identical limits' excludes homonyms (mushtarak) which cover different meanings. 'Inclusive manner' excludes numbers, which cover parts not individuals.
The commentary also notes that numbers are excluded because they refer to parts, not whole individuals.
3
Examine the exclusion of mushtarak (homonym)
Mushtarak is excluded because it covers multiple meanings (different boundaries) and does so in a substitutive manner, not inclusively. This is a key distinction.
Some scholars argue the 'identical limits' condition alone excludes mushtarak.
4
Understand the disagreement on istighraq (comprehensiveness)
The author of the matn (following Fakhr al-Islam) does not require istighraq as a condition. However, Sadr al-Shariah in al-Tawdih does. This affects whether a nakirah manfiyyah (indefinite negative) is considered 'Aam.
Istighraq means the term must encompass every single individual without exception.
5
Apply the definition to examples
Example: The word 'rijal' (men) is 'Aam because it covers all individuals meeting the condition of being male adults with identical limits. In contrast, 'al-rajul' (the man) is khass (specific). Numbers like 'three' are not 'Aam; they denote parts of a set.
This step solidifies understanding through application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عام کی بحث

قوله : وأما العام فما يتناول أفراداً متفقة الحدود على سبيل الشمول .
عام کی تعریف:
ما يتناول أفراداً متفقة الحدود على سبيل الشمول
ترجمہ: عام وہ لفظ ہے جو علی سبیل الشمول ایسے افراد کو شامل ہو جو متفقہ الحدود ہوں ۔
فوائد محمود :
(ما) یہ جنس ہے اور اس سے مراد لفظ موضوع ہے ۔ یتناول افراد کی قید سے خاص الجنس خاص العین اور خاص النوع نکل گئے۔ اسی طرح اسمائے عدد بھی نکل گئے اسلئے کہ وہ اجزاء کو شامل ہوتے ہیں افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوتے۔ نیز مشترک بھی نکل گیا کیونکہ وہ معانی کو شامل ہوتا ہے افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوتا۔ یا دور ہے کہ متفقة الحدود على سبيل الشمول کی قید صرف عام کی حقیقت بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ البتہ بعض لوگوں نے کہا کہ متفقة الحدود کی قید سے مشترک نکل گیا اس لئے کہ وہ ایسے افراد کو شامل ہوتا ہے جو متفقہ الحدود نہیں ہوتے بلکہ وہ مختلفة الحدود کو شامل ہوتا ہے اور علی سبیل البدلیۃ شامل ہوتا ہے۔
کے مصنف نے عام کی تعریف میں استغراق کی قید علامہ فخر الاسلام کی اتباع کی وجہ سے نہیں لگائی ہے کیونکہ فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک عام میں استغراق شرط نہیں ہے۔ البتہ صاحب توضیح کے نزدیک عام میں استغراق شرط ہے۔ لہذا نکرہ منفیہ عام میں داخل نہ ہوگا۔
Discussion of 'Aam.

His saying: 'As for 'Aam, it is what encompasses individuals that are identical in limits in an inclusive manner.'
Definition of 'Aam:
'What encompasses individuals that are identical in limits in an inclusive manner.'
Translation: 'Aam is a word that inclusively covers such individuals that have consistent boundaries.

Benefits of Mahmud:
(ما) is a genus and by it is meant the lexically assigned word. The restriction 'encompasses individuals' excludes specific genus, specific individual, and specific type. Similarly, numbers are excluded because they encompass parts, not individuals. Also the shared word (mushtarak) is excluded because it encompasses meanings, not individuals. Or it is said that the restriction 'identical in limits in an inclusive manner' is only to express the reality of 'Aam. However, some have said that the restriction 'identical in limits' excludes the shared word because it encompasses individuals that are not identical in limits; rather it encompasses those with different limits and does so in a substitutive manner.

The author did not include the condition of comprehension (istighraq) in the definition of 'Aam due to following Allamah Fakhr al-Islam, because according to him, comprehension is not a condition for 'Aam. However, according to the author of al-Tawdih, comprehension is a condition for 'Aam. Hence, an indefinite noun in a negative context (nakirah manfiyyah) would not be included in 'Aam.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage defines the usul al-fiqh term 'Aam (general). The definition states that 'Aam is a word that comprehensively encompasses all individuals sharing identical boundaries (hudud). The commentary explains the exclusions: (1) 'particular genus, particular individual, particular type' are excluded because they do not encompass multiple individuals; (2) numbers are excluded because they refer to parts, not individuals; (3) the mushtarak (homonym) is excluded because it covers multiple meanings, not individuals. There is a discussion about whether the condition of identical limits excludes mushtarak as well. Finally, it notes a difference among Hanafi scholars: Fakhr al-Islam did not require istighraq (comprehensiveness) as a condition for 'Aam, while the author of al-Tawdih (Sadr al-Shariah) did. Consequently, a nakirah manfiyyah (indefinite noun in negation) is not considered 'Aam according to the latter.

Key Terms
عام ('Aam): A word that encompasses all individuals that share identical boundaries (ḥudūd) in an inclusive manner (ʿalā sabīl al-shumūl).
متفقة الحدود (muttafiqat al-ḥudūd): Individuals that share the same essential defining characteristics or limits, allowing them to be grouped under one general term.
استغراق (istighrāq): The condition that a general term includes every single individual without exception; a point of disagreement between Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Numbers (asmā' al-ʿadad)
C) Khāṣṣ al-jins (specific genus)
D) Nakirah manfiyyah (indefinite negative)

Key Takeaway
'Aam is a word that inclusively covers all individuals sharing identical boundaries; the Hanafi school differs on whether absolute comprehensiveness is required.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Definition of 'Amm and Its Definitive Ruling
Defining 'amm and establishing its definitive ruling against three schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term 'amm (general word) according to the Hanafi school, identify its conditions, and explain why its ruling is definitive (qat'i) against three opposing views.

Core Idea
A general word (amm) in Hanafi usul covers all individuals of a kind with certainty until proven otherwise.

The concept of 'amm (general) is foundational in Hanafi usul, determining how far a ruling extends. This lesson walks through the precise definition, the subtle conditions that exclude specific forms, and then tackles the three rival schools on whether the ruling from a general text is certain or merely probable. Understanding this will sharpen your ability to work with Quranic and hadith texts in deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Deconstruct the Definition
Read the definition: 'amm is a word that comprehensively includes individuals of agreed boundaries. Break down each component: what does 'comprehensively' mean? What are 'agreed boundaries'?
Note that the definition excludes words that refer to parts (like numerals) or different meanings (like mushtarak).
2
Identify What Is Excluded
The commentary explains what is excluded: specific expressions (like proper names), numerals, and common homonyms. Understand why each fails the definition.
Also note the difference between Fakhr al-Islam (who does not require istighraq) and Sahib al-Tawdih (who does) – this affects whether a negative indefinite is considered 'amm.
3
Examine the Three Opposing Schools
The text lists three positions that contradict the Hanafi view. Identify each: (1) 'amm is ambiguous, (2) singular 'amm applies only to one, plural only to three, (3) Shafi'i – 'amm is presumptive. Understand the refutation given by the author.
Focus on the addition of 'qat'an' in the matn as the key refutation.
4
Analyze the Consequence: Abrogation
The passage ends with an example: a general hadith can abrogate a specific one, as in the case of urine of edible animals. This practical consequence demonstrates the strength of 'amm's definitiveness.
This shows that a general ruling can override a specific one if the general is later or stronger.

الحدود ہوں ۔ فوائد محمود : (ما) یہ جنس ہے اور اس سے مراد لفظ موضوع ہے ۔ یتناول افراد کی قید سے خاص الجنس خاص العین اور خاص النوع نکل گئے اسی طرح اسمائے عدد بھی نکل گئے اسلئے کہ وہ اجزاء کو شامل ہوتے ہیں افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوتے نیز مشترک بھی نکل گیا کیونکہ وہ معانی کو شامل ہوتا ہے افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوتا یاد دور ہے کہ متفقة الحدود على سبيل الشمول کی قید صرف عام کی حقیقت بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے البتہ نکرہ منفیہ عام میں داخل نہ ہوگا۔ قوله : وانه يوجب الحكم فيما يتناوله قطعاً عام کے حکم میں مسالک ثلاثہ: عام جن افراد کو شامل ہوتا ہے ان میں حکم کو قطعا ثابت کرتا ہے عام کے حکم کے بارے میں تین مسلک اور ہیں۔ (۱) یہ مجمل ہوتا ہے اس میں توقف کرنا ضروری ہے۔ مصنف نے موجب الحکم کی قید لگا کر اس کی تردید کر دی ہے۔ (۲) یہ کہ عام کا صیغہ اگر مفرد ہو تو صرف ایک فرد میں حکم ثابت ہوگا اور اگر صیغہ جمع ہو تو صرف تین میں حکم کو ثابت کرتا ہے اور باقی میں حکم موقوف ہوگا مصنف نے یتناول افراد کی قید لگا کر اس کی تردید کردی۔ (۳) امام شافعی کا قول ہے کہ عام ظنی ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ ہر عام میں احتمال ہے کہ وہ مخصوص منہ البعض ہو شوافع کا قاعدہ ہے مامن عام الا وقد خص عنه البعض مصنف نے قطعاً کی قید لگا کر اس کی بھی تردید کر دی ۔ اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ احتمال ناش بلا دلیل ہے جس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے قوله : حتى يجوز نسخ الخاص به عام خاص کے لئے ناسخ بن سکتا ہے عام کے حکم پر تفریع یہ اٹھائی ہے کہ عام کیساتھ خاص کو منسوخ کرنا جائز ہے جیسا کہ حدیث عربین جو کہ حضرت انس بن مالک رضی اللہ عنہ سے مروی ہے امام محمد اس حدیث سے استدلال کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ ماکول اللحم یعنی حلال گوشت والے جانوروں کا پیشاب پاک ہے اور اس کا پینا حلال ہے لیکن شیخین کے نزدیک یہ خاص حدیث منسوخ ہے اس عام حدیث سے جس میں حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ( استنز هم من البول فان عامة عذاب القبر منه .... الخ ) پیشاب سے بچو کیونکہ عذاب قبرا اکثر اسی سبب سے ہوتا
His saying: 'And as for al-'amm, it is that which encompasses individuals of agreed boundaries in a comprehensive manner.' Definition of 'amm: that which encompasses individuals of agreed boundaries comprehensively. Translation: 'amm is a word which comprehensively includes such individuals that have agreed boundaries. Beneficial points: (ما) is the genus and by it is meant the meaningful word. The condition 'ytanaawil afraad' (encompasses individuals) excludes specific of genus, specific of individual, and specific of type; similarly, numerals are excluded because they encompass parts, not individuals; also the common (mushtarak) is excluded because it encompasses meanings, not individuals. It is correct that the condition 'differing boundaries comprehensively' is only to describe the reality of 'amm. However, some said that the condition 'agreed boundaries' excludes the common (mushtarak) because it encompasses individuals that are not of agreed boundaries, rather it encompasses individuals of different boundaries, and it does so in an alternative manner. The author did not include the condition of istighraq (exhaustiveness) in the definition of 'amm due to following 'Allamah Fakhr al-Islam, because according to Fakhr al-Islam, istighraq is not a condition in 'amm. However, according to Sahib al-Tawdih, istighraq is a condition in 'amm, so a negative indeterminate noun (nakirah manfiyyah) would not be included in 'amm. His saying: 'And that it establishes the ruling definitively in what it encompasses.' The three schools regarding the ruling of 'amm: 'amm establishes the ruling definitively in the individuals it includes. There are three schools regarding the ruling of 'amm. (1) It is ambiguous (mujmal) and one must pause. The author refutes this by including 'establishes the ruling' (yojib al-hukm). (2) If the form of 'amm is singular, it establishes the ruling only for one individual; if plural, only for three, and for the rest the ruling is suspended. The author refutes this by including 'encompasses individuals' (yatanaawil afraad). (3) Imam al-Shafi'i said that 'amm is presumptive (zanni) because every 'amm has the possibility of being specified from it partially. The Shafi'i principle is 'there is no general statement except that part of it has been specified.' The author refutes this by including 'definitively' (qat'an). And we say: this possibility is unknown without evidence, which is not to be considered. His saying: 'So that abrogation of the specific by it is permissible.' The implication of the ruling of 'amm is that abrogating the specific by it is permissible, like the hadith of 'urbayn (donkey urine) narrated from Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him). Imam Muhammad argues from this hadith that the urine of halal-meat animals is pure and drinking it is permissible. But according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), this specific hadith is abrogated by the general hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Protect yourself from urine, for indeed the general punishment of the grave is from it...' etc.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage defines 'amm (general term) in Hanafi usul and establishes its definitive (qat'i) ruling. The author begins by presenting the definition: 'amm is a word that comprehensively includes individuals that share common boundaries (متفقة الحدود). The commentary explains that 'amm is a genus noun meaning a word placed to indicate individuals, not parts or meanings. This excludes specific expressions (like proper names), numerals, and ambiguous common words (mushtarak). The condition 'individuals of agreed boundaries' is explained to exclude words that refer to different entities (like المشترک) because those do not have consistent boundaries. The author did not include the condition of istighraq (exhaustive coverage) following Fakhr al-Islam, who did not require it in 'amm, unlike Sahib al-Tawdih who does. Hence, some forms like نكرة منفیة (negative indefinite) may not be considered 'amm according to the latter. Next, the passage discusses the three schools on the ruling of 'amm: (1) One view says 'amm is ambiguous (mujmal) and one must pause; this is refuted by stating that 'amm establishes the ruling (یوجب الحکم). (2) Another view says 'amm singular establishes only one individual, plural only three; refuted by 'encompasses individuals' (یتناول افراد). (3) The Shafi'i view that 'amm is presumptive (ظنی) because every 'amm has the possibility of being specified; this is refuted by emphasizing that the ruling is definitive (قطعا), and the mere possibility without evidence is disregarded. The Hanafi position is one of certainty for 'amm until evidence of specification appears. Finally, the passage illustrates that a general statement can abrogate a specific one, citing the example of the hadith about urine of edible animals (ماکول اللحم). Imam Muhammad held that such urine is pure based on a specific hadith, but the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) considered this specific hadith abrogated by the general command to avoid urine (استنز هم من البول). This demonstrates that a later general text may abrogate an earlier specific one, provided the general is stronger or later in revelation.

Key Terms
عام (‘āmm): A word that comprehensively includes individuals of agreed boundaries.
قطعاً (qaṭ‘an): Definitively; the ruling established by 'amm is certain and not open to doubt.
متفقة الحدود (muttafiqat al-ḥudūd): Individuals that share the same boundary or definition, i.e., all individuals of a single genus.
استغراق (istighrāq): Exhaustiveness; the condition that 'amm must cover every single individual without exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling of a general term ('amm) regarding the individuals it encompasses?
A) It is ambiguous (mujmal) and requires pause.
B) It establishes the ruling definitively (qat'an).
C) It establishes the ruling only for one individual if singular, three if plural.
D) It is presumptive (zanni) due to possible specification.

Key Takeaway
A general word ('amm) in Hanafi usul is definitive in its coverage over all individuals of a kind, and this definitiveness holds until a specific exception is proven.

Three Positions on the Decisiveness of ʿĀmm
Refuting three views on whether ʿāmm is decisive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the three views on the legal force of ʿāmm, and defend the Hanafi position that ʿāmm is qaṭʿī until evidence of specification appears.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, ʿāmm is decisive until specification is proven; mere possibility does not weaken its force.

This passage presents a foundational dispute in uṣūl al-fiqh: does a general term (ʿāmm) in the Qurʾān or Sunnah establish a ruling decisively over all its individuals, or is its indication presumptive and subject to immediate suspicion of specification? The Hanafī school holds the former view, while three opposing positions—including that of Imām al-Shāfiʿī—are refuted. Understanding this debate is critical for deriving rulings from revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opposing views
List the three views mentioned in the passage: (1) ʿĀmm is mujmal (ambiguous) and requires suspension; (2) If the wording is singular, it applies to one; if plural, to three; (3) ʿĀmm is ẓannī because every general has been partially specified (the Shāfiʿī position).
The first two views are not widely held today but are mentioned to show extremes.
2
Understand the Hanafī refutations
For each view, note how the author refutes it by the wording of the text: 'establishes the ruling' refutes mujmal; 'encompasses individuals' refutes the limited-number view; 'decisively' refutes the ẓannī claim.
The refutations are brief but show the author's commitment to the qaṭʿī nature.
3
Grasp the Hanafī argument for qaṭʿī
The Hanafī argument is that a general term is taken at face value until there is actual evidence (dalīl) of specification. The mere possibility of specification does not affect certainty; otherwise, all texts would be uncertain.
This is based on the principle that iḥtimāl (possibility) without evidence is not considered.
4
Appreciate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf)
For Hanafīs, a general verse like 'Kill the polytheists' (9:5) is decisive for all polytheists until a specific exception is proven. For Shāfiʿīs, the verse is presumptive, obliging the seeker to look for specification before acting.
This affects how one prioritizes and applies scriptural evidence.
5
Evaluate both sides
Consider the strengths of each position: Shāfiʿīs point to the many cases where ʿāmm has been specified; Hanafīs argue that specification is a separate operation that does not undermine the default decisiveness.
Both schools agree that ʿāmm can be specified; the disagreement is about its epistemological status before specification.

Source Text

قوله : وانه يوجب الحكم فيما يتناوله قطعاً عام کے حکم میں مسالک ثلاثہ: عام جن افراد کو شامل ہوتا ہے ان میں حکم کو قطعا ثابت کرتا ہے عام کے حکم کے بارے میں تین مسلک اور ہیں۔ (۱) یہ مجمل ہوتا ہے اس میں توقف کرنا ضروری ہے۔ مصنف نے موجب الحکم کی قید لگا کر اس کی تردید کر دی ہے۔ (۲) یہ کہ عام کا صیغہ اگر مفرد ہو تو صرف ایک فرد میں حکم ثابت ہوگا اور اگر صیغہ جمع ہو تو صرف تین میں حکم کو ثابت کرتا ہے اور باقی میں حکم موقوف ہوگا مصنف نے یتناول افراد کی قید لگا کر اس کی تردید کردی۔ (۳) امام شافعی کا قول ہے کہ عام ظنی ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ ہر عام میں احتمال ہے کہ وہ مخصوص منہ البعض ہو شوافع کا قاعدہ ہے مامن عام الا وقد خص عنه البعض مصنف نے قطعاً کی قید لگا کر اس کی بھی تردید کر دی ۔ اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ احتمال ناش بلا دلیل ہے جس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے
His statement: And that it establishes the ruling in what it encompasses decisively. Regarding the ruling of the general term ('amm), there are three schools: (1) It is ambiguous (mujmal) and suspending judgment is necessary. The author refuted this by adding the qualification 'establishes the ruling'. (2) If the wording of the general is singular, it establishes the ruling for only one individual; if plural, it establishes the ruling for only three, and the rest are suspended. The author refuted this by adding 'encompasses individuals'. (3) Imam al-Shafi'i said that the general is presumptive (zanni) because every general has the possibility of being specified partially. The Shafi'is have a principle: 'There is no general except that part of it has been specified.' The author refuted this by adding 'decisively'. And we say that this possibility arises without evidence and is not considered.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of 'amm (general term) in usul al-fiqh. The author, following the Hanafi school, asserts that 'amm is decisive (qat'i) in establishing the hukm over all individuals it encompasses. Before that, he mentions three opposing views, all of which he refutes by the phrasing of the text. The first view says 'amm is ambiguous (mujmal) requiring suspension. The second view distinguishes between singular and plural forms. The third, attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, says 'amm is only presumptive (zanni) because every general term is subject to specification. The Hanafi response is that the mere possibility without evidence is not considered. This is a foundational debate: Hanafis hold 'amm as qat'i in the absence of takhsis, while the Mutakallimun (including Shafi'is) consider it zanni.

Key Terms
عام (āmm): A general term that encompasses all individuals of its category without limit
قطعة (qat'an): Decisively, without doubt
ظني (ẓannī): Presumptive, not decisive; leaves room for doubt
مجمل (mujmal): Ambiguous, requiring clarification

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafī uṣūl, the general term is decisive until evidence of specification is found; mere possibility does not affect its certainty.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
